  - **B-15: derive `config('bridge.providers')` keys from `SUPPORTED` (or vice versa) at runtime.** Rejected: they encode different facts (which providers can be received vs which have a configured API base), so collapsing them would force a config entry for webhook-only providers or an adapter assumption for API-only ones. The containment assertion catches the real drift (a typo'd / orphan provider key) without conflating the two.
  - **B-15: warn instead of fail.** Rejected: a configured provider with no adapter can never work (the receiver 400s it) — a definite misconfig, so fail-closed matches the project posture, unlike the secret-perms *warnings* (DL-014) which are defense-in-depth over a hard backstop.
  - **B-16: rely on dependabot alone.** Rejected (the review's point): dependabot is asynchronous and easy to let lapse; a CI gate makes a vulnerable dep block the PR that introduces/keeps it.
- **Consequences:** `bridge:check` gains one provider-containment assertion (uses `WebhookAdapterFactory::supports`). New `composer-audit` CI job. Both are low-churn drift/CVE guards. Files: `app/Console/Commands/Bridge/CheckCommand.php`, `.github/workflows/security.yml`, `tests/Feature/Console/BridgeCommandsTest.php`.

---

## DL-016 — Cleanups: one `ensureDir`, `CheckCommand extends BridgeCommand`, trimmed Python-provenance docstrings, documented no-`TrustProxies` (B-18 + B-19 + B-10/S3)

- **Date:** 2026-05-31
- **Context:** Three NICE-TO-HAVE/maintainability tail items from the architecture review:
  - **B-19:** four call sites created a state/secret-adjacent directory with an inline `if (! is_dir) mkdir($dir, 0700, true)` — the mode (`0700`) was duplicated and could drift per site. Also (Sec N4): the no-`TrustProxies` posture was undocumented.
  - **B-18:** several docblocks carried bare "mirrors the v0.11.x Python contract" provenance — archaeology that adds noise without explaining a behavior (the Python tree is long gone, DL-001).
  - **B-10/S3:** `CheckCommand` still extended `Illuminate\Console\Command` directly, leaving the DL-007 `BridgeCommand` base-class consolidation incomplete.
- **Decision:**
  - **B-19:** add `BridgePaths::ensureDir(string $dir)` (the one place a `0700` dir is created) and route all four call sites (`appendJsonl`, `WebhookProvisioner::writeSecret`, `InboxCommand::writeSeen`, `SpawnDetachedHandler`) through it, so the mode can't drift. **Document the no-`TrustProxies` posture** in `CLAUDE_ARCHITECTURE.md`: the app never trusts `X-Forwarded-*` (HMAC is over the raw body, scope from the URL re-checked vs the body, the loopback gate uses the configured URL) — nothing reads a forwardable header, so registering `TrustProxies` would only widen the trust surface.
  - **B-18:** trim the bare Python-provenance docstrings (`Classifier` signature note, `PathHelper::expandUser`, the `appendJsonl` ksort note's Python parenthetical) to state the *behavior/contract* instead. KEEP the ones that justify a real PHP behavior — `ChannelPushHandler`'s `parse_url`-vs-`urlparse` gotcha and `DispatchService`'s `23000`-handling reference (an internal cross-ref, not Python).
  - **B-10/S3:** `CheckCommand extends BridgeCommand` (dropping the direct `Command` import) — completing the base-class consolidation. No behavior change (it uses no options; `self::SUCCESS/FAILURE` come through the base).
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - **B-19: a configurable dir mode.** Rejected: every bridge-created dir holds (or sits beside) secrets and must be `0700`; a knob would invite a non-0700 value. One hardcoded `0700` helper is the safe shape.
  - **B-18: delete the docblocks entirely.** Rejected: the *contract/behavior* parts are useful (the classifier signature is a real contract); only the Python archaeology is noise.
  - **B-10/S3: leave `CheckCommand` on `Command`.** Rejected: it's the one `bridge:*` command not on the shared base — a small consistency gap the review flagged; aligning it is zero-risk.
- **Consequences:** New `BridgePaths::ensureDir`; the four `mkdir(0700)` sites collapse to it. `CheckCommand` is on `BridgeCommand`. Docstring noise trimmed. `CLAUDE_ARCHITECTURE.md` documents the no-`TrustProxies` posture. No runtime behavior change. Files: `app/Bridge/Support/BridgePaths.php`, `app/Bridge/Provision/WebhookProvisioner.php`, `app/Console/Commands/Bridge/{InboxCommand,CheckCommand}.php`, `app/Bridge/Handlers/SpawnDetachedHandler.php`, `app/Bridge/Contracts/Classifier.php`, `app/Bridge/Support/PathHelper.php`, `CLAUDE_ARCHITECTURE.md`.

---

## DL-017 — Group AgentConfig's identity triple into an `IdentityConfig` DTO (B-9, partial)

- **Date:** 2026-05-31
- **Context:** `AgentConfig`'s constructor carried three loose identity args (`?int $kanbanUserId, ?int $githubUserId, ?string $githubLogin`) inline — the largest remaining flat-field cluster in an otherwise DTO-grouped shape (`EchoSuppressionConfig`, `ChannelConfig` are already sub-DTOs). The architecture review (B-9) flagged the constructor's positional-arg count and proposed grouping the identity fields, "the same medicine DL-008 applied to the channel tuple."
- **Decision:** Extract `App\Bridge\Support\IdentityConfig` (`kanbanUserId`, `githubUserId`, `githubLogin` + a `selfIds()` helper for echo-seeding + a `fromArray()` parser), and hold it as a single `AgentConfig::$identity` prop. `AgentConfig::fromArray` builds it via `IdentityConfig::fromArray(section('identity'))`; the two readers (`AgentRegistry::fromAgentConfigs`, the `AgentConfig` tests) go through `$cfg->identity->…`. Mirrors the `EchoSuppressionConfig`/`ChannelConfig` idiom so the YAML `identity:` block has a 1:1 typed shape.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - **The full B-9 (also split `BridgePaths` into `BridgePaths` + `JsonlStore` + `InboxLayout`, and extract an `AgentConfigParser` from `AgentConfig`).** **Declined** (see "Deferred / declined" in the review doc): those are line-count-driven splits of cohesive, well-tested classes with broad call-site churn and no correctness gain — the kind of "while I'm here" restructure the project's right-sizing posture resists. The identity grouping is the one concrete smell (a related-field cluster begging for a DTO); the file splits are deferred until a real second reason to touch those files appears.
  - **Leave the three args inline.** Rejected: they are conceptually one thing (the agent's identity), map 1:1 to the YAML `identity:` block, and grouping them removes a positional-mismatch hazard at construction — a proportionate, idiom-consistent change.
- **Consequences:** New `app/Bridge/Support/IdentityConfig.php`; `AgentConfig`'s constructor drops from 11 to 9 args; `$cfg->kanbanUserId` → `$cfg->identity->kanbanUserId` at the two read sites. No runtime behavior change (the YAML schema is unchanged). Files: `app/Bridge/Support/{IdentityConfig,AgentConfig,AgentRegistry}.php`, `tests/Feature/Config/AgentConfigTest.php`, `tests/Unit/Support/IdentityConfigTest.php`, `CLAUDE_ARCHITECTURE.md`.

---

## DL-018 — Implement the durable-reaction seam: `DurableReaction` + durable-first dispatch + global echo (FR #2016, phase 1)

- **Date:** 2026-05-31
- **Context:** DL-009 *designed* the seam for the planned GitHub-PR→card-move writeback (board 8 #2016) but shipped no code. This is **phase 1 of the implementation**: the contract + dispatch-loop change + echo seam the writeback handler will plug into — built and tested **without** the writeback itself, so the foundational behavior change lands and is verified in isolation (the `KanbanClient` / `KanbanMoveCardHandler` / correlation classifier are phases 2–4).
- **Decision:**
  - **`App\Bridge\Contracts\DurableReaction`** — an empty marker interface. A handler implementing both `Handler` and `DurableReaction` is durable; durability is a property of the operator-registered handler, never of the classifier-emitted `ReactionTarget` (un-spoofable from the classify path), exactly as DL-009 specified.
  - **`DispatchService` partitions the per-agent target loop by durability.** Durable handlers run **first**; an uncaught durable throw **propagates** (treatment B → 5xx → redelivery) instead of being swallowed as a best-effort note. Best-effort handlers (today's behavior) run after, in the existing try/catch-as-note. Durable-first means a durable failure short-circuits before any best-effort handler fires, so redelivery re-runs the whole dispatch (durable handlers MUST be idempotent) without re-amplifying best-effort pushes. The four shipped handlers implement nothing → unchanged.
  - **Global echo seam in `isEcho()` via `config('bridge.global_echo_ids')`** (a list; `BRIDGE_GLOBAL_ECHO_IDS`, comma-separated) — provider actor ids whose events are never a signal for **any** agent (the bridge's own machine-write identities), unioned on top of the per-agent self ids. `isEcho()` was strictly per-agent; this is its one non-per-agent input. **Refinement of DL-009:** DL-009 named `writeback.<provider>.identity_id`; the implementation uses a more general `global_echo_ids` **list** so any machine identity (not just one writeback) can be globally suppressed — the writeback identity will be added to this list when phase 2/4 wires the `writeback` config block.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - **Durable as a `ReactionTarget` field.** Rejected (DL-009): classifier-emitted = attacker-influenceable; the marker on the operator-registered handler is un-spoofable.
  - **Run durable handlers last (after best-effort).** Rejected: a late durable failure would re-fire the already-run best-effort handlers on every redelivery — durable-first short-circuits that.
  - **A single `writeback.identity_id` scalar (DL-009's literal wording).** Generalized to a list now so the seam isn't writeback-specific; the scalar would have needed widening the first time a second machine identity appeared.
- **Consequences:** New `app/Bridge/Contracts/DurableReaction.php`; `DispatchService` loop partition + `isEcho` global union (`global_echo_ids` helper); `config/bridge.php` `global_echo_ids`; `BRIDGE_GLOBAL_ECHO_IDS` in `.env.example`; `docs/customization.md` durable-handler note. No behavior change for existing installs (nothing implements `DurableReaction`; `global_echo_ids` defaults empty). Tests: durable-first ordering, durable-throw propagation + best-effort short-circuit + unprocessed dispatch, global-echo suppression (`DispatchServiceTest` + recording-handler fixtures). Unblocks phase 2 (`KanbanClient` + writeback token). Files: `app/Bridge/Contracts/DurableReaction.php`, `app/Bridge/Dispatch/DispatchService.php`, `config/bridge.php`, `.env.example`, `docs/customization.md`, `tests/Feature/Dispatch/DispatchServiceTest.php` + `tests/Fixtures/{HandlerRecorder,RecordingHandler,RecordingDurableHandler,DualTargetClassifier}.php`.

---

## DL-019 — Writeback infrastructure: `writeback.json` policy + `KanbanClient` + dedicated token (FR #2016, phase 2)

- **Date:** 2026-05-31
- **Context:** Phase 2 of FR #2016, building on the DL-018 seam: the config + the kanban writeback client the move handler (phase 3) and the correlation classifier (phase 4) plug into. Per DL-009: operator-config-only repo→board mapping; a dedicated least-privilege writeback token; the writeback identity echo-suppressed.
- **Decision:**
  - **`<config_dir>/writeback.json`** (new) holds the per-install writeback policy — `identity_id` (the kanban user the writeback acts as) + `mappings` (`"owner/repo" → {board_id, stages:{opened|merged|merged_to_main|closed_unmerged → workflow_stage_id}}`). It lives in the **config dir, not the repo-tracked `config/bridge.php`** (the `shared-identities.json` precedent, DL-007: per-install policy isn't tracked config). **Absent ⇒ writeback disabled** (`WritebackConfig::load` returns null); **present-but-malformed ⇒ fail-closed** (throws) — a half-configured writeback must not move cards to the wrong place. The mapping keys on the **GitHub-controlled outcome**, never the PR title (DL-009 decision 5) — *which* card is the classifier's correlation job, *which board+stage* is operator config the webhook body can't influence.
  - **`App\Bridge\Writeback\KanbanClient`** — sibling to `KanbanProvisionClient` but in a distinct `Writeback` namespace (a card-mover doesn't belong under `Provision`). Exposes only `getCard` (for the belongs-to-board + already-in-stage checks) and `moveCard` (column-only `PATCH /tasks/{id}.json {task:{workflow_stage_id}}` — never touches payload/other fields). Authenticates with a **dedicated writeback token** at `TokenPath::forWriteback()` = `<secret_dir>/<provider>/writeback-token` — a distinct path from the broad provisioning token (`/token`), so a leaked writeback token is bounded to card moves (least-privilege, DL-009). The operator places this least-privilege token; the bridge can't mint a scoped token itself.
  - **Echo wiring:** `BridgeServiceProvider` seeds `writeback.json`'s `identity_id` into `bridge.global_echo_ids` (the DL-018 seam) when building `DispatchService`. This is **best-effort, not the fail-closed gate** — `DispatchService` is constructor-injected (e.g. into `ReplayCommand`), so it builds at console boot too; a malformed `writeback.json` must surface as a `bridge:check` error / a treatment-B 5xx in the move handler, NOT crash every CLI command. So the bind catches a bad file and skips the seeding (logged); the authoritative fail-closed is the handler (phase 3) + `bridge:check`.
  - **`bridge:check`** validates `writeback.json` when present (malformed → fail; missing `identity_id` → warn; missing/insecure writeback token → warn).
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - **Mappings in `config/bridge.php`.** Rejected (DL-007): repo-tracked config forces operators to edit tracked files + creates `git pull` merge conflicts on per-install policy. The config-dir json is the right home.
  - **Reuse the provisioning token for the move.** Rejected (DL-009): least-privilege — that token can create/delete webhook subscriptions; the card-mover gets card-move scope only, at its own path.
  - **`KanbanClient` under `App\Bridge\Provision`** (DL-009's anticipated path). Deviated: the writeback is not provisioning; a `Writeback` namespace groups the feature (`KanbanClient`, `WritebackConfig`, `WritebackMapping`) and reads clearly.
  - **Fail-closed in the bind closure on a malformed `writeback.json`.** Rejected: it would crash *every* artisan command (the bind runs at console boot via the injected `ReplayCommand`), turning a config typo into a total CLI outage. Fail-closed belongs where the writeback actually acts (the handler) + where it's reported (`bridge:check`); the echo-seed optimization degrades gracefully.
- **Consequences:** New `app/Bridge/Writeback/{WritebackConfig,WritebackMapping,KanbanClient}.php`; `TokenPath::forWriteback`; `BridgeServiceProvider` echo-seed; `bridge:check` writeback validation. New optional `<config_dir>/writeback.json` + `<secret_dir>/<provider>/writeback-token`. No behavior change when `writeback.json` is absent. Unblocks phase 3 (`KanbanMoveCardHandler`). Files: `app/Bridge/Writeback/*`, `app/Bridge/Support/TokenPath.php`, `app/Providers/BridgeServiceProvider.php`, `app/Console/Commands/Bridge/CheckCommand.php`, `docs/config-schema.md`, tests in `tests/Feature/Writeback/*` + `BridgeCommandsTest`.

---

## DL-020 — `KanbanMoveCardHandler`: the durable card-move writeback + transient-vs-permanent failure split (FR #2016, phase 3)

- **Date:** 2026-05-31
- **Context:** Phase 3 of FR #2016: the handler that actually moves a kanban card, plugging the phase-1 `DurableReaction` seam into the phase-2 `KanbanClient`/`WritebackConfig`. DL-009 set the authz model (operator-config board+stage, belongs-to-mapped-board guard, GitHub-controlled-outcome gating); this DL pins down the **failure treatment**, the one genuinely new decision — a durable handler throws → 5xx → *retry*, which is right for a transient failure but catastrophic (a retry-storm) for a permanent one.
- **Decision:** `App\Bridge\Handlers\KanbanMoveCardHandler implements Handler, DurableReaction`. The classifier (phase 4) supplies the payload `{card_id, repo, outcome}`; the handler:
  - **Splits failure by transience, inside the handler.** THROW (→ 5xx → redelivery) only for **transient / operator-fixable** conditions: a missing or insecure writeback token, an unconfigured API base URL, or a kanban **5xx / timeout / connection** error — these succeed on retry once fixed/recovered (the missing-token case mirrors the HMAC-secret fail-closed: kanban holds the event until the operator places the token). **LOG + NO-OP** (no throw, dispatch acks) for **permanent** conditions, which can never succeed and would 5xx-storm kanban-board's ~11-day retry curve if thrown: writeback disabled (no `writeback.json`), no mapping for the repo, no stage for the outcome, a **malformed payload** (a deterministic classifier bug), a kanban **4xx** on get/move (a deleted card, or a config'd stage that isn't on the card's board — kanban 404/422s these), or — the **security guard** — the card is **not on the mapped board** (belongs-to-mapped-board, DL-009). The dividing line is *retryability by HTTP status*: a kanban 4xx is the upstream saying "this will never work" (no-op); a 5xx/network error is "try again" (throw). This keeps the `DurableReaction` "failure → retry" contract honest: only retryable failures throw.
  - **Idempotent** (the marker's contract): a `getCard` showing the card already in the target stage is a no-op (no `moveCard`), so redelivery is safe.
  - **Config is authoritative; payload board/stage is ignored.** Board + stage come only from `writeback.json` keyed on the outcome; the belongs-to-board check compares the card's *real* `board_id` (from `getCard`) against the *mapped* board — a payload `board_id` can't influence it.
  - **Always-registered** (not opt-in like `spawn_detached`): it is **inert** without `writeback.json` + a token (it no-ops, never executes), and the classifier only emits the target for configured repos — so it carries none of `spawn_detached`'s RCE blast radius and needn't be gated.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - **Throw on every failure (uniform durable treatment).** Rejected: a permanent failure (no mapping, card on the wrong board) would 5xx every redelivery forever — an infinite retry-storm into kanban-board's ~11-day retry curve. The transient/permanent split is the whole point.
  - **No-op on every failure (never throw).** Rejected: a transient kanban API error or a not-yet-placed token would then silently drop the move (the exact loss DL-009 built durability to prevent). Transient failures must retry.
  - **Gate the handler behind an opt-in flag (like `spawn_detached`).** Rejected: it's inert without config and bounded by config (no RCE), so the flag adds friction without safety; the `writeback.json` presence is the de-facto enable.
  - **Throw uniformly on any kanban API error (the first cut).** Rejected after review: a kanban **4xx** (deleted card, a config'd stage not on the card's board) is permanent — throwing it would 5xx-storm forever. The fix classifies by HTTP status (4xx → no-op, 5xx/network → throw); a non-existent stage/board id surfaces as a kanban 4xx and is correctly no-op'd, so load-time id validation stays unnecessary.
  - **Throw on a malformed payload (treat it like a bad ReactionTarget elsewhere).** Rejected: `HandlerException` is best-effort (ack 200) in every *other* handler, but this is the first `DurableReaction`, so the same throw 5xx-storms. A malformed payload is a deterministic classifier bug → log + no-op (the event can't be moved regardless — we don't know the card).
- **Consequences:** New `app/Bridge/Handlers/KanbanMoveCardHandler.php`, registered always-on in `HandlerRegistry` (now four always-on defaults). The bridge can now perform its first outward-facing write — but only when an operator has placed `writeback.json` + a least-privilege token, and only a card on the mapped board to a config-mapped stage. Unblocks phase 4 (the correlation classifier that emits the target + provisioning the GitHub webhook). Files: `app/Bridge/Handlers/KanbanMoveCardHandler.php`, `app/Bridge/Support/HandlerRegistry.php`, `docs/customization.md`, `tests/Feature/Handlers/{KanbanMoveCardHandlerTest,HandlerRegistryTest}.php`.

---

## DL-021 — `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` + correlation read + no-code GitHub provisioning (FR #2016, phase 4 — feature complete)

- **Date:** 2026-05-31
- **Context:** The final phase of FR #2016: the classifier that turns a `pull_request` webhook into a `kanban_move_card` target, wiring the durable handler (DL-020) to real GitHub events. Open questions: where correlation lives, and how the GitHub webhook gets provisioned.
- **Decision:**
  - **`App\Bridge\Classifiers\GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier`** — emitted as an agent's `classifier.class` for a github-repo subscription. It (a) derives the move **outcome** from GitHub-controlled fields only — the action + `pull_request.merged` + `base.ref` (`opened`/`reopened`→`opened`; `closed`+merged+`base.ref==main`→`merged_to_main`; `closed`+merged+other base→`merged`; `closed`+not-merged→`closed_unmerged`), never the PR title; (b) correlates the card by the `DL-NNN` token in the PR title or head branch against the mapped board's `dl_number`. Emits **no Intent** (machine-only, "no agent in the loop"). A PR with no `DL-NNN`, an unmapped repo, or no matching card → empty result (graceful no-op, per the FR).
  - **Correlation lives in the classifier, as a kanban READ** (`KanbanClient::findCardByDlNumber` — board-search, client-side `dl_number` match on the numeric part so `DL-9`/`9` compare equal). A transient read failure is a **classify error (treatment A)** — recorded, ack 200, recoverable via `bridge:replay` — so a kanban blip during correlation never 5xx-storms and never drops the move silently. The *move* (the write) is the durable handler's job (treatment B). Splitting the read (recoverable) from the write (auto-retried) is deliberate.
  - **No GitHub provisioning code.** GitHub webhooks are configured in the repo's Settings → Webhooks (the bridge has no repo-admin GitHub token, and `bridge:provision` already skips github by design). "Provisioning" is an operator runbook step (`docs/writeback.md`): point a repo webhook at the bridge's `…/webhooks/github?b=<owner/repo>` receiver with the per-`(github, scope)` HMAC secret. The bridge already *receives* github webhooks (`GitHubAdapter`); nothing new is needed on the receive side.
  - **Shared `WritebackClientFactory::make()`** builds the `KanbanClient` (config + dedicated writeback token via `SecretFile`) for both the classifier (read) and the handler (write); the handler's inline `client()` is removed in favour of it (it now throws `ConfigException` on a missing token/base-url, same propagate-→retry behaviour).
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - **Correlation in the handler (the classifier emits a `DL-NNN`, the handler resolves the card).** Rejected: it would put a kanban read on the durable path where a transient read failure 5xx-retries — fine, but it also makes the handler's payload contract depend on a board-search; keeping correlation in the classifier matches DL-009 decision 8 ("correlation is classifier/agent business logic; the bridge provides the primitive") and lets the read fail as treatment-A (replayable) rather than a 5xx.
  - **Build GitHub webhook provisioning into `bridge:provision`.** Rejected: it needs a repo-admin GitHub PAT the bridge deliberately doesn't hold; the repo-settings webhook is a one-time operator action, not worth the credential surface.
  - **Match the card by `pr_number` instead of `DL-NNN`.** Rejected for the *initial* correlation: a card has no `pr_number` until the first `opened` move sets it; `DL-NNN` (already the board convention) is present from the first event.
- **Consequences:** New `app/Bridge/Classifiers/GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier.php`, `app/Bridge/Writeback/WritebackClientFactory.php`, `KanbanClient::findCardByDlNumber`; handler refactored onto the factory. New `docs/writeback.md` runbook. **FR #2016 is feature-complete** (DL-009 design → DL-018 seam → DL-019 infra → DL-020 handler → DL-021 classifier). To enable end-to-end: an operator places `writeback.json` + the writeback token, runs a github-subscribed agent with `classifier.class: …\GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier`, and configures the repo webhook. Files: `app/Bridge/Classifiers/GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier.php`, `app/Bridge/Writeback/{WritebackClientFactory,KanbanClient}.php`, `app/Bridge/Handlers/KanbanMoveCardHandler.php`, `docs/writeback.md` + subfile index, tests in `tests/Feature/Classifiers/` + `tests/Feature/Writeback/KanbanClientTest`.

---

## DL-022 — `Classifier::classify()` receives the serving `AgentConfig` (per-agent classification)

- **Date:** 2026-06-01
- **Context:** FR from a multi-agent operator: a classifier cannot make per-agent decisions because it isn't told which agent it serves. `Classifier::classify(eventType, payload, actor, provider, scopeId)` omits the agent; `ClassifierResolver` caches one instance per class (shared across agents), so the agent can only arrive as a call parameter, not instance state. `DispatchService` already loops per-agent and applies author-based gates (`isEcho`/`isSignal`) but has no recipient-aware seam. Concretely: a single install fanning out to N agents that share a coordination repo addressed with `to:<agent>` labels delivers every message to every agent — `backend` live-wakes on a `to:device` thread. Second time agent-blindness forced a work-around: DL-008 (channel auth) carries its per-agent Bearer token in `AgentConfig` + the handler precisely because the classifier couldn't be per-agent (its Context names this verbatim).
- **Decision:** Add the serving agent's **`AgentConfig`** as a required **final** parameter: `classify(eventType, payload, actor, provider, scopeId, AgentConfig $agent)`. The dispatcher passes `$agent` (already in hand at the per-agent loop, `DispatchService:113`). A classifier reads `$agent->agentName` / `$agent->identity` for recipient filtering (or any per-agent logic). Trailing position keeps the recognizable event-tuple readable (aesthetic only — see below). Concrete `AgentConfig` (not just `agentName`): already fully `readonly`, carries identity for author-vs-recipient logic, and avoids a second break if a classifier later needs more than the name. Instances stay shared/cached, so `$agent` is a call-local (docstring + `docs/customization.md` say so).
- **This is a BREAKING contract change, intentionally not "additive."** Verified empirically: PHP rejects an implementor whose `classify()` signature is narrower than the interface (`Declaration … must be compatible`), even with a default on the new param — so a default cannot soften it. Every implementor (3 in-tree + each operator's classifier) must add the parameter and thread it through any `parent::classify()`. Compile-checked (fatal-on-load makes a missed implementor impossible to ship silently); at this scale (pre-1.0, 3 in-tree, ~1 operator) the one-time mechanical update beats a permanent capability-interface or recipient-tagging indirection.
- **Supersedes DL-005's rejection of this option.** DL-005's "Alternatives considered" evaluated and **rejected** "pass `AgentConfig`/self-identity into `classify()`" as breaking and as "moving the echo decision into each classifier — contradicting the documented invariant." That calculus changed: DL-008 proved agent-blindness is a *recurring* forcing function, not a one-off, and recipient-addressing **policy** belongs in the operator's classifier anyway (the bridge supplies the mechanism — agent identity — not label semantics). DL-005's `reattributedActor` echo mechanism **stays**: for shared-identity *echo* you still report the author and let the dispatcher apply that agent's canonical echo rules (reuse, not reimplement). The two are orthogonal axes — recipient (this DL) vs author-echo (DL-005).
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - **Post-classify recipient-tagging hook** (classifier tags intents with recipients; dispatcher drops those not for the serving agent). Rejected: bakes recipient/label semantics into the bridge core, and the classifier still couldn't do *other* per-agent logic.
  - **Label-predicate subscription filtering** (`to:<self>` allowlist on the subscription). Rejected: needs per-agent label templating and pushes addressing policy into bridge config.
  - **Capability interface (`AgentAwareClassifier`) the dispatcher branches on.** Rejected: non-breaking but adds permanent two-shapes complexity + a dispatcher branch to dodge a one-time, compile-checked update — not worth it at this implementor count.
- **Consequences:** The contract now structurally depends on the config DTO (`Contracts\Classifier` → `Support\AgentConfig`; verified no cycle — `AgentConfig` references the default classifier only as a string). Custom classifiers must update (migration note in CHANGELOG + `docs/customization.md` § Per-agent classification). New acceptance test `tests/Feature/Dispatch/PerAgentClassifyTest.php` proves both halves: each agent's classify sees its own `$agent` through the shared instance (no leak), and a classifier filters by recipient. Files: `app/Bridge/Contracts/Classifier.php`, `app/Bridge/Dispatch/DispatchService.php`, `app/Bridge/Classifiers/{InboxOnlyClassifier,EventDrivenClassifier,GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier}.php`; docs `docs/customization.md`, `docs/multi-host.md`, `docs/multi-agent.md`; 7 test classifiers + 3 classifier tests updated.

---

> **How to add a DL entry.** Use the next available `DL-NNN`. Lead with Date + Context (what made the decision necessary), then Decision (what was chosen), then Alternatives considered (with one-line rejections), then Consequences (what this enables or constrains downstream). Cite specific files/lines when load-bearing. If correcting a prior DL, write a new one titled "Correction to DL-NNN" and leave the original frozen.

## DL-023 — Release card-promotion for board 8 via the shared `bin/promote-released-cards` script

- **Date:** 2026-06-05
- **Context:** Board 8 (the bridge's tracking board) has the same gap kanban-board's board 5 hit: a bundled `dev → main` release PR carries no single DL token, so the `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier`'s `merged_to_main` correlation (DL-021) can't advance the release's cards to "released" (stage 53) — they stall at "shipped to dev". kanban-board solved this (its DL-141 → DL-142) with a release-CI step that derives the shipped DL set deterministically from `git log <prev-tag>..HEAD` and moves each card, then generalized it to a framework-free script. The bridge is the second consumer of that script (extract-at-the-second-caller).
- **Decision:** adopt the **same `bin/promote-released-cards`** (bash + curl + jq) verbatim, configured for board 8 via `.release-pr.json` `.promote` (`board_id: 8`, `released_stage_id: 53`, `api_base`) + `.github/workflows/release-promote-cards.yml` (on `push: main`, isolated from auto-tag, `workflow_dispatch` dry-run default). Identical correlation (card `payload.dl_number`), idempotent + best-effort per card, plus the empty-board guard (refuses loudly when the token can't see the board, instead of silently reporting every ref "no card"). No Laravel/PHP in the promote job — `jq`/`curl`/`git` only.
- **Consequences:** the bridge's own webhook writeback is unchanged and still owns the per-feature-PR transitions (opened/merged-to-dev); this only fills the release→released hop it structurally can't do for a bundled PR. Requires a `KANBAN_WRITEBACK_TOKEN` Actions secret on the bridge repo whose user is a **member of board 8** (the kanban-board token's user must also have board-8 access, or use a board-8-capable token); without it the step refuses loudly. Ships at the next bridge release (push:main triggers it). Same script + toolkit as kanban-board; the only per-repo difference is the `.promote` block + the VERSION-file `version_regex`.

## DL-024 — Dependabot-PR → kanban card (create-on-open / move-on-close), opt-in per repo

- **Date:** 2026-06-05
- **Context:** The writeback (DL-021) only MOVES existing cards correlated by a `DL-NNN` token. Dependabot PRs carry no DL and have no pre-existing card, so dependency updates never surface on the tracking boards (5/8). The user wants a dependabot PR to appear as a card automatically when it opens on GitHub, for both repos.
- **Decision:** Extend the writeback to CREATE a card for a dependabot PR (head ref `dependabot/*`) and carry it through the lifecycle, keyed by **PR number** (no DL). OPT-IN per repo via a new `writeback.json` mapping flag **`create_dependabot_cards`** (default `false` — off, consistent with the writeback's opt-in philosophy).
  - `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier`: when the mapping opts in AND the PR is dependabot, emit a `kanban_dependabot_card` target keyed by PR number (carrying repo / outcome / pr_number / title / url) instead of taking the DL-correlation path.
  - New `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` (DurableReaction): idempotent on `payload.pr_number`. Card exists → move to the outcome's stage (no-op if already there). No card + opened/merged/merged_to_main → **create** at that stage, tagged `dependencies` + `triaged` (so the routine churn doesn't flood the untriaged sweep). No card + closed_unmerged → **skip** (don't mint a card just to close one we never tracked). Same transient(5xx→retry)/permanent(4xx→log+no-op) split as the move handler (DL-020).
  - `KanbanClient`: + `findCardByPrNumber` + `createCard`.
- **Consequences:** reuses the existing per-repo stage mapping (opened/merged/merged_to_main/closed_unmerged → stages) — no new stage config, just the boolean opt-in. The writeback token now also needs CREATE (`POST /tasks.json`); its kanban user already has write + board membership. Idempotency is best-effort: a concurrent duplicate `opened` delivery could create two cards (no unique constraint on `pr_number`) — acceptable at dependabot's low rate; an `external_id`-unique guard is a future hardening. Enable per-install by adding `"create_dependabot_cards": true` to a repo's `writeback.json` mapping (boards 5 + 8). Tests: `KanbanDependabotCardHandlerTest` (create / move / idempotent / closed-skip / opt-out) + 2 classifier cases; 319/319, Pint + PHPStan L7 clean.

## DL-025 — `Classifier::classify()` takes a single `ClassifyContext` (the LAST breaking signature change) + out-of-process pre-flight validation (#2053)

- **Date:** 2026-06-05
- **Context:** A custom classifier still on a prior positional `classify()` signature is an **uncatchable `E_COMPILE_ERROR`** ("Declaration must be compatible") the instant `ClassifierResolver` loads it — `try/catch(Throwable)` cannot catch it (verified PHP 8.3.6). Sola hit this in the v0.21 update window. Two harms: (a) the FPM worker dies mid-request → 500 → permanent retry-storm (config unchanged, recurs every redelivery); (b) `bridge:check`, the pre-flight that exists to catch exactly this, ALSO fatals (exit 255). The deeper cause: `classify()` is a **positional parameter list that keeps growing** — DL-002 added the provider-aware actor, DL-022 added the serving `$agent` — and every addition is an uncatchable break. Validating the bad signature is treating a symptom; the recurring break is the bug.
- **Decision (two parts):**
  - **A — parameter object (the root-cause fix).** `classify(ClassifyContext $ctx): ClassifyResult`, where `ClassifyContext` is a readonly DTO carrying eventType / payload / actor / provider / scopeId / agent. **Adding a field to `ClassifyContext` never changes the method signature**, so it can never again produce the compile-fatal. This is the **LAST breaking change** to `classify()`; future context needs are new DTO fields, not new params. Migrated the 3 in-tree classifiers + the dispatcher call site + 8 test fixtures.
  - **B — out-of-process pre-flight + SF-1.** `bridge:check` validates each classifier via `ClassifierResolver::probeLoadable()`, which loads the class in a **child php process** (Symfony Process, CLI `PHP_BINARY`); the child crashing on the compile fatal is fine — the parent reads its exit code and reports a clean, named failure instead of dying. SF-1: `ClassifierResolver::for()` wraps `new $class` to catch `\Error` (a ctor that requires args) → `ConfigException` (catchable → treatment-A, not a 500).
- **Consequences:** BREAKING for any custom classifier — it must migrate to the `ClassifyContext` signature — but it is the **last** such break (the whole point). Pre-1.0, acceptable; ~1–2 external classifiers. The **operator pre-flight is the primary defense**: `bridge:check` now survives + names the offending agent/class with a fix hint, so a stale classifier is caught before deploy. **Residual:** the *dispatch-time* uncatchable fatal isn't fully neutralized (a subprocess from FPM is unreliable — `PHP_BINARY` is `php-fpm` there), but once A is adopted, future param-equivalent additions are DTO fields → no fatal, and the pre-flight catches a transitional stale classifier. New `app/Bridge/Dispatch/ClassifyContext.php`; `ClassifierResolver::probeLoadable()`. Tests: `ClassifierResolverTest` (probe valid/missing/non-classifier + the SF-1 ctor wrap) + `CtorRequiringClassifier` fixture. 330/330, Pint + PHPStan L7 clean.

## DL-026 — Make degraded-but-not-erroring writeback states loud (blind/0-card token + page-cap truncation) (#2141)

- **Date:** 2026-06-06
- **Context:** Sola reported that the GitHub-PR → card-move writeback (FR #2016 / DL-021) **silently no-ops every move when its token can't see the board.** `KanbanClient::findCardByDlNumber`/`findCardByPrNumber` read the board via `GET /tasks/search.json?q=board_id=X&limit=200` and return `?int`. `null` conflated two very different causes: (1) a **genuine no-match** (N cards returned, none carry this PR's ref — a PR with no tracking card, correct to no-op quietly); (2) a **blind/degraded token** — the read returned **0 cards** because the token's user lost board membership (or `board_id`/instance is wrong). kanban answers `200` + empty `data`, so the existing `->throw()` never fires. Because the writeback is "machine-only, no agent in the loop," nobody is alerted — the board quietly stops advancing, looking identical to the healthy "no PR had a card" path. Two consequences (sibling audit): the classifier path **silently no-ops**; the `create_dependabot_cards` handler path is **worse** — a blind token makes it `createCard()` a **duplicate** on every redelivery (the DL-024 idempotency hole). The `limit=200` cap was likewise silent (a >200-card board misses correlations).
- **Decision:** extend the `->throw()`-loud-on-errors discipline to the two **non-erroring** degradations, in the **non-transient** register (NEVER a 5xx — a genuinely-blind board would retry-storm; a genuine no-match stays quiet):
  - **Runtime (catches post-deploy drift).** Both finders route through a shared `KanbanClient::correlationCards()` that `Log::warning`s once per read when the board returns **0 cards** (blind token) or **≥`SEARCH_LIMIT` (200)** cards (truncation). One choke-point covers both the classifier and the dependabot-handler sibling. A pure `searchBoardCards()` does the read (no logging); `boardCardCount()` exposes the count.
  - **Config-time (catches the persistent misconfig where it belongs).** `bridge:check` probes each mapped board with the writeback token (`boardCardCount`) and warns on 0 cards / cap / read-failure / factory-failure. **All warn-level — never fails the check** (a temporarily-unreachable kanban or a genuinely-empty new board must not fail an install check). The factory build is wrapped in `catch (\Throwable)` (an insecure-perms read throws a non-`ConfigException`) so the probe can never crash `bridge:check` — a #2053-class regression guard.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) **surfaced intent** (handler → inbox) — the writeback path is reaction-only and the classifier deliberately emits no intents; plumbing a handler-emitted intent is the most invasive option and unnecessary once config-time + runtime warnings exist. Rejected. (b) **transient 5xx** — explicitly the wrong register (retry-storm). Rejected. (c) **hard-fail `bridge:check` on 0 cards** (the prior-art CI promoter `die`s on 0) — risks failing a legitimately-empty brand-new board; the CI promoter runs against a known-populated board, `bridge:check` runs at install time. Chose warn (flagged as a possible future tightening).
- **Consequences:** the blind-token and truncation states are now visible at both deploy time and runtime; the genuine-no-match path is unchanged (quiet, returns `null`). `KanbanClient` now logs — a deliberate deviation from the "thin client throws, caller logs" convention (no other `app/Bridge/Writeback` or `Adapters` class logs), justified because the shared read is the single point where the degradation is observable (docblock updated to say so). No schema/migration; opt-in posture unchanged (no `writeback.json` ⇒ unaffected). New: `KanbanClient::SEARCH_LIMIT`/`correlationCards`/`searchBoardCards`/`boardCardCount`, the `CheckCommand` board-visibility probe. Tests: 5 in `KanbanClientTest` (0-card warn + return null, dependabot-finder warn, 200-cap warn, genuine-no-match quiet, `boardCardCount`), 4 in `BridgeCommandsTest` (0-card warn, count info, read-failure warn, base-url-unset guard-lock with `assertNothingSent`) + hardened the existing missing-token test. **Residual:** actual paging past 200 is out of scope (warn is the floor). 340/340, Pint + PHPStan L7 clean.

## DL-027 — Per-mapping `swimlane_id` for writeback-CREATED cards (create-only, never on move) (#2148)

- **Date:** 2026-06-06
- **Context:** Sola requested (required FR) that the writeback be able to place created cards in a specific swimlane — the concrete case being one board shared across repos with a lane per repo, where every dependabot/PR-origin card a mapping creates should land in that repo's lane instead of the board's default. Today `KanbanClient::createCard()` (the only create path, reached by the DL-024 dependabot handler) posts no `swimlane_id`, so kanban assigns the default lane.
- **Decision:** add an **optional** `swimlane_id` to each `writeback.json` mapping (`WritebackMapping::$swimlaneId`, nullable, trailing ctor param). It is applied **at card CREATE only — never on a move.** A move stays a column-only `workflow_stage_id` PATCH (DL-020), so a human re-laning a card is preserved and a webhook redelivery can't yank a card back to its origin lane. `KanbanClient::createCard()` gains a trailing `?int $swimlaneId` and adds `task.swimlane_id` to the POST **only when non-null** (absent ⇒ omit the key ⇒ default lane, byte-for-byte today's request). Parsing is **strict like `board_id`/`stages`, NOT the `identity_id` silent-null pattern**: a present non-numeric `swimlane_id` **throws** `ConfigException` (fail-closed) rather than dropping to the default lane — silently landing cards in the wrong lane is exactly the fail-quiet trap DL-026 fought. `bridge:check` validates a pinned `swimlane_id` against the board's actual lanes (new `KanbanClient::boardSwimlaneIds()` via the lightweight `GET /boards/{id}/preload.json` — carries swimlanes, not every task, unlike `GET /boards/{id}.json`) and **warns** (never fails) that created cards would `422`-and-silently-no-op when the lane is missing (deleted, or on a different board).
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) **swimlane on move too** — rejected: moves are deliberately column-only; re-laning on every PR event would fight human organization and make redelivery non-idempotent w.r.t. lane. (b) **silent-null on bad value** (the `identity_id` precedent) — rejected per DL-026: a wrong-lane card is invisible-degraded, the class of bug we just made loud. (c) **read lanes via `GET /boards/{id}.json`** — rejected: that endpoint is task-heavy; `preload.json` returns the lanes alone (M1 review fix). (d) **validate the lane at runtime in the handler** — unnecessary: config-time `bridge:check` catches the misconfig where it belongs, and a runtime 422 is already the permanent-refusal (log + no-op) branch.
- **Consequences:** opt-in and backward-compatible — every existing `writeback.json` (no `swimlane_id`) produces byte-identical POSTs; no schema/migration. Only the dependabot create path exercises it today (a DL-correlated card is created by the board's own automation, not the writeback). New surface: `WritebackMapping::$swimlaneId`, `KanbanClient::createCard($swimlaneId)` + `boardSwimlaneIds()`, the `CheckCommand` lane probe. Tests: 2 in `WritebackConfigTest` (loads optional id, non-numeric throws), 3 in `KanbanClientTest` (create with/without lane, `boardSwimlaneIds` reads preload), 2 in `KanbanDependabotCardHandlerTest` (lane reaches/omitted from the create POST), 2 in `BridgeCommandsTest` (lane-ok info, lane-missing warn). 349/349, Pint + PHPStan L7 clean. **Note (S1):** `boardSwimlaneIds` is bridge:check-only — runtime trusts config + kanban's 422, no extra per-create read. **Note (N1):** only the bot/dependabot create path creates cards, so the lane affects only those today; a future non-dependabot writeback-create would inherit it for free.

## DL-028 — Page the writeback correlation read (close the DL-026 >200-card truncation residual) (#2151)

- **Date:** 2026-06-06
- **Context:** Sola hit this standing up `create_dependabot_cards` (DL-024) on a **mature board (~300 live cards)**: `bridge:check` correctly fired the DL-026 cap warning, but the warning was the *only* mitigation. `KanbanClient` read a board in **one** capped request (`GET /tasks/search.json?q=board_id=N&limit=200`); kanban hard-caps a single search response at 200 rows regardless of `limit` (verified in source: `min(200, …)` + `forPage($page,$perPage)` over an `id`-desc total order). So on a board past 200 live cards, any card beyond #200 was **invisible** to `findCardByDlNumber`/`findCardByPrNumber` → a move silently no-ops (DL-021), and worse, the DL-024 create path read "not found" as "no card exists" and **minted a duplicate on every redelivery** — the same idempotency hole DL-026 closed for the *blind-token* case, reproduced for the *truncation* case. Released/terminal cards accumulate, so any long-lived tracking board crosses 200 and stays there. DL-026 explicitly deferred actual paging ("warn is the floor").
- **Decision:** make the shared board read **page until a short page**. The search body is a bare `{data:[...]}` (no `total`/`meta`/`links`), so the stop condition is "keep incrementing `?page` while a page returns exactly `SEARCH_LIMIT` rows; stop on the first page that returns fewer." A hard `MAX_PAGES` ceiling (50 → 10,000 live cards) bounds a pathological/non-paging upstream. The read stays **eager-full** (read all pages, then iterate to match) because the degraded-state guards need the whole result and a page-1 match on a 300-card board is still only 2 GETs. **Crucially** (the plan-review must-fix): the short-page break and the truncation decision are made **inside the loop on the RAW batch length** (rows kanban returned), surfaced as an explicit `BoardRead{cards, truncated}` value object — **not** re-derived downstream from `count($cards)`. The rows are array-filtered (a non-array row is dropped), so a count-based check would desync and miss truncation at the boundary — the read-time-reconstruction anti-pattern and precisely the silent-loss class DL-026 exists to kill. DL-026's separation is preserved: `readBoard()` is **pure (no logging)** and merely *reports* what it observed (the `truncated` flag); `correlationCards()` still owns the runtime `Log::warning`s (0-card blind-token guard on empty; truncation guard on the flag) and `bridge:check` prints its own line. The old `bridge:check` "200-card cap; paging needed" warning is replaced by an "exceeds the 10,000-card safety ceiling" warning gated on the flag; the normal branch now reports the **true paged count**.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) **lazy page-by-page, stop when matched** — rejected: it can't compute the 0-card/truncation guards (which need the full read) and saves nothing at real board sizes (1–2 pages). (b) **derive truncation from `count($cards) >= SEARCH_LIMIT*MAX_PAGES`** — rejected (plan-review must-fix): array-filtered count desyncs from raw page sizes → false-negative truncation at the boundary, the COALESCE-at-read-time smell (canon #5). (c) **per-run memoization of the board read** — rejected as dead complexity: `WritebackClientFactory::make()` returns a fresh client per call and no handler calls both finders, so no board is read twice in one request today; revisit if a future caller does N correlations on one client. (d) **dedup-guard a non-paging upstream** (page N == page N-1) — rejected as over-engineering for a server we control; documented as the one assumption the truncation flag makes (kanban honors `page`).
- **Consequences:** boards >200 go from silently-truncated to fully-correlated; ≤200-card boards are behaviorally identical (page 1 short ⇒ one GET, as before). No config/schema/migration; internal read-loop only. New surface: `KanbanClient::MAX_PAGES`, `readBoard()` (replaces `searchBoardCards`), `boardVisibility(): BoardRead` (replaces `boardCardCount(): int`), the `BoardRead` value object. Tests: 4 new in `KanbanClientTest` (multi-page find beyond #200, MAX_PAGES ceiling warning + `assertSentCount`, raw-length-not-filtered-count break lock, `boardVisibility` shape) + the obsolete 200-cap test removed; 1 new in `BridgeCommandsTest` (ceiling warning). 352/352, Pint + PHPStan L7 clean. **Cost:** each correlation now costs ≈ ⌈live-cards ÷ 200⌉ GETs (eager-full, no memoization) — negligible at real sizes, bounded at 50 by the ceiling. **Residual:** a board **at or past** 10,000 live cards is reported truncated (loudly) — at exactly 10,000 that's a conservative false-positive warning, since distinguishing "exactly full" from "more beyond" would cost an extra page request; prune terminal cards or raise `MAX_PAGES`.

## DL-029 — Writeback correlation cutover: indexed `by-ref` lookup + move-ALL-matching cards (consumes kanban DL-147/148)

- **Date:** 2026-06-06
- **Context:** correlation downloaded the whole board and digit-matched `payload.dl_number`/`pr_number` client-side (DL-021), paged in DL-028 — O(board size), with a `MAX_PAGES` ceiling that silently truncated very large boards. Kanban shipped the first-class fix (DL-147/148): a `task_external_references` table + `GET /boards/{b}/tasks/by-ref.json` (server-canonicalized, indexed, returns a collection — a PR/DL is one-to-many). This is the bridge consuming it. Supersedes the targeted-DSL-query idea in the original #2160 (dl_number is a *string* custom field, so a numeric DSL query couldn't work — the upstream primitive was the right fix).
- **Decision:** add `KanbanClient::findCardsByRef()` + `correlateDl()`/`correlatePr()` that dispatch on a new bridge-wide flag **`writeback.correlation` (`BRIDGE_WRITEBACK_CORRELATION`, default `scan`)**: `ref` → one indexed `by-ref` query (O(1), no paging); `scan` → the existing board-scan fallback. **Both modes return ALL matching card ids** (collection) — a bundled PR/DL tracks multiple cards (kanban DL-148), so the classifier emits one `kanban_move_card` target per card (distinct `targetId` ⇒ no DL-003 coalesce) and the dependabot handler moves every match. **Default `scan`** so upgrading the bridge is inert until an operator sets `ref` per-install after confirming that install's kanban exposes `by-ref` AND is backfilled — opt-in activation, zero deploy risk (chosen over the design's default-`ref` for fleet safety).
- **Health probe decoupled (DL-026):** the blind/degraded-token check no longer rides the correlation read. New `KanbanClient::visibility()` — a single `limit=1` search reading the DL-146 `meta.total` — answers "can the token see the board, how big is it?" cheaply, used by `bridge:check` regardless of correlation mode (`boardVisibility()` + its full read removed). In `scan` mode `bridge:check` additionally warns if `total` exceeds the scan ceiling and points at `correlation=ref`.
- **Rollout:** ship default `scan` (no behavior change on bridge upgrade) → operator deploys → sets `BRIDGE_WRITEBACK_CORRELATION=ref` once the install's kanban is on v0.17.2+ and backfilled → `bridge:check` confirms. `scan` retained as a one-flag fallback. The kanban `by-ref` response is a **collection** (DL-148); the bridge was built against that shape from the start.
- **Alternatives considered:** default `ref` (design doc) — rejected for fleet safety (an un-backfilled install would correlate nothing on upgrade); per-mapping correlation mode — rejected (it's an install-wide property of the upstream, not a per-repo policy); keep paging only — rejected (the O(board) cost doesn't hold for larger-volume customers, per the maintainer).
- **Consequences:** `KanbanClient` gains `correlateDl`/`correlatePr`/`findCardsByRef`/`visibility`, loses the single-result finders + `boardVisibility`; `config/bridge.php` gains `writeback.correlation`; classifier emits N targets; dependabot handler moves all matches; `CheckCommand` uses the cheap probe. `KanbanClientTest` + classifier + `bridge:check` tests updated; ref-mode + N:1 + visibility tests added. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 357/357. #2162 (orphaned-mapping guard) is the remaining seam item.

## DL-030 — `bridge:check` flags an orphaned writeback mapping (#2162)

- **Date:** 2026-06-06
- **Context:** a `writeback.json` mapping is only ever fired if some agent runs a classifier that emits writeback reactions (`kanban_move_card`/`kanban_dependabot_card`) AND is subscribed to that mapping's github scope. An operator who writes `writeback.json` but never wires up such an agent gets the silent "all green, zero cards ever move" state — the policy exists, nothing drives it. Nothing surfaced it.
- **Decision:** add a marker interface `App\Bridge\Contracts\EmitsWritebackReactions` (implemented by `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier`) and have `bridge:check` warn when a mapping's repo scope is not covered by any agent whose classifier implements it. During the per-agent validation loop, for each agent that passes `probeLoadable`, `bridge:check` records its github subscription scopes **iff** its classifier emits writeback reactions; after the loop, any `writeback.json` mapping whose `repo` isn't in that set warns "ORPHANED … the mapping is inert".
- **Out-of-process detection (DL-025):** the marker check uses a new `ClassifierResolver::probeImplements($class, $interface)` that loads the class in a child process (`class_implements`), mirroring `probeLoadable` — an in-process `instanceof`/load of a stale custom classifier is an uncatchable E_COMPILE_ERROR that would kill `bridge:check` itself. Called only after `probeLoadable` has passed.
- **Scope match:** an agent covers a mapping when it has a `github` subscription whose `scopeId` equals the mapping's repo (the `GitHubAdapter` scope = `repository.full_name`). Warn-level (never fails the check) — a mapping may be added before its agent, same posture as the other writeback warnings (DL-026/027).
- **Alternatives considered:** in-process `instanceof` after `for()` — rejected to keep the marker detection strictly out-of-process per DL-025 (consistency + defense even though `for()` is gated). A dispatcher-level runtime warning — rejected: the value is catching it at config time (`bridge:check`), before any event, not on first traffic.
- **Consequences:** new marker interface + `probeImplements` + `CheckCommand` orphaned-mapping pass; `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` implements the marker. Tests: orphaned warns / not-orphaned-when-an-emitting-agent-subscribes. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 361/361. Completes the writeback-seam FR cluster (with #2160/DL-029 + kanban DL-146/147/148).

## DL-031 — Default writeback correlation to `ref` (correction to DL-029) + a `bridge:check` by-ref reachability probe

- **Date:** 2026-06-07
- **Correction to DL-029** (which defaulted `BRIDGE_WRITEBACK_CORRELATION` to `scan` for an inert upgrade). **Decision (owner):** default to **`ref`** — an undefined env now uses the indexed `by-ref` lookup; an operator needing the legacy/board-scan behavior (or pointing at a kanban that predates `by-ref`) must explicitly set `BRIDGE_WRITEBACK_CORRELATION=scan`. Rationale: `ref` is the correct, scalable default; making operators opt OUT (rather than opt in) means new installs get the good path automatically.
- **Safety net for the new default:** defaulting to `ref` introduces a silent-failure mode — a bridge pointed at a kanban < v0.17.2 (no `by-ref` route) would 404 EVERY correlation. So `bridge:check`, in `ref` mode, now actively probes `by-ref` reachability (`KanbanClient::byRefAvailable` — a `by-ref` query whose 404 means the route isn't registered, since `by-ref` returns `200 {data:[]}` on a genuine no-match) and warns loudly to upgrade kanban or set `scan`. This closes the gap that the visibility probe (which uses `search.json`) can't see.
- **Where the default lives:** `config/bridge.php` `env('BRIDGE_WRITEBACK_CORRELATION', 'ref')`; `WritebackClientFactory` fallback `'ref'`; `KanbanClient::__construct` default `'ref'` — all three layers flipped for consistency.
- **Upgrade note:** an install crossing into a `ref`-default bridge **must** have its kanban on v0.17.2+ AND `task_external_references` backfilled, OR set `scan`. `bridge:check` will name the problem before traffic. (The reference prod bridge already sets `=ref` explicitly, so it's unaffected.)
- **Alternatives considered:** keep default `scan` (DL-029) — rejected by the owner; the safe-by-inertia default left every install on the slow path indefinitely. Auto-detect (probe by-ref and pick a mode at runtime) — rejected: hidden magic, a per-request probe cost, and it masks misconfig that `bridge:check` should surface loudly.
- **Consequences:** the three default layers flipped; `bridge:check` gains the reachability probe; scan-path unit/feature tests pin `correlation=scan` explicitly (ref is now the default, so a scan test must opt in); new tests cover the ref default, `byRefAvailable`, and the reachability warn/ok. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 367/367. Ships in the next bridge release (v0.27.0).

## DL-032 — `RecipientAddressing` helper + docs recipe for comment-level `TO:` recipient filtering (#2173)

- **Date:** 2026-06-07
- **Context:** Sola PM (peer integrator) reported that recipient filtering resolved only at the **issue/card-label** level, so every comment on a multi-recipient thread woke all recipients — including comments whose body was addressed (`TO: agentB`) to one. Triage (card #2173) found the **capability already exists**: per DL-022 recipient-addressing *policy* lives in the operator's classifier, and `ClassifyContext` already carries `eventType` + `payload` (the comment body) + the serving `agent`, so a classifier can already filter at the comment level. The only real gap was that each operator would re-implement the `TO:`-line parse, and the pattern wasn't documented.
- **Decision:** ship a small reusable parser, `App\Bridge\Support\RecipientAddressing`, + a `docs/customization.md` recipe — **not** a core/dispatcher filter (DL-022 settled that recipient policy stays in the classifier). `RecipientAddressing::addresses(string $commentBody, string $agentName): ?bool` returns a deliberate three-state: `true` (a `TO:` line names the agent or `all`), `false` (a `TO:` line names others, not this agent → drop), `null` (no usable `TO:` line → caller falls back to its label behavior). A bare/empty `TO:` is treated as **absent** (null), so a typo can't silently suppress everyone. Matching is case-insensitive; the first `TO:` line wins; `all` addresses every agent. `recipients()` is exposed for direct use.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) tell Sola PM to implement the parse themselves — works (the capability is there) but every operator re-implements it; the helper removes that duplication for one tiny class. (b) a dispatcher-level / core comment-`TO:` filter — rejected, DL-022 (policy belongs in the classifier; the bridge supplies the inputs + now a parse helper). (c) bake a `TO:` convention into config — rejected (over-fits one operator's addressing scheme; the classifier already owns convention).
- **Consequences:** new `RecipientAddressing` support class + `RecipientAddressingTest` (9 cases: addressed/not/all/no-line/case-insensitive/TODO-not-matched/first-line-wins/bare-empty→null/whitespace); `docs/customization.md` § Comment-level recipient filtering recipe. No core/dispatcher/config change; nothing wired into the runtime (it's a helper operators opt into from their classifier). Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit (full). Closes #2173.

## DL-033 — Commit a pinned `package-lock.json` for `examples/channel-servers/`; `npm ci` + an audit-flag CI gate (peer FR)

- **Date:** 2026-06-07
- **Context:** A peer integrator (AIMLA PM) reported that the documented adoption flow for the reference channel MCP server (`examples/channel-servers/`) — copy the dir + `npm install` — is **non-reproducible**: the only direct dep is a caret range (`@modelcontextprotocol/sdk: ^1.0.0`) pulling ~90 transitive packages, so two agents onboarded on different days resolve different trees and a regressed/compromised transitive lands silently on the next install. The server reads a **bearer token**, accepts **loopback POSTs**, and runs **as the agent's OS user** — a real trust boundary where a pinned, reviewed tree is the right control. The bridge shipped no lockfile here.
- **Decision:** commit `package-lock.json` (lockfileVersion 3) and switch the documented install (README **and** the `start-channel-session.sh` launcher) from `npm install` to **`npm ci`** (installs the exact pinned tree; fails on package.json/lock drift). State the **Node ≥ 20** requirement up front. **Keep the pin *watched*** with a dedicated, cost-scoped CI workflow (`channel-server-supply-chain.yml`): `npm ci --ignore-scripts` (the drift gate) + `npm audit --audit-level=high` (**fails loudly** on a high/critical CVE in the pinned tree). Triggers are **path-filtered** to `examples/channel-servers/**` on PR, plus a **weekly** cron to catch newly-disclosed CVEs without a code change. Added a scoped `.gitignore` (`node_modules/`).
- **Why watched (the FR didn't ask for this):** a committed lockfile with nothing watching it just inverts the supply-chain risk — a pinned-vulnerable transitive rots silently. The bridge's `dependabot.yml` has **no npm ecosystem** and `security.yml` has **no npm-audit**, so the pin needed its own watcher to be a net security win.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) **pin only** (FR as written) — reproducible but unwatched; rejected for a token-reading channel server. (b) **dependabot npm auto-bumps** — freshest/hands-off, but adds a recurring dependabot-PR + CI-run stream (Actions cost) for a single-dep example; rejected as churn-for-marginal-benefit, and the operator is actively cost-reducing CI. (c) **audit-flag (chosen)** — pinned + loud-on-CVE + manual deliberate bump, lowest CI cost (path-filtered + weekly), matching the bridge's "degraded states must be loud" posture.
- **Consequences:** new `examples/channel-servers/package-lock.json` + `.gitignore`; README install → `npm ci` (+ Node ≥ 20 upfront + trust-boundary rationale); `start-channel-session.sh` → `npm ci`; new `channel-server-supply-chain.yml`. Docs/config/example only — **no app code change**. Note (separate, minor): a root `package.json` also lacks a lock — out of scope here. Validated locally: `npm ci --ignore-scripts` + `npm audit --audit-level=high` both pass (0 vulns, 93 packages).

## DL-034 — `bridge:check` 0-card writeback warning disambiguates empty-board from non-member (operator FR-1)

- **Date:** 2026-06-07
- **Context:** An operator (running v0.27.0) reported that `bridge:check` false-alarms on a legitimately **empty** mapped board: it warned *"token sees 0 cards … its user is likely **not a member** … will SILENTLY no-op every move"* when the token's user WAS a member and the board simply had no cards yet (no dependabot PRs had created any). 0 cards on a 200 read is **ambiguous** (empty board vs membership gap), but the message asserted the alarming branch, sending the operator hunting a non-existent membership problem (and inviting "fixes" like re-granting membership / rotating tokens).
- **Decision:** reword the 0-card line to present **both** possibilities and not assert membership on that evidence alone — *"EITHER the board is empty (fine) OR the token isn't a member / board_id is wrong (then moves silently no-op); if you expect cards there, verify membership + board_id."* True inaccessibility is already caught **separately**: in the default `ref` mode the by-ref reachability probe (DL-031) 404s and warns for a non-member/inaccessible board, so the 0-card line doesn't need to (and shouldn't) carry the membership claim.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) actively probe membership — query the board's member list, or distinguish a non-member via a `preload.json` 403 vs a member's 200, then emit a definitive message. Rejected for now: needs a members endpoint + the least-privilege writeback token to have list-members permission (it may not), and an extra API call; the softening removes the false alarm and the by-ref probe already covers true inaccessibility. The active probe stays a possible future enhancement. (b) drop the warning on 0 cards entirely — rejected: a real membership gap must still be visible.
- **Consequences:** one message change in `CheckCommand` (the writeback visibility probe); behaviour otherwise unchanged (still warn-level, still per mapped board). No schema/config change.

## DL-035 — `RecipientAddressing::author()` (symmetric `FROM:` parser) + reply-direction footgun docs (operator FR-3)

- **Date:** 2026-06-07
- **Context:** Same operator: `RecipientAddressing` (DL-032) parses a comment's `TO:` line (`addresses()`/`recipients()`) but had **no `FROM:`/author parser**, so every operator hand-rolls FROM extraction (a regex against the body) — and the `docs/customization.md` shared-identity echo example shipped exactly such a hand-rolled `preg_match('/^FROM:.../')`. The operator's own live routing bug was a **role-reversal drop**: their classifier routed *comments* by the parent issue's frozen `to:`/`from:` labels, so a reply that reversed the thread's direction (B→A on an A→B thread) was silently dropped. Not a bridge bug — but a missing helper + a missing worked example let the *class* of bug recur.
- **Decision:** add **`RecipientAddressing::author(string $body): ?string`** — symmetric with `recipients()`: the first `FROM:` line, lowercased + trimmed, or `null` (bare/empty `FROM:` is absent; `FROMAGE:` doesn't match). Dogfood it by replacing the hand-rolled `preg_match` in the customization docs' echo example. Add a **⚠ footgun callout + worked role-reversal example** to `docs/customization.md` § Comment-level recipient filtering: *route a comment by the comment's OWN `TO:`/`FROM:`, never the parent issue's labels (those freeze at thread-open and silently drop a reversed-direction reply); use labels only as the `null` fallback.*
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) leave operators to hand-roll FROM — rejected: it's the same parse over and over, and a stale-label-vs-body mismatch is the most common shared-identity footgun. (b) a combined new `Addressing` class — rejected: `RecipientAddressing` already owns the comment-line parse; adding the symmetric method keeps one home (and the existing name stays accurate enough). Recipient/author *policy* still lives in the operator's classifier (DL-022/DL-032); this is only the shared parse.
- **Consequences:** `RecipientAddressing::author()` + 7 `RecipientAddressingTest` cases (from/case-insensitive/no-line/bare-empty→null/first-wins/`FROMAGE:`-not-matched/CRLF+CR); `docs/customization.md` reply-direction example + the echo example now using `author()`. No runtime wiring — a helper operators opt into.

## DL-036 — Dispatch outcome ledger: `outcome` + `reason` on `agent_dispatches` distinguishes delivered / gate-dropped / errored (operator FR-2)

- **Date:** 2026-06-07
- **Context:** The per-agent dispatch ledger recorded only two observable states: `processed_at` set (terminal) and `error_message` set (errored, replayable). But a **deliberate gate-drop** (echo of the agent's own write, actor not a signal, or the classifier emitting no reactions) and a **successful delivery** both end with `processed_at` set and `error_message` null — so `bridge:inspect` rendered them identically as "done", and an operator debugging "why didn't my agent react to event N?" had no recorded answer (dropped-on-purpose vs delivered-but-handler-noop are indistinguishable). Worse, `bridge:replay` without `--force` skips every row with `processed_at` set — *including gate-dropped ones* — so a replay after fixing a classifier/gate bug would **silently no-op for exactly the rows you wanted to re-run**, with no hint why. The ledger lost the one fact the operator needed: *what did the bridge decide, and why.*
- **Decision:** add two nullable columns to `agent_dispatches` — `outcome` (string(16): `delivered` | `dropped` | `errored`, the `AgentDispatch::OUTCOME_*` vocabulary) and `reason` (string(255), the human-readable why). `DispatchService` stamps the specific terminal at each exit: `markDelivered($note)` (classifier emitted reactions → intents/handlers ran), `markDropped($reason)` at each gate (`echo: own write` / `echo: own write (reattributed author)` / `actor is not a signal` / `classifier emitted no reactions`), and `recordError` now also sets `outcome=errored`. Both columns are **nullable with no backfill** — pre-DL-036 rows read `outcome=null`, and every reader falls back to the legacy `processed_at`/`error_message` inference (`bridge:inspect` shows `done (pre-DL036)`), so the migration is non-destructive and needs no data migration. `bridge:replay` without `--force` now reports `skipping N already-processed dispatch row(s) — M were gate-DROPPED (recoverable after a gate fix); pass --force to re-run them`, turning the silent no-op into an actionable message.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) **infer outcome at read-time** from `processed_at`/`error_message` (no schema change) — rejected: there's no stored signal that separates a deliberate drop from a handler-noop delivery, so the inference can't be made; the fact has to be *recorded at decision-time* (canon: don't add a read-time fallback for data the write-site should persist). (b) a **separate `dropped_at`/`drop_reason` pair** — rejected: a dispatch has exactly one terminal outcome, so one `outcome` enum + one `reason` is the honest shape (three timestamp columns would imply states that can't co-occur). (c) **a boolean `was_dropped`** — rejected: it can't express `errored`, and `reason` carries the *which-gate* detail an operator actually debugs with. (d) **a non-nullable column with a backfill** — rejected: pre-existing rows have no recoverable outcome (the distinction was never recorded), so an honest `null` (= "decided before DL-036") beats a guessed backfill.
- **Consequences:** new idempotent migration `2026_06_07_000001_add_outcome_to_agent_dispatches` (`Schema::hasColumn` guards; reversible `down()`); `AgentDispatch` gains the `OUTCOME_*` constants + `outcome`/`reason` in `$fillable`; `DispatchService` splits the former single `markDone` into `markDelivered`/`markDropped` (+ `Log::info` per outcome) and the echo/non-signal drops into distinct reasons; `bridge:inspect` renders an `outcome` column + `reason / error`; `bridge:replay` reports the gate-dropped skip count. 8 new `DispatchServiceTest` outcome cases (incl. a `--force`-replay outcome *transition* that pins the satellite fields mutually exclusive — each `mark*` writes the full terminal tuple, nulling the inapplicable field, so a `dropped`→`delivered` re-run can't leave a stale reason that `bridge:inspect` would show next to a `delivered` outcome) + 2 `BridgeCommandsTest` cases (inspect-shows-outcome, replay-skip-report). Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 395/395. No config change; opt-in nothing — the ledger is always-on.

## DL-037 — Adversarial bug-hunt sweep (post-v0.29.0): 6 correctness/security fixes across receiver, dispatch, replay, writeback, diagnostics

- **Date:** 2026-06-08
- **Context:** A four-agent adversarial read of the whole `app/Bridge` surface (receiver/HMAC/adapters · dispatch/classifiers/handlers · writeback · CLI/config) after the v0.29.0 release. **No CRITICAL/HIGH defects** — the HMAC, scope double-check, dedup gate, and the three failure-treatment branches are sound. Six MED/LOW findings were confirmed against the source and fixed. The two console/ledger fixes are pure correctness (no accept/reject change); the other four touch dispatch semantics, a security-exec path, and the receiver's accept/reject boundary, so they were surfaced and explicitly approved before applying.
- **Decision:** ship all six.
  1. **`bridge:replay --force` resets the WHOLE terminal tuple, not just `processed_at`** (sibling of DL-036). `--force` nulled only `processed_at`; a re-run that exits via a *non-terminal* path (durable-handler throw / config throw → 5xx) reaches no `mark*()` stamper, so the row kept its prior `outcome='delivered'` + stale `error_message` next to a now-null `processed_at` — the exact inconsistency DL-036 exists to prevent. `--force` now nulls `outcome`/`reason`/`error_message` too (the second mutation point that must reset the tuple, beside the `mark*` methods).
  2. **`bridge:check` surfaces id-collisions to the console.** A duplicate `kanban_user_id`/`github_user_id` (silent attribution bypass, DL-007 warn) was emitted only via `Log::warning` to the log file, despite a comment claiming `bridge:check` surfaces it. Added `AgentRegistry::collisions()`; `CheckCommand` renders them (warn-level, exit unchanged).
  3. **Receiver field-length guard generalized to every envelope field (5xx→400).** Only `delivery_id` length was asserted; an over-length `scope_id`/`event_type`/`actor_id` hit the DB column limit as a `QueryException` → 5xx → an upstream retry-storm of a deterministically-bad body. Replaced `assertDeliveryIdLength` with `assertFieldLengths(EventDto)` (all four columns), called by both adapters — *fix the primitive, audit the siblings*. An over-length field is now a deterministic 400 (`InvalidEnvelope`), matching the `delivery_id` rationale.
  4. **Same-event target coalescing keys on `(handler, debounceKey)`, not `debounceKey` alone.** The default `debounceKey` is the `targetId`, so two targets for the same subject routed to *different* handlers (e.g. `channel_push` + `log_intent`) collided last-wins and silently dropped one. No shipped classifier triggers it; it's a custom-classifier footgun. Prefixing the coalescing key with the handler can only *prevent* an erroneous drop — no shipped path changes.
  5. **`spawn_detached` resolves `setsid` to an absolute path.** `setsid` was exec'd by bare name, so a classifier-payload `env.PATH` could redirect *which* `setsid` ran — sidestepping the `cmd[0]` absolute-path allowlist (the launcher execs `cmd`). Now resolved to an absolute path (`bridge.spawn.setsid_path`, env `BRIDGE_SPAWN_SETSID_PATH`, auto-detected, fail-closed). Opt-in surface (`BRIDGE_SPAWN_ENABLED`), but a real allowlist bypass.
  6. **`KanbanClient::readBoard` scan stop-condition follows the documented `links.next` contract.** The board-read scan used a short-page heuristic while the integration contract specifies "page until `links.next === null`"; the in-house consumer was the one not honoring the rule the bridge wrote down. Now stops on `links.next === null` when a DL-146 kanban serves `links` (no wasted extra request at an exact page multiple, no false truncation flag), falling back to the short-page heuristic for a pre-DL-146 kanban that serves no `links`. Not a data-loss fix (the heuristic terminated correctly) — a contract-alignment + efficiency fix; also corrected a stale docstring that falsely claimed the search endpoint returns no `meta`/`links`.
- **Alternatives considered:** for (3), keep `delivery_id`-only and accept the 5xx-storm on oversized siblings — rejected (the guard's own rationale applies verbatim to every field through the same INSERT). For (4), document the global-key footgun instead of fixing — rejected (the correct coalescing identity is per-handler; documenting a sharp edge you can dull is worse). For (5), strip `PATH` from the child env instead of an absolute `setsid` — rejected (would also break a legitimately custom child `PATH`; pinning the launcher absolute is the narrower fix). For (6), switch fully to `links.next` with no short-page fallback — rejected (would break a pre-DL-146 kanban that serves no `links`).
- **Consequences:** edits to `ReplayCommand`, `AgentRegistry` + `CheckCommand`, `AbstractWebhookAdapter` + `KanbanAdapter` + `GitHubAdapter`, `DispatchService`, `SpawnDetachedHandler` + `config/bridge.php`, `KanbanClient`. New env `BRIDGE_SPAWN_SETSID_PATH` (documented in `docs/config-schema.md`). 9 new tests (replay-force-tuple-reset, check-surfaces-collision, 3× adapter over-length, distinct-handlers-same-key, setsid-fail-closed, 2× readBoard-links-next). Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 404/404 · doc-refs clean. The receiver accept/reject change is (3) only: over-length field → 400 (was 5xx). Ships in the next bridge release.

## DL-038 — `examples/channel-servers/package.json` `version` is the drift signal for copied snapshots, enforced by a CI version-bump gate

- **Date:** 2026-06-08
- **Context:** A peer integrator reported (verified against v0.29.0 source) that the reference channel MCP server's `package.json` has sat at `"version": "0.1.0"` since the repo's first commit and was **never bumped** — including by DL-033 (v0.28), which re-pinned `package-lock.json` and rewrote the README (`npm install`→`npm ci`, Node ≥ 20) but left `package.json` untouched. The README tells consumers to **copy** the directory into their own (often per-agent) deployment, so a copied snapshot drifts silently on the next bridge update: no single field reveals staleness — only a full tree-diff against canonical does. DL-033's reproducible-install/audit-gate intent is silently defeated for any agent provisioned from a stale snapshot, and the channel server is a real trust boundary (bearer token, loopback POSTs as the agent's OS user) — exactly the file you most want consumers running the pinned, audited version of. The drift DL-033 closed in the repo reopened one level downstream.
- **Decision:** make `package.json` `version` the **drift signal** — bump it on every change to the shipped channel-server files — and **enforce the convention as a guarantee** with a third job in the already-path-filtered `channel-server-supply-chain.yml`: on a PR, if any shipped file under `examples/channel-servers/**` changes (excluding the gitignored `node_modules` and the CI workflow itself) without a `package.json` `version` bump (base..head diff of the version field), the job fails with a remediation message. Bumped the long-stale `0.1.0` → `0.2.0` now (capturing the accumulated DL-033 state as the first signed version; `npm version --no-git-tag-version` moves `package.json` + `package-lock.json` together so the existing `npm ci` drift gate stays green). Added a README "Staying in sync" note (compare your copy's version against canonical; a symlink never drifts).
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) a separate `CHANNEL_SERVER_VERSION` stamp file — rejected: `package.json` already has a `version` field that's the natural home, and a second file is more surface to keep in sync.
