(b) a changelog note only ("re-sync downstream snapshots") — rejected: relies on humans reading release notes and re-syncing, the same silent-drift failure mode (DL-033's "degraded states must be loud" posture). (c) a `bridge:check` sub-check comparing a deployed channel server against the reference — rejected for now: the bridge doesn't know where downstream copies live, and it's far more surface than a one-field comparison the consumer can do themselves; a possible future enhancement. The chosen option is the lowest-cost durable signal and composes with the existing DL-033 gate so the bump can't be forgotten.
- **Consequences:** `examples/channel-servers/package.json` + `package-lock.json` → `0.2.0`; new `version-bump-guard` job in `channel-server-supply-chain.yml` (PR-only, `fetch-depth: 0` for the merge-base diff); README § Staying in sync. No app code, no migration, no runtime change — example + CI + docs only. Going forward, any PR touching the shipped channel-server files must bump the version or CI fails. Ships in the next bridge release.

## DL-039 — `channel.socket` expands `${XDG_RUNTIME_DIR}`/`${uid}` (uid-agnostic) + a loud `bridge:check` / runtime error when its parent dir is missing

- **Date:** 2026-06-09
- **Context:** A peer integrator (verified against source) hit a silent, confusing break restoring a channel install onto a host where the OS uid changed (e.g. `1008`→`1005`). The Node channel server **derives** its bind path (`$XDG_RUNTIME_DIR/agent-webhook-bridge-channel-${BRIDGE_CHANNEL_NAME}.sock`, so `BRIDGE_CHANNEL_SOCKET` is optional), but the **bridge had no equivalent** — `channel.socket` had to be an explicit absolute path, which on systemd Linux pins the uid (`/run/user/<uid>/…`). After a uid change the old `/run/user/<old-uid>` dir is gone, so the channel server dies on bind and the bridge keeps POSTing the stale path. The failure was effectively silent: `channel_push` *did* throw at runtime, but as a **best-effort** handler error (logged + recorded as a dispatch note, never surfaced), and its message — *"socket does not exist (start the channel server first)"* — **misdiagnosed** the uid case (the server is fine; the path is wrong). `bridge:check` validated the channel **token** but not the **socket**, so a post-restore pre-flight was falsely clean.
- **Decision:** ship the FR's option 1 (loud failure — *worth shipping regardless*) **and** option 3 (placeholder expansion). **(1)** `bridge:check` now warns (not fails — the socket itself is the server's to create) when a configured `channel.socket`'s **parent dir** is missing or non-writable, naming the likely uid mismatch; and `ChannelPushHandler::validateSocketPath` distinguishes *parent-dir-missing (uid mismatch / host restore)* from *socket-missing (server not up)*. **(3)** `PathHelper::expandRuntimeTokens` expands `${XDG_RUNTIME_DIR}` and `${uid}` in `channel.socket` at config-load (before `SocketPath::isValid`), so an operator writes the **uid-agnostic** literal `${XDG_RUNTIME_DIR}/agent-webhook-bridge-channel-<name>.sock` and the uid drops out of config. `${XDG_RUNTIME_DIR}` resolves to `$XDG_RUNTIME_DIR`, or **`/run/user/<posix_getuid()>` when the env is unset** (PHP-FPM usually doesn't inherit `XDG_RUNTIME_DIR`, so deriving from the running uid is the robust resolution); an unresolvable token throws (fail-closed).
- **Alternatives considered:** the FR's **option 2 (derive-when-unset, omit `channel.socket` entirely)** — rejected: the bridge **deliberately removed `channel.name`** (DL-007), so it has no channel name to build the full `…-<name>.sock` path; option 2 would *reintroduce* a name field and reverse that simplification. Option 3 gets the same uid-agnosticism while keeping the explicit name the operator already aligns with the server, and stays purely additive. Reading `XDG_RUNTIME_DIR` only (no uid fallback) — rejected: FPM lacks the env, so it would resolve empty exactly where it's needed; deriving `/run/user/<uid>` is correct for the systemd case and is what `XDG_RUNTIME_DIR` canonically equals. Making the runtime socket-missing error *fail* (5xx) instead of staying best-effort — rejected: `channel_push` is best-effort by design (the inbox is the durable backstop); the fix is to make the *message* loud + add a pre-flight, not to change the delivery contract.
- **Consequences:** `PathHelper::expandRuntimeTokens` (+ `ConfigException` import); `AgentConfig::resolveChannel` expands before validating; `CheckCommand` channel-socket parent-dir probe; sharper `ChannelPushHandler` error. Docs: `config-schema.md` `channel.socket` row, `agent.yml.example` (uid-agnostic example + rationale), `examples/channel-servers/README.md` (the "bridge does NOT compute that path" guidance corrected → use `${XDG_RUNTIME_DIR}`; channel-server `package.json` bumped `0.2.0`→`0.3.0` per DL-038's gate). The `0600` UDS trust model and the explicit-path escape hatch (macOS/containers) are untouched — additive, no contract break. A pre-PR adversarial review confirmed the security-critical aspects clean (expansion is trusted-YAML-only — a classifier-supplied socket never reaches it; `SocketPath::isValid` is a real backstop against an env-injected traversal; `ConfigException` propagates fail-closed → 5xx) and drove three hardenings: expansion uses `strtr` (one simultaneous pass, so a token inside a substituted value is never re-expanded), an unconsumed `${...}` (typo like `${XDG_RUNTIME}`) throws at load instead of riding as a literal dir, and the uid-restore wording branches on agent-vs-classifier socket so a classifier socket's missing dir isn't misattributed (canon #10). 8 new tests (3 expansion, 1 typo-throws, 3 sharper-error incl. classifier-message, 1 check-warns). Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 414/414. Ships in the next bridge release.

## DL-040 — Standardize on PHP 8.5 (composer floor `^8.3` → `^8.5`, CI runners 8.5)

- **Date:** 2026-06-11
- **Context:** The reference host (both the `dev-agent` and `prod-agent` installs) was upgraded 8.3 → **8.5.7**, in lockstep with the kanban-board upgrade (kanban DL-153). Two gaps: composer declared `"php": "^8.3"`, and every CI runner pinned `php-version: '8.3'` (the shared `setup-app` composite action + the `Security` workflow) — so the validated surface lagged the deployed runtime. Unlike kanban, the bridge needed **no code change**: Laravel 13's stock `config/database.php` already uses `Pdo\Mysql::ATTR_SSL_CA` (not the 8.5-deprecated `PDO::MYSQL_ATTR_SSL_CA`), and the suite was already deprecation-clean under 8.5 (696/696, 0 deprecations).
- **Decision:** bump `composer.json` require to `"php": "^8.5"` (lock content-hash + `platform.php` refreshed; deps frozen); point the `setup-app` composite action and `security.yml` at PHP **8.5**. Doc-sync: `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `CLAUDE_DEPLOYMENT.md` (incl. the operator `systemctl reload php8.3-fpm` → `php8.5-fpm` commands — the FPM service is versioned, so the old command would reload the wrong/absent pool post-upgrade), `CLAUDE_TESTING.md`.
- **Deliberate non-change — the required-check job label:** the `laravel-tests.yml` SQLite job is named `PHPUnit + Pint + PHPStan (PHP 8.3, SQLite)`, and that exact string is a **required status check** pinned in `dev` *and* `main` branch protection (verified via `gh api`). The job now *runs* on 8.5 (via `setup-app`), but renaming the label would leave branch protection waiting forever on the old-named check and **block every PR**. Renaming is therefore deferred to a coordinated step: rename the job + update the `required_status_checks.contexts` on both branches in the same change (a gated branch-protection config op). Until then the label reads "8.3" by design; `CLAUDE_TESTING.md` documents the lag. Append-only history (DL-001/DL-025 consequences, `docs/CHANGELOG.md`) keeps its original "PHP 8.3" — those record what was true at the time.
- **Consequences:** `composer.json`, `composer.lock` (hash + platform only), `.github/actions/setup-app/action.yml`, `.github/workflows/security.yml`, `.github/workflows/laravel-tests.yml` (header comment only), `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `CLAUDE_DEPLOYMENT.md`, `CLAUDE_TESTING.md`. No app code, migration, or `.env` change. An install on PHP <8.5 now fails the `composer install` platform check — intentional. **Follow-up (gated):** coordinated required-check rename + branch-protection contexts update.

## DL-154 — Make a deaf/duplicate channel connector VISIBLE: bind-failure marker + single-session launcher guardrail + bridge:check liveness ping (FR #2444)

- **Date:** 2026-06-12
- **Context (incident):** An agent ran two concurrent Claude Code sessions. The second (active) session's channel connector hit `EADDRINUSE` (the first session's connector held the UDS) and `exit(2)`'d — but its stderr message is **swallowed by Claude Code** (MCP-server startup stderr is not surfaced), so the second session kept running with **no channel = deaf to live-wake**. The bridge kept classifying events to the agent and delivering to the socket the *first (idle)* connector still held, which accepted them (`HTTP 202`) — so `bridge:stats` showed `delivered`/0-errored and `bridge:check` was green, while the session the operator was actually in received nothing. Net: "all connected" yet "the bridge stopped working," diagnosable only by manual process inspection.
- **Root cause (sharpened from the FR):** the rendezvous is keyed on **agent identity** (socket path `…-<name>.sock`), not **session identity**, so which session gets live-wake is decided by a first-come socket-bind race. The connector already *detects* the collision (`EADDRINUSE`) and is the one non-bypassable chokepoint (it runs no matter how Claude was started) — the entire gap is that its refusal is **invisible**.
- **Decision — make the existing refusal visible at three composing points (no cron, no daemon):**
  - **Connector (`examples/channel-servers/agent-webhook-bridge-channel.mjs`):** on `EADDRINUSE` (unix *and* http transports) write a visible **marker file** (ISO timestamp + pid + reason) in addition to the swallowed stderr; the connector that **successfully binds clears** it (cleanup owner = current holder), so the signal reflects the live holder rather than a week-old failure (it persists, by design, until the next successful bind or a launcher (re)start — fail-loud-until-acknowledged). **Surfacing is UDS-only:** the unix marker is the socket's sibling `<socket>.FAILED`, the exact path `bridge:check` derives from `channel.socket`, so it is surfaced on demand. The HTTP transport (minority SSH-tunnel topology) has no `channel.socket` in its agent config (it carries `url`), so `bridge:check` cannot derive its marker — the HTTP marker is keyed by name+port (never masquerading as a socket failure) and its signal is the stderr + `exit(2)` + the file, not `bridge:check`. `package.json` 0.3.0 → 0.4.0 (DL-038 snapshot-drift signal).
  - **Launcher (`examples/start-channel-session.sh`):** a **process-level** single-session refusal (`pgrep -f` for a `claude … server:<channel>` already running this channel) — closes the "started outside the wrapper" bypass and the HTTP topology with no socket to collide on. Framed as a **guardrail, not a guarantee** (it's a cmdline match); the connector's `EADDRINUSE` refusal + marker is the backstop the wrapper can't be. Also clears a stale marker on (re)start.
  - **`bridge:check` (runtime counterpart to its config validation):** on-demand **liveness ping** of `channel.socket` (a UDS connect — distinguishes a live, listening session from a stale socket that would still accept the bridge's push and log `delivered`), and surfaces any `.FAILED` marker. Warn/info only — never fails the check (at preflight the server legitimately may be down).
- **Descoped (deliberately NOT built — canon #6, don't build for states single-session enforcement prevents):** (a) a standalone `bridge:doctor` command that pgreps the Claude **process table** — that couples the stateless webhook app to the channel-server's deployment topology it intentionally stays out of (zero `pgrep`/`/proc` in `app/` today); the cheap part folds into `bridge:check`, and any process-count check belongs in a sibling script under `examples/`. (b) A connector **session-liveness/last-active-at heartbeat endpoint** — only needed to disambiguate the multi-session mess that the single-session guardrail *prevents*. (c) The FR's **post-launch verify-then-KILL** loop — killing a user's just-started interactive session from a wrapper is heavy/surprising, and the marker surfaces the problem immediately anyway.
- **Rejected alternative:** per-session socket paths + bridge fan-out to all live sockets (would dissolve the race so *both* sessions wake) — breaks the one-session-per-agent model and duplicates reactions; bigger change, worse downside.
- **Consequences:** `examples/channel-servers/agent-webhook-bridge-channel.mjs` (marker helpers + EADDRINUSE write + clear-on-bind, both transports), `examples/channel-servers/package.json` (version bump), `examples/start-channel-session.sh` (pgrep guardrail + marker clear), `app/Console/Commands/Bridge/CheckCommand.php` (marker surfacing + liveness ping). Tests: `BridgeCommandsTest` +3 (marker surfaced / socket live / stale-socket warned, the latter two via a `pcntl_fork` UDS listener). The live operator launcher `~/start-claude.sh` should get the same guardrail (operational sync, outside the repo). No app-runtime code (handlers/classifiers/receiver), schema, migration, or `.env` change.

## DL-155 — Correction to DL-154: the launcher SURFACES the `.FAILED` marker, it does not silently clear it (#2444 follow-on)

- **Date:** 2026-06-13
- **Correcting:** DL-154's launcher clause ("Also clears a stale marker on (re)start") and its connector clause ("persists … until the next successful bind **or a launcher (re)start**"). DL-154 itself remains frozen; this entry supersedes those two phrases.
- **Context (gap):** DL-154 designed the `<socket>.FAILED` marker to be **fail-loud-until-acknowledged**, but made `start-channel-session.sh` `rm -f "${SOCK}.FAILED"` *before* binding — a **silent** clear. So the one moment the operator returns to relaunch a session that previously came up deaf, the durable signal is wiped without ever being shown. The acknowledgment DL-154 intended was real, but **uninformed** — which defeats the marker's whole purpose (a customer FR, board-8 #2456, surfaced it). The launcher clear was also redundant: the connector already clears the marker unconditionally on a successful bind (`agent-webhook-bridge-channel.mjs` `server.listen` callback → `clearFailureMarker()`), and a launch always triggers a bind attempt.
- **Decision:** the launcher **surfaces** the marker loudly to stderr at launch (the prior deaf-session's timestamp + pid + reason) and does **not** clear it. The **connector is the sole clearer**, on the next successful bind (which the launch triggers moments later) — so a clean relaunch still ends with no marker, but a relaunch whose new session *also* comes up deaf correctly leaves a fresh marker. Net: the marker now persists until the next *successful bind*, full stop; launcher-restart becomes a **surface point, not a clear point**. Single owner for the clear (the connector), aligned with DL-154's own "cleanup owner = current holder."
- **Why not keep a launcher clear (even loud):** no second clearer is needed — the connector already owns it on bind, and a launcher clear can only ever race ahead of the bind it's redundant with. Surface-only is strictly less code and removes the silent-wipe footgun.
- **Out of scope (held):** the FR's heavier Part C (fork + post-launch verify-then-kill) and a standalone `bridge:doctor` stay descoped exactly as DL-154 ruled (canon #6) — no recurrence evidence to reopen them.
- **Consequences:** `examples/start-channel-session.sh` (replace the `rm -f` with a surface-if-present block), `examples/channel-servers/README.md` lifecycle note (launcher surfaces, not clears). The deployed `~/start-claude.sh` gets the same operational sync. No connector/`bridge:check`/app code change — the connector's clear-on-bind already does the right thing. Behavior change is operator-facing stderr only; no schema/migration/`.env`/API change. (The v0.32.0 CHANGELOG entry stays as-is — it faithfully records what that release shipped; this correction lands in the next release's notes.)

## DL-156 — `bridge:check` is HTTP-transport-aware: liveness-probe the loopback/tunnel port + surface the HTTP `.FAILED` marker; channel-server marker base is `os.tmpdir()` (Windows-correct) (Sola PM FR-2)

- **Date:** 2026-06-13
- **Context (gap):** DL-154/155 made a deaf/duplicate channel connector visible — but only for the **UDS** transport. `bridge:check` derived both the `.FAILED` marker path and the liveness ping from `channel.socket` (`CheckCommand.php`: `$marker = channel.socket.'.FAILED'`; `stream_socket_client('unix://…')`). An **HTTP-transport** agent (the multi-host / SSH-reverse-tunnel topology — a peer integrator's *most common* shape) carries `channel.url`, not `channel.socket`, so `bridge:check` could neither probe liveness nor surface the marker. The deaf-session signal was invisible at preflight for exactly the bind-race-prone (remote, tunneled) agents. Separately, the channel server's `markerPath()` HTTP branch fell back to a literal `'/tmp'` when `XDG_RUNTIME_DIR` is unset — which under Node on **Windows** resolves to `C:\tmp`, never matching the Windows launcher's `%TEMP%` lookup, so the marker was unfindable there.
- **Decision:**
  - **`bridge:check` HTTP branch** (when `channel.url` set, no `socket`): parse `host:port` from the URL and run the liveness probe as a **TCP connect to `host:port`** (warn/info, never fails — DL-154 posture). This is the meaningful **cross-host** check: `bridge:check` runs on the receiver host, and a connect to the loopback endpoint travels the reverse tunnel to the remote connector. Also surface the HTTP marker **best-effort** (`$XDG_RUNTIME_DIR` else `/tmp`-equiv `/agent-webhook-bridge-channel-<name>.http-<port>.FAILED`, keyed on the agent name as the `BRIDGE_CHANNEL_NAME` proxy) — only meaningful when `bridge:check` runs **on the agent host**, since the marker file lives where the connector runs.
  - **Marker surfacing on the agent host is the launcher's job** (FR-1), which knows `BRIDGE_CHANNEL_NAME`/port exactly; `bridge:check`'s primary HTTP value is the liveness probe.
  - **Channel server `markerPath()`**: `XDG_RUNTIME_DIR || '/tmp'` → `XDG_RUNTIME_DIR || os.tmpdir()` so the base is `%TEMP%` on Windows (matching the Windows launcher) and unchanged (`/tmp`/`$TMPDIR`) on Linux/macOS. `examples/channel-servers/` example → **0.4.2** (DL-038 drift signal).
- **Topology caveat (why marker surfacing isn't symmetric with UDS):** in the tunnel topology the full bridge (and `artisan bridge:check`) runs only on the receiver host; the remote agents run just the channel server + Claude Code. So the remote HTTP marker is unreachable from `bridge:check` — the launcher on the agent host owns its surfacing. The liveness probe is the cross-host-meaningful half and is the symmetric win.
- **Consequences:** `app/Console/Commands/Bridge/CheckCommand.php` (HTTP branch: liveness TCP probe + best-effort marker), `examples/channel-servers/agent-webhook-bridge-channel.mjs` (`os.tmpdir()` fallback + comment), `examples/channel-servers/package.json` (0.4.2), `docs/config-schema.md` (`channel.url` row). Tests: `BridgeCommandsTest` +3 (HTTP live / not-answering / HTTP marker surfaced). Warn/info only — no receiver/handler/schema/migration/`.env` change. Pairs with DL-157 (canonical cross-platform launcher).

## DL-157 — Canonical self-resolving, transport-aware, cross-platform channel launcher (Sola PM FR-1)

- **Date:** 2026-06-13
- **Context (gap):** the shipped launcher was bash + UDS-only, so every consumer hand-rolled a per-OS/per-transport copy that froze at its install version and drifted (launchers found several minor versions stale, missing the v0.32/v0.33 guards). The DL-154/155 deaf-session guards didn't apply on HTTP (no socket file) or Windows (no `pgrep`/`sed`), and force-fitting the bash onto Windows/HTTP silently broke live-wake. A peer integrator (Sola PM) — whose multi-agent, multi-host (HTTP-over-SSH-tunnel) + Windows topology is the most common real-world shape — supplied validated reference launchers; this folds them into the canonical examples.
- **Decision — one self-resolving launcher per OS, sharing the same identity chain + guards:**
  - `examples/start-channel-session.sh` (Linux UDS+HTTP) + `examples/start-claude.ps1` + `examples/start-claude.bat` (Windows HTTP-tunnel).
  - **Self-resolving identity** (first hit): `--channel` → `$BRIDGE_CHANNEL_NAME` → `settings.local.json` `.env.BRIDGE_CHANNEL_NAME` → `<namespace>-<agent>` from `$COORD_CONFIG.bridge.channel_namespace` + `$COORD_AGENT`. **`settings.local.json` is load-bearing:** the launcher runs in the login shell, which doesn't inherit Claude Code's session-injected env — relying on exported env alone is the #1 "can't resolve channel" failure, so the keys are read from the file (jq / `ConvertFrom-Json`). One launcher serves any agent → kills the per-agent-copy drift.
  - **Transport-aware guards:** UDS — socket-curl stale check + stale-socket rm + `pgrep` single-session; HTTP — TCP-port listener probe + process-table/listening-port single-session. DL-154/155 marker surfacing (never clear) rendered for both, with the transport-correct marker path.
  - **Export the resolved identity before `exec`** (`BRIDGE_CHANNEL_NAME`/`TRANSPORT`/`PORT`, and `SOCKET` for UDS): the channel server otherwise re-derives its endpoint independently from `~/.mcp.json`, and a divergence guards one path while the server binds another — a deaf-session footgun. Exporting guarantees the server binds exactly what the launcher guarded. (Added on top of Sola's reference, which resolved+guarded but didn't export.)
  - **Vocabulary fix:** the server reads `BRIDGE_CHANNEL_TRANSPORT` and branches on `=== 'unix'`; the launcher normalizes `''`/`uds`/`unix` → `unix` (and validates) so exporting it can't push the server into the wrong branch.
- **Windows specifics (baked-in, don't regress):** PowerShell + a `.bat` ExecutionPolicy shim (not pure cmd — native JSON / `Get-NetTCPConnection` / PID-tree teardown). The reverse tunnel runs as a **`-WindowStyle Hidden`** side process torn down by PID tree — `Minimized` (`SW_SHOWMINIMIZED`) activates the window and a delayed child steals focus. A Git-Bash-style `COORD_CONFIG` (`/c/…`) is normalized to `<drive>:/…`.
- **Scope:** Windows shipped as validated reference scripts (Sola PM validated end-to-end), not the "documented recipe only" originally floated — a working script beats a recipe given the force-fit hazard, and they exist. Marker base aligned cross-platform via DL-156 (`os.tmpdir()`).
- **Consequences:** `examples/start-channel-session.sh` (rewritten self-resolving + HTTP), `examples/start-claude.ps1` + `examples/start-claude.bat` (new), `CLAUDE_DEPLOYMENT.md` ("The canonical channel launcher" + "Multi-agent channel-server distribution" reconcile, FR-3). Examples + docs only — no app code, schema, migration, or `.env` change. The deployed operator launchers get the same operational sync (outside the repo). Pairs with DL-156.

## DL-158 — Canonical reference for a GitHub-issue-comment classifier (forward the comment identity) + classifier reconcile step (Sola PM FR / #2514)

- **Date:** 2026-06-14
- **Context (gap):** a peer integrator (Sola PM) reported that the `github_issue_comment` channel notification they consume carries only the thread (`number`), not the comment — forcing an O(number-of-comments) thread re-read plus a positional guess for "which comment is new." That guess is a footgun: GitHub's REST issue-comments endpoint paginates 30/page, oldest-first, with no `sort`/`direction` param, so a naive `.[-1]` on an un-paginated fetch returns the 30th comment (not the newest) on any thread with >30 comments — new replies look like stale replays and get dropped. **Traced to ground:** that notification is **not produced by the bridge.** Core ships only the kanban-event classifiers (`InboxOnly`/`EventDriven`) + `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` (PR-only, emits no Intent); `issue_comment.*` parses (`GitHubAdapter`) but classifies to an empty result. The notification comes from an operator-authored **custom classifier** (confirmed: the integrator's own `SolaPmClassifier`), which already receives the full webhook body via `ClassifyContext->payload` (including `comment.id`/`created_at`/`html_url`) and forwards an arbitrary `Intent` payload verbatim to the channel. So the consumer-side fix was ~3 additive lines in *their* classifier (applied integrator-side); **zero core change was needed.** The remaining gap is that every integrator hand-rolls this surfacer with no canonical reference, so the clean `comment_id` forwarding drifts (a second integrator, AIMLA, forwards only an id-bearing `html_url`, forcing a fragment regex).
- **Decision:** canonicalize a **minimal worked-example** classifier in [`docs/customization.md`](docs/customization.md) ("Surfacing GitHub issue comments to a channel") — `issue_comment.created` → a `github_issue_comment` Intent whose payload forwards `comment_id` + `comment_created_at` + `comment_html_url`, paired with a `channel_push` (target_id == subject_id). It documents the pagination footgun as the *why*, notes the same shape generalizes to PR review comments, and cross-references the existing recipient-aware / shared-identity sections as an **optional** addressing layer kept out of the base. Plus extend the [`CLAUDE_DEPLOYMENT.md`](CLAUDE_DEPLOYMENT.md) "Reconcile out-of-repo copies" step to cover the custom classifier: new installs start from the reference; each update diffs the deployed classifier against it and adopts improvements (a reconcile-merge preserving deployment-specific extensions, not a blind replace).
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) **ship it as a wired/default core classifier** — rejected (canon #6): reverses the deliberate "GitHub is machine-only / no agent in the loop" core posture, and the addressing/recipient policy is deployment-specific (DL-022 keeps it in the operator's classifier, not the core). (b) **ship a real `examples/classifiers/*.php` file** — rejected: `examples/` is excluded from Pint and outside the PHPStan `app/Bridge` scope, so a file there gets no more gate coverage than a snippet, while a file under `app/` would ship an autoloaded class we don't want as core; a `docs/customization.md` snippet matches how the other four custom-classifier patterns are already documented. (c) **adopt the integrator's submitted `CoordinationClassifier.php` verbatim** — rejected: it declares `namespace App\Bridge\Classifiers` (would ship an autoloaded class), and bundles one coordination framework's shared-identity addressing protocol (label/`FROM:`-line reattribution) that shouldn't read as bridge-blessed; the minimal example + a pointer to the optional layer is the right altitude.
- **Validation:** the snippet was extracted and exercised against the real bridge classes (a throwaway Feature test: real `ClassifyContext`/`AgentConfig`, representative `issue_comment.created` payload) — emits the `github_issue_comment` Intent with `comment_id`/`created_at`/`html_url`, pairs a `channel_push` with `target_id == subject_id`, skips non-`created` events; `php -l` clean. (Doc snippet ⇒ not under Pint/PHPStan scope, same as the existing classifier examples.)
- **Consequences:** `docs/customization.md` (new "Surfacing GitHub issue comments" worked example), `CLAUDE_DEPLOYMENT.md` ("Reconcile out-of-repo copies" now covers the custom classifier). Docs only — no app code, classifier, schema, migration, or `.env` change; no behavior change to any shipped class. FR #2514's consumer issue was already resolved integrator-side; this closes the canonicalization follow-on.

## DL-159 — Channel-server example unlinks its UNIX socket on every ordinary quit (server-side counterpart to DL-154/155/157) (Sola PM / #2533)

- **Date:** 2026-06-14
- **Context (gap):** a peer integrator (Sola PM) reported that the reference channel server (`examples/channel-servers/agent-webhook-bridge-channel.mjs`, 0.4.2) had exactly one signal handler — `process.on('SIGTERM', () => { server.close(); process.exit(0); })` — and no explicit `fs.unlink`. Node only runs that on SIGTERM, so terminal-close (SIGHUP), Ctrl-C (SIGINT), and parent-pipe close (stdin EOF) all leak the pathname AF_UNIX socket. A leftover pathname socket makes the *next* direct `bind()` fail `EADDRINUSE` on Linux **regardless of any listener**, so the server writes a `<socket>.FAILED` deaf-session marker reading "another session already holds the channel" when zero sessions run. The launcher's stale-socket guard (DL-157) auto-recovers, so severity is low, but the false markers read as a live concurrency collision. Two secondary defects same-area: (a) even on the SIGTERM path, `server.close()` unlinks *asynchronously* while `process.exit(0)` runs synchronously on the next line — an in-flight connection at SIGTERM can leak; (b) no parent-death self-exit, so an orphaned server lingers holding the socket and the launcher's liveness probe then gets a live response and aborts (worse than the stale-file case). This is the server-side counterpart the DL-154/155/157 deaf-session work was missing.
- **Decision:** route SIGTERM/SIGINT/SIGHUP through one idempotent `shutdown()` that calls `server.close()` then **synchronously** `fs.unlinkSync(SOCKET_PATH)` (UNIX transport only) so the socket is gone deterministically before `process.exit()` — fixing both the missing-handler leak and the async/exit race. The unlink is gated on a `bound` flag set in the listen-success callback, so a signal during the `EADDRINUSE` failure window never removes a *live peer's* socket we don't own. Parent-death without a signal is handled via `process.stdin.on('end', …)`.
- **The stdin hook — why not `onclose`, why no `resume()`:** the FR's *optional* suggestion was `process.stdin.resume()` + `stdin.on('end')`. Reading the MCP SDK (`@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/.../server/stdio.js`): `StdioServerTransport` registers `stdin.on('data')` (which already puts stdin in flowing mode) and `'error'`, but **no `'end'`/`'close'` listener** — so it does NOT surface parent-pipe EOF via the protocol's `onclose`. Hence `mcp.onclose` won't fire on EOF (it's wired anyway as cheap defense-in-depth for a protocol-level close), and the real EOF hook must be a direct `stdin.on('end')` — a *separate* event from `'data'`, so it doesn't conflict with the SDK reader, and `resume()` is unnecessary (the SDK already flows stdin). Adopting the FR's `resume()` verbatim would have been redundant; the bare `'end'` listener is the correct minimal form.
- **Out of scope (agreed):** SIGKILL and hard crashes can never run cleanup and will always leak the socket — that is exactly what the launcher's stale-socket guard + the `.FAILED` marker backstop (DL-154/155/157) are for. The layered design is correct; this only closes the ordinary-quit paths.
- **Validation:** exercised on the real surface via a Node child-process harness (clean env, dedicated temp socket, deterministic `child.kill()` + controlled stdin): SIGTERM/SIGINT/SIGHUP/stdin-EOF all remove the socket; SIGKILL leaves it (backstop control). `node --check` clean. (An earlier shell harness reported a false "leak" — background processes in a non-interactive shell have SIGINT set to ignore and inherit a closed stdin; not a code defect.)
- **Consequences:** `examples/channel-servers/agent-webhook-bridge-channel.mjs` (the shutdown machinery), `examples/channel-servers/README.md` (Lifecycle notes bullet), example version **0.4.2 → 0.4.3** in `package.json` + `package-lock.json` (DL-038 drift signal; CI `version-bump-guard` + `channel-server-supply-chain`). Example + docs only — no app code, classifier, schema, migration, or `.env` change.

## DL-160 — Branch-create push → card "In Progress": derive work-begun from the artifact (writeback `started` outcome) (#2650)

- **Date:** 2026-06-19
- **Context:** The GitHub-PR → card-move writeback (DL-021) only advances a card once a **pull request** exists — i.e. once work is far enough along to open a PR. The earlier, equally-deterministic "work has begun" signal — **creating the feature branch** — was unused, so a card sat in Backlog/Prioritized through the whole first stretch of work and only jumped to "In Review" at PR-open. The user wants that gap closed by codifying work-begun from the artifact (the branch), not from any agent in the loop, consistent with the writeback's "machine-only" posture.
- **Decision:** add a fifth writeback outcome, **`started`**, driven by a GitHub **`push`** event (already parsed by `GitHubAdapter`; the classifier previously ignored it). `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` now emits a `kanban_move_card` target with `outcome: 'started'` when the push **created a branch** (`payload.created === true`) whose ref (`refs/heads/…`) carries a `DL-NNN`, correlating DL→card exactly as the PR path. Gated to fire **once on branch creation** (`created === true`, not every subsequent push), and a `dependabot/*` branch or a DL-less ref is a no-op. Like every outcome, **which board+stage `started` maps to is operator config** (`writeback.json` `stages.started`), never hard-coded (board 8's In-Progress is stage 49, but that lives in config).
  - **No-stage-regression guard (the load-bearing safety decision).** A `started` move must only **promote** a card — never drag an already-In-Review/Shipped/Released card backward (re-creating or force-pushing an old branch re-fires `push`+`created`). The guard lives in `KanbanMoveCardHandler`: for `outcome === 'started'` it reads the card's current `workflow_stage_id` and applies the move **only** when that stage is in the mapping's new optional **`started_from_stages`** (the board's Backlog/Prioritized stage ids). Config-driven, not hard-coded. Parsed strictly like `board_id`/`stages`/`swimlane_id` (a non-list or non-numeric element fails the config closed). **Absent `started_from_stages` ⇒ the `started` move is refused** (fail-closed: the guard can't know what's safe to promote from — the DL-026 "never silently do the wrong thing" rule), logged + no-op. Idempotent (the already-in-target-stage short-circuit still applies first).
  - **PR path untouched.** The `push` branch is a pure addition ahead of the existing `pull_request.` logic; the four PR outcomes and their tests are byte-identical.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) **fire on every push (drop `created`)** — rejected: a `started` move would re-fire on each commit; `created === true` makes it a one-shot at branch birth (idempotent on the board, but no wasted reads/moves). (b) **hard-code the promote-from set to Backlog/Prioritized stage ids** — rejected (canon #6 / config-driven): stage ids are board-specific; `started_from_stages` keeps the guard operator-config like `stages`. (c) **default-allow when `started_from_stages` is unset** (promote from anywhere except the target) — rejected: that is exactly the silent-regression risk the FR calls "critical"; fail-closed (refuse until the operator declares the safe source stages) is the safe default. (d) **enforce the guard in the classifier** — rejected (DL-021 decision): current-stage is a kanban read on the *durable* path; keeping the read+guard in the handler matches where the belongs-to-board and idempotency reads already live, and lets a transient read failure retry as a 5xx rather than a treatment-A classify error.
- **Operator step (REQUIRED, not bridge-managed):** the repo webhook must now subscribe to **push** events in addition to **Pull requests**. `bridge:provision` manages only the `kanban` provider — it does **not** touch GitHub webhooks (no repo-admin token, by design), so the event subscription is configured by hand in the repo's **Settings → Webhooks**. A webhook left on *Pull requests* only will silently never fire the `started` move. Operators must also map a `started` stage **and** set `started_from_stages` to enable the trigger.
- **Validation:** `vendor/bin/phpunit` green (438/438 with APP_KEY set), `vendor/bin/pint` clean, `vendor/bin/phpstan analyse -c phpstan-laravel.neon` 0 errors (level 7). New tests: classifier (branch-create+DL → `started`; push to existing branch → no-op; DL-less / dependabot / tag ref → no-op; unmapped repo / no matching card → no-op; bundled DL → one target per card); handler (promote from an allowed Backlog stage; **no regression** from In-Review; refused when `started_from_stages` unset; idempotent when already In-Progress); config (parses `started` outcome + `started_from_stages`; strict on non-list / non-numeric element). Not yet exercised end-to-end against a live repo webbook subscribed to push.
- **Consequences:** `app/Bridge/Classifiers/GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier.php` (push branch + `classifyPush`), `app/Bridge/Handlers/KanbanMoveCardHandler.php` (the `started` regression guard), `app/Bridge/Writeback/WritebackConfig.php` (`started` in `OUTCOMES`, `started_from_stages` parse), `app/Bridge/Writeback/WritebackMapping.php` (`$startedFromStages`), `docs/writeback.md` (the trigger + the push-event subscription step + the no-regression guard), tests across classifier/handler/config. **Behavior change:** a new outward card-move trigger — gated by operator config (`started` stage + `started_from_stages`) and OFF until both are set, so an upgraded install with neither is inert. Requires the operator to add **push** to the repo webhook.

## DL-161 — Dependabot writeback ARCHIVES the card on a closed-unmerged PR (#2659)

- **Date:** 2026-06-19
- **Context:** The DL-024 dependabot writeback (`create_dependabot_cards`) creates a card per dependabot PR and moves it through the `stages` map. On a `closed_unmerged` PR the handler only ever `moveCard`'d it to the `closed_unmerged` stage — and dependabot **routinely closes its own PRs** (a newer bump supersedes an older one, or a maintainer closes it), so those cards piled up live on the board. A peer integrator (Sola PM, #2659) reported 7 cards sitting in Backlog whose dependabot PRs had been closed-unmerged 8–11 days earlier: their mapping had no (or a non-terminal) `closed_unmerged` stage, so the card was born at `opened` (Backlog) and never retired. A move can only shuffle a card between columns; it cannot retire one — retiring is the kanban lifecycle verb (`_action: archive`), a different operation than a `workflow_stage_id` write.
- **Decision:** on a `closed_unmerged` dependabot PR with an existing card, **archive** the card instead of moving it. New `KanbanClient::archiveCard()` issues `PATCH {"_action":"archive"}` (the top-level lifecycle verb) and **reports whether the response confirms the archive** (`data.archived_at` non-null) — a `{"task":{"archived_at":…}}` *field* PATCH returns 200 but silently no-ops, so a `false` return catches a wrong-verb / contract regression. It **returns the signal rather than throwing**: that 200-but-not-archived failure is *deterministic*, so 5xx-ing it would retry-storm an unfixable event for ~11 days — the DL-020 / `DispatchService` anti-pattern. The handler treats `false` as **permanent**: `Log::error` (loud, monitorable) + no-op, never a retry-storm. A genuine HTTP error still throws via `->throw()` (transient 5xx → retry, 4xx → permanent), exactly as the move path does. The handler's `closed_unmerged` branch needs **no stage mapping** (archive ignores `stages.closed_unmerged` for the dependabot path). "No card + closed_unmerged → skip" is unchanged. Idempotent for free: kanban excludes archived cards from by-ref/search correlation, so a redelivered close finds nothing and no-ops.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) **move to a configurable terminal lane** instead of archive — rejected as the default (canon #6): archive is the FR's primary ask and the cleanest fit for routine churn; a `dependabot_close_action` knob is the extension point if an operator ever needs move-to-lane, not built speculatively. (b) **keep moving to `closed_unmerged` and tell operators to map it to a Done column** — rejected: a "Done" column still accumulates dead dependabot cards; archive removes them from the board entirely. (c) **also archive DL-tracked cards on closed_unmerged** — rejected (scope): a closed-unmerged *DL* PR usually means work continues, so that path still just moves; the change is dependabot-only. (d) **assert via a follow-up read** that the card left active search — rejected: an extra round-trip when the archive response already carries `archived_at`.
- **Validation:** `vendor/bin/phpunit` green (with `APP_KEY`), `vendor/bin/pint` clean, `vendor/bin/phpstan` level-7 0 errors. New tests: client (`archiveCard` sends the `_action` verb not a field write; returns `false` when the response shows it didn't archive); handler (closed-unmerged archives an existing card not moves it; archives even with **no** `closed_unmerged` stage mapped; archives **all** N matching cards; a not-confirmed archive logs `error` + no-ops without throwing — no retry-storm; no-card-on-close still skips). Verified the archive response shape (`data.archived_at` timestamp) + idempotency (archived card excluded from active search) against the live kanban API before coding. The not-confirmed → log+no-op choice (vs throw) was adopted in pre-PR review to honor the codebase's deterministic-failure-must-not-5xx-storm convention.
- **Consequences:** `app/Bridge/Writeback/KanbanClient.php` (`archiveCard`), `app/Bridge/Handlers/KanbanDependabotCardHandler.php` (closed-unmerged → archive, restructured so the archive path needs no stage), `docs/writeback.md` (dependabot lifecycle table + the archive note), tests. **Behavior change:** a closed-unmerged dependabot PR now **archives** its card (previously moved to the `closed_unmerged` stage). Only affects the dependabot-card path (`create_dependabot_cards: true`); the DL-tracked move path is byte-identical. No new config, no migration.

## DL-162 — `bridge:check` flags a `create_dependabot_cards` mapping whose board lacks the create-payload custom fields (#2949)

- **Date:** 2026-06-20
- **Context:** A mapping with `create_dependabot_cards: true` makes `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` POST a new card with the custom-field payload keys `pr_number`, `pr_url`, `origin`. Kanban 422s any payload key not registered as a custom field on the target board (its DL-028). The handler treats a 4xx as **permanent** → `Log::warning` + no-op (DL-020). So a board missing even one of those fields makes **every** dependabot-card create 422 and vanish: the delivery returns 200, the operator sees nothing, no card appears. Found live on board 8 — `create_dependabot_cards` was on and the agent was subscribed, yet zero dependabot cards had ever been created, because the board defined `dl_number/pr_number/version_target/origin` but **no `pr_url`**. This is the DL-026 "degraded writeback must be loud" posture being violated for the *create* path, the exact twin of the DL-027 swimlane gap (a static config/board mismatch that never self-resolves and is invisible per-event).
- **Decision:** in the per-mapping board probe (the same loop as the DL-027 swimlane check), when `createDependabotCards` is set, read the board's registered custom-field keys via `GET /boards/{id}/custom_fields.json` and warn loudly if any of the create-payload keys is missing — naming the missing field(s) and the consequence (silent 422 no-op). Warn-level, never fails the check (a board may be configured after the mapping; same posture as DL-026/027/030). The required key list is **not** duplicated: `KanbanDependabotCardHandler::CREATE_PAYLOAD_KEYS` is the single source of truth that both the create call and the check read, so the check can never drift from the actual payload.
- **Why a dedicated read (not preload):** kanban's lightweight `preload.json` carries swimlanes/stages but **not** custom fields (verified against `BoardResource`), so the new `KanbanClient::boardCustomFieldKeys()` hits the dedicated `custom_fields.json` endpoint and reads each field's `key` (kanban's payload-key identity), not `slug`/`label`.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) auto-create the missing custom fields — rejected: whether a board *should* track its own dependabot bumps is an operator decision (canon #14, an outward-facing schema change), and the writeback token is least-privilege; surface, don't mutate. (b) make the handler create-422 loud at runtime — rejected as the primary fix: a repeated per-event config-mismatch 422 is operationally invisible, and `bridge:check` is the right place to catch it once, before traffic (same rationale as DL-030). The runtime `Log::warning` stays.
- **Consequences:** `app/Bridge/Writeback/KanbanClient.php` (`boardCustomFieldKeys`), `app/Console/Commands/Bridge/CheckCommand.php` (the new per-mapping check), `app/Bridge/Handlers/KanbanDependabotCardHandler.php` (`CREATE_PAYLOAD_KEYS` constant), `docs/writeback.md`, tests (missing-field warns / all-present confirms / flag-off skips the probe). No behavior change to any delivery path — diagnostics only. No config, no migration. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 448/448.

## DL-163 — Generalize the writeback no-regression guard to all four PR-driven outcomes (#2935)

- **Date:** 2026-06-20
- **Context:** DL-160 added a no-regression guard ONLY to the new `started` outcome (`KanbanMoveCardHandler` promotes from `started_from_stages` only). The original four PR-move outcomes — `opened` / `merged` / `merged_to_main` / `closed_unmerged` — still moved the card **unconditionally** to their mapped stage with no check on the card's current stage. So any `pull_request` event carrying a card's `DL-NNN` could drag it **backward**: a **release PR title** contains the DL (e.g. "Release v0.38.0 … (DL-161)"), so opening/redelivering that PR's `opened` event fires opened→In-Review on a card already at Released; and GitHub **webhook redelivery** of an older `opened` re-applies it. Found live — cards #2650 (DL-160) and #2659 (DL-161) had drifted from Released-to-main back to In-Review this way, reconciled by hand.
- **Decision:** generalize the guard to the four PR outcomes using the board's **workflow-stage order** (positions) as the authority — the card's option (b), "most general," now that `GET /boards/{id}/preload.json` is confirmed to carry `workflows[].stages[]` with `position` cheaply (new `KanbanClient::boardStageOrder()`). For `opened` / `merged` / `merged_to_main` (forward outcomes): refuse any move whose target stage is **earlier** than the card's current stage. For `closed_unmerged` — the one **legitimately backward** outcome (an abandoned PR returns its In-Review card to In-Progress) — allow the regression **unless** the card has already reached a **terminal** stage (current position ≥ the earliest of the mapping's `merged` / `merged_to_main` targets), so a stale close can't resurrect a shipped/released card (the card's option (c) folded in for this outcome). A refused move logs `info` + no-ops, mirroring the `started` guard.
- **Fail-OPEN, not fail-closed (deliberate divergence from DL-160):** when the order can't be read (preload unavailable, or a stage isn't on the board) the move PROCEEDS as it did pre-guard. DL-160's `started` guard fails *closed* because an absent `started_from_stages` is a config CHOICE (the operator hasn't opted in). Here, an unreadable order is a transient/infra condition, not a config choice — failing closed would let a diagnostic safety-net **break** the primary writeback, which is worse than the rare regression it guards. The guard only ever blocks on a *definite* backward step.
- **Alternatives considered:** (a) per-outcome `*_from_stages` allowlists like `started_from_stages` — rejected: verbose operator config for every outcome when the board already encodes the order. (c) terminal-stages-sticky alone — folded into the `closed_unmerged` branch rather than used standalone, since the forward outcomes want strict monotonic-forward, not just terminal-stickiness. Blanket monotonic-forward for ALL outcomes — rejected: it would break the documented `closed_unmerged` In-Review→In-Progress move.
- **Consequences:** `app/Bridge/Writeback/KanbanClient.php` (`boardStageOrder`), `app/Bridge/Handlers/KanbanMoveCardHandler.php` (the guard + `isRegressiveMove`/`terminalFloor` helpers + class docblock), `docs/writeback.md`, tests (opened/merged regress-refused, opened forward-allowed, closed_unmerged returns-to-in-progress vs not-resurrecting-a-released-card, fail-open on unreadable order). **Behavior change** scoped to the four PR outcomes' move path: a move that would regress a card past its current stage is now refused (was applied). One extra lightweight preload GET per PR-move event. No config, no migration. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 451/451.

## DL-164 — `bridge:check` flags a half-configured `started` trigger + any mapped stage id not on the board (#2652)

- **Date:** 2026-06-20
- **Context:** The DL-160 branch-create `started` trigger is **fail-closed**: it fires only when a mapping sets BOTH `stages.started` AND `started_from_stages`. Setting exactly one leaves the trigger **silently inert** (the `stages.started`-only half is refused for lack of a promote-from set; the `started_from_stages`-only half has no `started` outcome to fire) — safe, but invisible, exactly the half-configured state an operator hits mid-setup. Separately, a typo in ANY mapped stage id (a `stages.*` value or a `started_from_stages` id) is the same silent-misconfig class as the DL-027 swimlane / DL-162 dependabot-CF gaps: a forward outcome 422s, or the `started`/no-regression guard never matches.
- **Decision:** two `bridge:check` checks. (1) **Config-only XOR (no board read):** in the orphaned-mapping loop, warn when exactly one of `stages.started` / `started_from_stages` is set — fires even on a tokenless/half-configured install (the card's primary "cheap fix"). (2) **Board stage-id validation:** in the per-mapping board probe, read the board's stage ids via `KanbanClient::boardStageOrder` (added DL-163 — the card noted this "deeper check" needed a board-stage read that didn't exist *then*; #2935 created it, so it's now cheap) and warn on any `stages.*` value or `started_from_stages` id not on the board. Both warn-never-fail (DL-026 posture); the second skips silently when the order can't be read (no false-warn).
- **Scope note (canon #7):** the board-stage-id check validates **all** the mapping's stage targets, not just `started` — a typo in `opened`/`merged`/etc. is the same shape and the read is the same one call, so closing the whole class costs nothing extra.
- **Consequences:** `app/Console/Commands/Bridge/CheckCommand.php` (the two checks), `docs/writeback.md`, tests (started-stage-only warns / started-from-only warns / both-set silent / unknown-stage-id warns). Diagnostics only — no delivery-path change, no config, no migration. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 458/458.
## DL-165 — `promote-released-cards` exits non-zero when it derives shipped refs but promotes 0 cards (#2446)

- **Date:** 2026-06-20
- **Context:** `release-promote-cards.yml` ran GREEN on the v0.32.0 release yet promoted **0 tracking cards** — cards 2444/2202 sat in shipped-to-dev, moved by hand. Root cause: the v0.32.0 release PR was **squash-merged** to main, collapsing its constituent PR commits (#119/#120/#121) into one commit whose subject carries only the release-line tokens. `promote-released-cards` derives shipped refs from `git log <prev-tag>..HEAD --no-merges` commit subjects, so the per-PR refs that would have matched the cards were lost. Two compounding gaps: (1) squash defeats PR-correlation (the "don't squash a release/sync PR" anti-pattern is documented in VERSIONING.md but not enforced), and (2) the script **exited 0 (green)** despite promoting nothing — the silent half.
- **Decision:** fix the **silent half** — when the script reaches the summary with a NON-EMPTY shipped-ref set (an empty set already exits "nothing to do") but promoted nothing (`0 moved AND 0 already-released`), it now exits **2** with a loud message naming both likely causes (squash-merged release PR → use a merge commit; or a release with no tracked cards) so the post-merge promote job goes RED and the operator verifies/promotes manually. The systemic-failure exit 1 (every move failed) is unchanged; an isolated card hiccup still never fails the release.
- **Why not auto-work-around the squash (reject the larger fix):** parsing the squash commit's full BODY (`%B`) to recover the bulleted per-PR refs would catch them but **risks over-matching** — a DL/PR merely *mentioned* in a commit body would move a card that wasn't actually released. Moving a card on a false match is worse than a loud failure. The **primary** mitigation is the discipline (merge-commit, not squash, for release/sync PRs — now actively followed: the v0.39.0 prep-PR was merge-committed); this exit-code change is the defense-in-depth that makes an accidental squash (or a genuinely cardless release) impossible to miss. Enforcing merge-method via GitHub settings is unavailable (branch-protection requires Pro for private repos; a repo-wide squash-disable would break the feature-PR squash workflow).
- **Shared script:** `bin/promote-released-cards` is byte-identical across bridge + kanban-board (DL-023/DL-143), so this hardening lands in both — the same incident class applies to either release.
- **Consequences:** `bin/promote-released-cards` (the exit-2 branch + header doc). Validated on the live board (canon #9): `--dls DL-99999 --dry-run` → 0 promoted → exit 2 + FAILED message; `--dls DL-163 --dry-run` → would-move card 2935 → exit 0. No app code, no migration. (Bash script — no PHPUnit harness; real-surface dry-run is the authoritative check.)

## DL-166 — dependabot card create is idempotent on the PR key: collapse a concurrent-delivery duplicate (#2982)

- **Date:** 2026-06-20
- **Context:** peer-integrator (Sola PM) report #2982 — the DL-024 dependabot writeback double-created a card for one PR (live: board-3 cards 2965 + 2968, identical payload, for `actions/checkout` PR #289), and on merge one advanced while the other orphaned in In-Review. Root cause is a **check-then-create TOCTOU race**, NOT a correlation miss: `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` correlates by `payload.pr_number` *then* creates, but those two steps aren't atomic across concurrent deliveries. Two events for the same PR (`opened` then `reopened`, or a fresh-`delivery_id` re-emit that the receiver's `UNIQUE(delivery_id)` gate doesn't catch) land in parallel PHP-FPM workers; both correlate empty, both create. The kanban side indexes `payload.pr_number → (github_pr, ref)` synchronously at the `TaskMutator` chokepoint (verified: `TaskExternalReferenceIndexer`), so correlation itself is sound — the window is purely create-vs-create.
- **Decision:** make the create **self-healing and idempotent on the (repo, PR) key** rather than add a local card registry (the bridge keeps kanban as the single source of truth — DL-009/019). New `collapseDuplicates()`: given the cards for one repo+PR, keep the **lowest id** (a deterministic survivor, so two racing workers converge on the same one and the same archive set — no flip-flop) and **archive the rest** (idempotent: an archived card drops out of correlation). Wired at two points: (1) **after create** — re-correlate by the PR key (the just-written card is now indexed, so a racer's card is visible too) and collapse when `>1`; (2) **on the move path** — collapse first, then move only the survivor, which **self-heals duplicates minted before this guard shipped** on the PR's next non-terminal event.
- **Cross-repo guard (load-bearing — pre-PR review finding):** `correlatePr` keys on the **bare PR number** — kanban's `github_pr` by-ref index is NOT repo-qualified (DL-029) — so on a board **shared across repos** (DL-027, lane-per-repo) a same-numbered PR in *another* repo correlates too. Those are DISTINCT cards, never duplicates: a naive collapse would **silently archive a live foreign-repo card** (strictly worse than the pre-existing move path, which only mis-*moved* it). So the handler **attributes each correlated card to its repo** — `cardsForRepo()` reads the `github.com/<owner>/<repo>/pull/` segment of the card's stored `pr_url` (no new payload field, so no board-custom-field migration — DL-162) — and filters to the **current repo** before *any* archive/move/collapse, across all three branches (closed_unmerged archive, move, create-recorrelate). A card whose repo can't be parsed is dropped (never archived on a guess). This also fixes the pre-existing cross-repo mis-*move* the old "move them all" code had.
- **Why not a durable local registry / atomic upsert (reject the larger fix):** a bridge-side `(board, github_pr, ref)` unique table inserted before create would *prevent* the duplicate outright, but it reintroduces the local card state the design deliberately avoids and duplicates an index kanban already owns. The race is rare (overlapping deliveries for one PR) and the impact is cosmetic (reporter-rated **Low** — a stale card in In-Review), so a self-healing collapse that stays stateless is correctly right-sized (canon #6). An idempotent create endpoint on the kanban side was also rejected as out-of-proportion to a low-frequency cosmetic race in the consumer.
- **Re-read failure handling:** the post-create re-correlate is inside the existing `try`, so a 5xx propagates → redelivery → the redelivery finds the card(s) on the move path and self-heals there; a 4xx logs permanent and the next PR event collapses it. The `closed_unmerged` branch (archives ALL matching — DL-161) is unchanged: on an unmerged close every duplicate is retired, no survivor needed.
- **Consequences:** `app/Bridge/Handlers/KanbanDependabotCardHandler.php` (`cardsForRepo`/`cardRepo`/`collapseDuplicates` + repo-filtering at all three branches; the move path now moves the repo's survivor only, not all correlated). Tests: create-collapses-a-racer, **cross-repo-same-PR-number-not-collapsed**, no-duplicate-archives-nothing, move-path-collapses-pre-existing. No new config, no migration, no change to what the receiver accepts/rejects. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 462/462.

## DL-167 — Source-aware correlation: pass the repo as the kanban `source` qualifier (ref mode)

- **Date:** 2026-06-20
- **Context:** kanban's by-ref correlation gained a `source` (repo) dimension (kanban DL-163, v0.21.0) — on a board aggregating multiple repos, a bare `(github_pr, 28)` / `(dl, 28)` ref collides across repos (live: AIMLA board-9 `by-ref?system=github_pr&ref=33` → 4 rows across platform/magento/moodle; Sola board-3 shares 296 PR numbers across 3 repos). The bridge papered over this client-side for the dependabot path (#2982: `KanbanDependabotCardHandler::cardsForRepo` re-attributes each correlated card by its `pr_url`); the **DL-tracked move path had no cross-repo guard at all**. AIMLA + Sola (both on `correlation=ref`, the default) are explicitly waiting to "pull the source-aware bridge update."
- **Decision (fix the primitive upstream — canon #2):** thread the **repo through correlation** as the kanban `source` qualifier. `KanbanClient::findCardsByRef` gains an optional `$source`; `correlatePr`/`correlateDl` gain an optional `?string $repo` and, in **`ref` mode**, pass `canonSource($repo)` (trim + lower-case, matching the kanban server's canonicalization) so the server returns only this repo's card(s). `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` passes the event's `$repo` to `correlatePr`; `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` passes it to `correlateDl` — so **both** the dependabot path and the DL move path are now repo-precise on a shared board. Omitted repo ⇒ no `source` key ⇒ the prior any-source behavior (back-compat: a pre-DL-163 kanban ignores the unknown query param; single-repo boards unaffected).
- **Scope — `ref` only, `cardsForRepo` KEPT (right-sized):** the source qualifier is applied **server-side in `ref` mode** (the default, and the only mode AIMLA/Sola run). `scan` mode (legacy fallback) does **not** filter by source — the dependabot path's existing `cardsForRepo` client-side guard still covers it, so `scan` is unregressed without replicating the kanban derivation in the bridge. `cardsForRepo` is therefore **retained**, not removed: in `ref` mode it's a redundant belt-and-suspenders confirm; in `scan` mode it's the actual guard. (Considered removing it as the "downstream patch the upstream fix obsoletes" — deferred: it still earns its keep for `scan`, and removing it would force a ~15-fake scan-mode test rewrite for a legacy path. Tracked as a possible later cleanup once `scan` is retired.)
- **Consequences:** `app/Bridge/Writeback/KanbanClient.php` (`findCardsByRef` `$source`, `correlatePr`/`correlateDl` `$repo` + `canonSource`); `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` + `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` pass the repo; `docs/writeback.md`; `tests/Feature/Writeback/KanbanClientTest.php` (ref passes canonical `source`; omits it when no repo). No config, no migration. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 305/305. Requires kanban **v0.21.0+** for the `source` param (degrades to any-source on an older kanban). Closes the cross-repo collision AIMLA + Sola reported.

## DL-168 — Triage-wake classifier: human-filed untriaged card_created → channel_push (#3010)

- **Date:** 2026-06-20
- **Context:** in the DL-driven board model a work item filed **directly on the board by a human** (operator/lead) is untriaged — no `DL-NNN`, no `triaged` tag — and needs the PM to triage it. Today the PM discovers these only at SessionStart (the untriaged-snapshot check), i.e. **session-cadence** — a card filed mid-session waits until the next session. Peer FR (AIMLA #3010): wake the triaging session in near-real-time. **Low priority — a latency nicety**; the SessionStart snapshot already covers discovery and is the durable backstop.
- **Decision:** a new opt-in built-in classifier `KanbanTriageClassifier` (extends `InboxOnlyClassifier`) that, for a `task.created` which is **human-filed** (actor is NOT a known agent) AND **untriaged** (no `triaged` tag, no `id:pr:*` tag, no `dl` external reference), pairs the `new_card` Intent with a `channel_push` to the serving (triage-owner) session — the same live-wake transport the bridge already uses. Other `task.created` (and all other events) stay inbox-only.
- **The filter runs at classify time with NO API call (the key payoff of DL-164):** the kanban `task.created` webhook now carries the scoped `card` snapshot (kanban DL-164 — `tags`, `external_references`, `card_type`, `workflow_stage_id`), so the classifier reads `triaged`/`id:pr:*`/`dl`-ref straight off the event. This is why the upstream kanban `card`-snapshot was built first: it lets the bridge filter without a `GET /tasks/{id}` per event and without a kanban read token in the PM agent (the two per-consumer workarounds — DL-164 rejected A/B — that this avoids). Against a pre-DL-164 kanban the `card` key is absent ⇒ reads as untriaged ⇒ the wake fires (an over-wake, never a miss; the SessionStart snapshot is the durable backstop).
- **No self-wake (each automated creator is suppressed by a *different* mechanism — `isKnownAgent` is NOT the catch-all):** the actor-is-known-agent check drops only cards filed by an agent **registered in this install's YAMLs**. The bridge's own card creations come from the dependabot-card path, which tags every card `triaged` at create (DL-024) → dropped by the untriaged filter (the bridge has no other card-CREATE path; writeback only *moves* existing cards). The dedicated writeback `identity_id` user's events are dropped **pre-classify** by the dispatcher's global-echo gate (`DispatchService`/`globalEchoIds`, active only when `identity_id` is configured) → they never reach this classifier. The poll adapter's auto-`triaged` backstops carry `triaged` → same untriaged filter. So the wake never loops regardless of which path created the card. **Recipient model:** opt-in via `classifier.class: App\Bridge\Classifiers\KanbanTriageClassifier` on the triage-owner agent + subscribe it to `task.created`; the push uses that agent's cfg-default channel — so the triage owner IS the recipient by configuration (no new `triage_channel` config key needed; other agents keep `InboxOnly` and never wake).
- **Consequences:** new `app/Bridge/Classifiers/KanbanTriageClassifier.php`; `tests/Unit/Classifiers/KanbanTriageClassifierTest.php` (human-untriaged wakes; agent/triaged/id:pr/dl-ref suppress; bare github_pr still wakes; missing-snapshot wakes; non-created inbox-only); `docs/customization.md` opt-in note. No config schema change, no migration. Requires kanban **v0.22.0+** for the `card` snapshot (degrades to over-wake on older). Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit. The SessionStart untriaged-snapshot remains the durable backstop — this path is additive, never the sole guarantee.

## DL-169 — `bridge:inbox` hook wiring: stress PreToolUse as the only mid-session recovery trigger; recommend `matcher: ""` (docs only)

- **Date:** 2026-06-27
- **Context:** a peer integrator (Sola PM) reported addressed comments "silently lost" — events stamped `delivered` that the recipient never surfaced. Diagnostics (read-only, on their install) traced it to **consume-side hook wiring, not bridge code**: `bridge:inbox --agent pm` was wired on **`SessionStart` only**, with **no `PreToolUse`**. The live `channel_push` is best-effort by design (DL-001) and the durable inbox is the recovery road — but the inbox only surfaces when a hook fires `bridge:inbox`, and `SessionStart` fires once per session, so a long-lived session that never restarts never re-checks the inbox. Tell-tale: an `inbox-seen-<agent>.json` cursor stale for days while the inbox holds unseen intents. This is the second peer to hit a wiring-completeness gap (DL-072 covered the silent-surfacing envelope; this covers the missing mid-session trigger). The shipped `examples/claude-code/settings.json.example` *did* include `PreToolUse`, but with `matcher: "Bash"` (fires only before Bash tools — a long non-Bash stretch reopens the same gap) and without stressing that the leg is **required**, so a reader could (and did) omit it.
- **Decision (docs/example only — no code, no behavior change):** make the two-leg requirement explicit everywhere the wiring is documented. (1) `docs/consumer-guide.md` § Wiring: a "both legs are load-bearing" callout — `SessionStart` = boundary recovery, **`PreToolUse` = the recommended per-tool-call mid-session trigger** (`PostToolUse` equivalent; `UserPromptSubmit` misses a long autonomous tool-turn), `SessionStart`-only is the most common misconfiguration; recommend **`matcher: ""`** (all tools) over `"Bash"`, with the subprocess-per-tool tradeoff stated (idempotent + silent-when-empty per DL-072, so cheap-when-quiet). (2) A troubleshooting entry keyed on the observable symptom (missed events in a long session / stale seen-cursor) pointing at the fix. (3) `examples/claude-code/settings.json.example`: `PreToolUse` matcher `"Bash"`→`""` + a `_wiring_note`. **Also fixed a pre-existing doc bug** in the same section: a line claimed wiring on `Stop` *advances* the cursor — the opposite of the code (`Stop` ∉ `ADDITIONAL_CONTEXT_EVENTS` ⇒ `$reachesConsumer=false` ⇒ no advance, per `InboxCommand::handle`) and of the correct statement earlier in the same doc. A doc that wrongly says `Stop` advances would actively mislead anyone debugging the stale-cursor symptom.
- **Not done (deliberately, per the integrator's own agreement):** no ack/retry on the live push (re-litigates DL-001/DL-154 best-effort-push + durable-inbox design; MCP `notifications/*` are one-way so a true session-consumed ack isn't sourceable at that layer anyway); no `delivered`→`pushed` outcome-vocabulary split (a genuine `bridge:replay`-honesty win but off the critical path — the inbox road already recovers these once wired). A possible future code-level safety net — `bridge:check` warning when an agent's hooks have `SessionStart` but no mid-session trigger — is noted but not built (it can't see the consumer's `~/.claude/settings.json` from the bridge install; left as a docs fix).
- **Consequences:** `docs/consumer-guide.md`, `examples/claude-code/settings.json.example`. No app code, classifier, schema, migration, or `.env`. No behavior change — existing correctly-wired consumers are unaffected; the fix is guidance for the next integrator.

## DL-170 — PM consumption standard: MCP channel + upstream-truth reconcile is the recommended model; `bridge:inbox` is the fallback (docs only)

- **Date:** 2026-06-27
- **Context:** DL-169 hardened `bridge:inbox`, but the deeper question — *what is the **best** way for a PM agent to consume bridge events?* — surfaced when AIMLA PM documented its model and it differed from Sola's. AIMLA: **MCP channel live-push** (`notifications/claude/channel`) + **reconcile from the source of truth** (GitHub `to:pm` via `gh`, kanban via API) at SessionStart, inbox unused by design. Sola: MCP channel + **`bridge:inbox`** recovery (the DL-169 path). The operator asked which is best (event-based, fastest) and to standardize all PMs on it.
- **Decision (the standard):** **MCP channel push for the live wake + reconcile-from-upstream-truth for recovery; the bridge inbox is the *fallback*, not the PM path.** Reasoning, argued on mechanism: (a) the MCP channel is the only genuinely *event-based* path (bridge pushes the instant it processes the webhook); `bridge:inbox` is a *poll* at hook cadence, so it can't be "fastest/event-based." (b) Reconcile-from-truth beats inbox-replay as the backstop — idempotent, drift-proof, recovers *what's actually open now* rather than replaying a notification log — and is **redundant** for an agent whose every event is an upstream artifact. (c) Recovery runs in **two modes**: SessionStart = **full-dump** reconcile; mid-session = **light *delta*** reconcile (only new-since-watermark, silent-when-empty, throttled ~3–10 min, **sub-second** — NOT the full reconciler inline, which is ~40s on a real install and would stall the tool call).
- **Validated by two independent implementations.** After relaying changeover guides, **both** PMs converged: both confirmed their **entire** event set is upstream-reconcilable with **zero bridge-only intents** (Sola: 7 intent kinds, all GitHub/kanban; AIMLA: exactly 5 emitted kinds — `coord_issue`/`coord_comment` → GitHub, `new_card`/`column_move`/`content_edit` → kanban), so the inbox is genuinely redundant for them; both independently built the **same** SessionStart-full + mid-session-delta-throttled reconcile (Sola 180s, AIMLA 600s); and both disclosed the **same** bounded gap (mid-session delta is GitHub-coord-only; kanban cards recover at SessionStart — low-risk low-frequency board-state, with the kanban triage-wake classifier already pushing the high-value ones live). This is why the standard is canonized as confirmed rather than hedged.
- **Corrected a flaw in my own interim guidance:** I first told AIMLA to "run the *same* reconcilers mid-session, throttled" — wrong for a **full-dump** reconciler (re-injecting the full open list every N min is noise / violates silent-when-empty). The correct rule is a **delta** mid-session reconciler. Both PMs caught/built this independently.
- **Open follow-up (consumer-side, NOT this repo) — the convergence ask (AIMLA "FR #1"):** upstream the **delta mid-session reconcile, covering GitHub *and* kanban, with an event-aware surface envelope**, into the **shared coord-plugin framework** so every agent runs the identical thing instead of per-agent scripts (the framework currently ships SessionStart/full-dump only). This is the durable fix for the bounded kanban-mid-session gap. Tracked for the operator/framework maintainer; the bridge repo only documents the pattern.
- **Relationship to DL-169:** DL-169 stays valid — it hardens the **fallback** (`bridge:inbox`) path for consumers that need it (bridge-only intents, non-GitHub-anchored, cross-language). DL-170 sets the **primary** recommendation for upstream-anchored PM agents above it.
- **Consequences:** `docs/consumer-guide.md` § Consumption patterns (new "Recommended model for live agents" callout; `bridge:inbox` relabeled the fallback; the A/B/C pick-guidance re-aimed). No app code, classifier, schema, migration, or `.env`. No behavior change.

## DL-171 — Optional `writeback.alert_channel`: a loud per-event signal on a permanent move-failure (FR-4)

- **Date:** 2026-06-28
- **Context:** a permanent writeback move-failure (refused/un-actionable move — bad payload, a kanban 4xx, the belongs-to-mapped-board refusal) is **logged + no-op** (DL-020): a durable record, but no *live* signal. An operator watching for a real misconfiguration (a rotated/blind token surfacing as `getcard_4xx`, a drifted board_id surfacing as `card_not_on_mapped_board`) had to be tailing logs to notice. FR-4 asks for an opt-in loud signal *in addition to* the log — log = durable record, push = live wake.
- **Decision:** an optional top-level **`alert_channel`** in `writeback.json` (`{"socket": "/abs"}` XOR `{"url": "http://127.0.0.1:PORT/", "auth": {"token_path": "/abs"}}`, mirroring the agent `channel` shape). When set, the 5 **`Log::warning` permanent branches** of `KanbanMoveCardHandler` *also* push a one-line `{"type":"writeback_move_failed", repo, outcome, card_id, reason}` to it. Absent ⇒ null ⇒ log-only (unchanged). No timer/poll/watchdog/standing-listener — the signal is emitted **inline, event-driven**, on the failing delivery only, reusing the existing channel-push transport.
- **Loud/quiet line = the existing warning-vs-info split:** the 5 `Log::warning` branches signal (`card_id_not_int`, `repo_or_outcome_invalid`, `writeback_not_configured`, `getcard_4xx`, `card_not_on_mapped_board`); the 2 `Log::info` "not tracked" branches (no mapping for repo / no stage for outcome) and the fail-open no-regression-guard `Log::warning` stay **quiet**. The info branches are the *normal* case for an unmapped event, not a failure — signalling them would be noise.
- **Branch-#3 degrades to log-only (by construction):** the `writeback_not_configured` branch fires precisely when there is no `writeback.json`, so the notifier — which loads `alert_channel` from that same file — has nothing to load and no-ops. Documented in `docs/writeback.md`; the call is kept for symmetry. (Place a `writeback.json` to arm the other branches.)
- **Dedup via an atomic `O_EXCL` marker:** one alert per `sha1(repo \x00 outcome \x00 reason)` — a marker file created with `fopen($path, 'x')` under `<state_dir>/writeback-alerts/`. First create wins → push; a pre-existing marker → skip (already alerted); a create failure for ANY OTHER reason (FS error) → skip + warn rather than risk a per-event storm. Only the **push** is gated — the caller's `Log::warning` always runs.
- **Best-effort, never breaks the move (structural):** the ENTIRE notify body — config load, dedup claim, and push — is wrapped in one `try/catch (\Throwable)`, so "never throws out of the handler" is structural, not dependent on every internal call being individually warning-safe. (Pre-PR review caught a real escape: `claimSignature` calls `mkdir` for the marker dir, and an unwritable state dir makes `mkdir` emit `E_WARNING` → Laravel's error handler rethrows it as `ErrorException` → it propagated out of the handler → 5xx storm — the exact failure FR-4 forbids. The outer catch + a suppressed `@mkdir` close it.) Short timeouts (1s connect / 2s) like `ChannelPushHandler`.
- **A failed push RELEASES the dedup marker (review fix):** claim-before-push is the dedup primitive, but never-releasing it meant one dropped first packet (channel down — highly correlated with the very trouble these alerts surface) would silence that signature FOREVER. So on a caught push failure the marker is `@unlink`ed → a later redelivery re-attempts. A concurrent racer could then double-alert; an extra alert is strictly better than a forever-suppressed one. A SUCCESSFUL push keeps the marker (the once-per-signature dedup the FR asked for).
- **A SEPARATE notifier — `ChannelPushHandler` deliberately NOT modified.** `WritebackAlertNotifier` does its OWN validated send (operator-config socket: `SocketPath::isValid` + exists + not-a-symlink + is-a-socket; localhost url: http-only loopback, no userinfo; optional `ChannelToken::read` Bearer). `ChannelPushHandler` is a security-critical surface (classifier-supplied sockets, the `allowed_socket_dir` gate); a shared extract is the clean fix but would mean touching that handler, so the socket/url validation is **intentionally duplicated** (one-line comment + this DL). The alert socket is operator-config, so it is exempt from the classifier `allowed_socket_dir` gate (same exemption the agent's own `channel.socket` gets).
- **Config is NOT fail-closed on a malformed `alert_channel`** (deliberate divergence from the mappings, which fail closed): a bad alert_channel (both/neither socket+url) is an *opt-in diagnostic* — failing the whole config closed would take every card move dark for it. `WritebackConfig::load` parses it leniently into an `AlertChannel` value object; `bridge:check` **warns** (both/neither, missing socket parent dir, non-loopback url); at runtime the notifier rejects the bad channel and the caught push failure is logged. The writeback move is unaffected.
- **Consequences:** new `app/Bridge/Writeback/AlertChannel.php` + `WritebackAlertNotifier.php`; `WritebackConfig` (`alertChannel` field + lenient `parseAlertChannel`); `KanbanMoveCardHandler` (constructor injects the notifier — default-instantiated so existing `new KanbanMoveCardHandler` call sites are unchanged — + 5 additive `notify()` calls; **control flow on the non-failure paths is byte-identical**); `CheckCommand::checkAlertChannel`; `docs/writeback.md` + `docs/config-schema.md`. Tests: alert-on-a-warning-branch (+ log still fires), non-scalar-repo-at-branch-#1-doesn't-throw, unset⇒no-push, info-branch⇒no-push, dedup-fires-once, push-failure-doesn't-throw, failed-push-releases-marker-for-retry, config parse (socket/url+token/malformed-doesn't-fail-closed), bridge:check warns on malformed/non-localhost. No migration, no new `.env`, no change to what the receiver accepts/rejects. Pint clean · PHPStan L7 0 · PHPUnit 486/486.

## DL-172 — `promote-released-cards`: make the "0 promoted" exit CAUSE-AWARE (squash vs. cardless) — correction to DL-165

- **Date:** 2026-06-28
- **Correction to DL-165** (which stays frozen): DL-165 made the script exit 2 on ANY "0 cards promoted despite a non-empty shipped-ref set," to catch the v0.32.0 silent-green (a squash-merged release dropped the per-PR refs, leaving cards unpromoted while the job passed). That guard could not tell the squash case from a **legitimately cardless** release (a docs-only DL, or a DL tracked elsewhere), so it failed loud on both — surfaced when v0.43.0 (DL-171 shipped uncarded) reddened the promote check.
- **Decision:** distinguish the two ROOT CAUSES by whether ref-derivation was COMPLETE, via the **parent count of the release tip**. A MERGE commit (>=2 parents) — or explicit `--dls` — means the range carried every feature/prep commit subject, so derivation was complete and "0 newly promoted" means the DLs are genuinely cardless → **WARN, exit 0**. A non-merge tip (the release PR was squash/rebase-merged) may have collapsed the per-PR subjects this reads → **FAIL, exit 2** (the v0.32.0 class). New helper `merge_commit_tip` (`git rev-list --parents -n1`).
