**Decision:** three opt-in per-mapping keys, all absent ⇒ v0.52.0 byte-identical. **`unpark_from_stages`** (list<int>, strict-parsed like `started_from_stages`): from these stages a `started` event promotes the card **even if pinned** (the DL-178 reversal, scoped to these stages only) — it **must be disjoint from `started_from_stages`** (a stage can't be both refuse-if-pinned and move-if-pinned; overlap ⇒ `ConfigException`, fail-closed). The handler's `started` block gates DL-178 refuse on `PinGuard::isPinned($card) && !$isUnpark` (unchanged everywhere outside the unpark set), and the promote-from set becomes `startedFromStages ∪ unparkFromStages` (both null→[]; both absent ⇒ [] ⇒ refuse, DL-160 fail-closed preserved). After a **confirmed** move (never on a 4xx no-op) and **before** the correlation-ref stamp, a `shouldAlertUnpark(card, mapping): ?string` predicate returns the hold-signal discriminator (`no_automove` / `block_reason` / `hold_tag` / `failsafe`, or null) that BOTH gates the alert AND labels a durable `Log::warning` (one computation, no drift) — the alert floor is "we actually overrode a *deliberate* hold": a real PinGuard pin (`no-automove` / human `block_reason` ≠ the draft sentinel) or a configured hold tag ALWAYS alerts; a benign automated draft-park (`block_reason` == the sentinel, no other signal) never alerts; with **no `hold_marker_tags`** declared a **fail-safe** alerts on every non-benign unpark. **`hold_marker_tags`** (list<string>, default `[]`) only *widens* the alert to an install's own hold convention (e.g. aimla's `gate`) — it can never narrow/suppress the alert for a PinGuard-pinned card. **`draft_block_reason`** (non-empty string, default `KanbanBlockReasonHandler::MARKER` = `'PR is in draft'`, strict-parsed) names the benign DL-193 draft sentinel. The alert rides the existing `alert_channel` as a **distinct `type: writeback_auto_unparked`** with **NO dedup** (a re-park→re-unpark is a distinct human cycle worth re-surfacing); redelivery is bounded to one alert per successful unpark by the handler's idempotent already-in-stage short-circuit (a partial-failure redelivery short-circuits *before* the alert line), not a persistent marker. `WritebackAlertNotifier` grew a shared private `emit(type, ?dedupKey, body)` (null dedupKey ⇒ skip claim / always push); `notify()` routes through it byte-identically (the raw `(repo,outcome,reason)` tuple is handed to `claimSignature`, which hashes exactly once), and the catch push-failure log draws from `$body` keys (present on both paths). `PinGuard` gained boundary-safe `blockReason(): ?string` (is_string-guarded, untrimmed) + `tags(): array` (is_array-guarded) accessors, extracted behavior-identical from `isPinned` (which now reroutes through them) and reused by `shouldAlertUnpark` — a bare `trim($nonString)`/`in_array(_, $nonArray)` on the boundary card would be a PHP 8.5 TypeError between the move and the stamp.

**Alternatives considered:** (a) **cardid-only dedup on the unpark alert** (a false analogy to the FR-4 failure dedup) — REJECTED: it collapses distinct human re-park cycles into "alert once per card ever"; the handler's idempotent short-circuit already bounds redelivery to one per successful unpark without a marker. (b) **`hold_marker_tags` *suppressing* an alert for a genuinely-pinned card** (round-1 BLOCKER, fixed here) — REJECTED: a real PinGuard pin must alert regardless; a marker only widens the set. (c) **`if isPinned → alert`** as a shortcut — REJECTED: the DL-193 draft sentinel is a non-empty `block_reason` and thus *pins*, so that would alert on every benign draft-park; the benign-draft discriminator is load-bearing. (d) **placing the alert after the stamp** — REJECTED: `stampCorrelationRefs` can 5xx-throw, so a pre-stamp throw + every redelivery short-circuiting would make the unpark permanently silent; between move and stamp is the only correct spot. (e) **importing an install-specific `block_reason` sentinel onto the reference** (rev-1's premise that `block_reason` is baseline-stamped, verified false: `KanbanBlockReasonHandler` writes the known constant add-if-missing, DL-193) — REJECTED: cross-install sentinels are handled by `draft_block_reason`.

**Load-bearing safety (verified in code + test):** (1) **default byte-identical** — all three keys absent ⇒ `unparkFromStages` null → `$isUnpark` always false → DL-178 refuse + promote-from set unchanged; no alert path reached. (2) **DL-178 preserved off the unpark set** — a pinned card in a `started_from_stages`-only stage still refuses `pinned_no_automove` (`test_started_pinned_card_in_a_started_from_stage_still_refused_dl178`). (3) **disjoint invariant fail-closed** at load (`test_unpark_overlapping_started_from_stages_throws`), surfaced by `bridge:check`. (4) **alert only after a confirmed move** — a 4xx move no-op emits no unpark alert (`test_unpark_alert_not_sent_when_the_move_4xx_noops`). (5) **durable-first** — the `Log::warning` fires with no `alert_channel` and when the push 500s (two tests). (6) **no-dedup / short-circuit bound** — a re-park re-alerts, a redelivery-while-in-progress does not (two tests). (7) all 8 semantics-table rows have a dedicated test; `PinGuardTest` stays green (behavior-identical accessor extraction). 702/702 phpunit (+30), phpstan L7 0, pint clean.

**Consequences:** `PinGuard` (extract `blockReason`/`tags`, reroute `isPinned`), `WritebackMapping`/`WritebackConfig` (parse the three keys + disjoint guard), `KanbanMoveCardHandler` (unpark-scoped DL-178 reversal + promote-from union + post-move alert + `shouldAlertUnpark`), `WritebackAlertNotifier` (`emit`/`notifyUnpark`, hash-once split of `claimSignature`), `CheckCommand` (unpark ids in the stage-on-board warn; the disjoint invariant surfaces via `load()`), `docs/writeback.md` + `docs/config-schema.md`. **No migration, no new `.env`, no change to what the receiver accepts/rejects, no token-scope change.** Fully opt-in; the DL-178 reversal only reaches a board once an operator adds `unpark_from_stages`, and prod release stays operator-gated. Roundtable #19 converged three-seat; card #4172.

## DL-195 — Won't-Do-revival (opt-in `revive_on_reopen`): a reopened PR revives its parked card from the abandon stage back to In-Review

**Date:** 2026-07-14
**Context:** An operator may map `closed_unmerged → <a "Won't Do" terminal stage>` (documented option, CHANGELOG #167) so an abandoned PR parks its card there. When that PR is **reopened**, GitHub fires `pull_request.reopened`, which `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier::outcome()` collapses to the `opened` outcome → target the In-Review stage → but the **DL-163 no-regression guard refuses the backward Won't-Do → In-Review move**, so the card **strands in Won't-Do while its PR is alive again**. Roundtable #19 sibling of the auto-unpark (DL-194); operator-APPROVED build 2026-07-14. The design deliberately mirrors DL-194 (reverse a specific guard for a specific opt-in transition + a compensating override alert) so the code shape + risk are already proven. Card #4189.

**Decision:** one opt-in per-mapping bool **`revive_on_reopen`** (default false, parsed like `draft_overlay`/`create_dependabot_cards`), absent ⇒ v0.52.0 byte-identical. When on, the classifier emits a **distinct `reopened` move-outcome** — computed in `classify()` **after the dependabot branch** and after `$mapping` is resolved (`$moveOutcome = ($eventType === 'pull_request.reopened' && $mapping->reviveOnReopen) ? 'reopened' : $outcome`), used only in the two non-dependabot move-target emissions. `outcome()` itself is **untouched** (see alternative (a) — a silent dependabot regression). The handler resolves a `reopened` outcome's stage via **`stageFor('opened')`** (reuse; there is no `stages.reopened` key, and `reopened` is deliberately NOT added to `WritebackConfig::OUTCOMES`, which validates config stage keys). Revival fires **only** when the card's current stage equals the mapped **`closed_unmerged`** (abandon) stage (`$isRevive = $outcome === 'reopened' && is_int($current) && $current === $mapping->stageFor('closed_unmerged')`). `isRegressiveMove` gains a `reopened` branch: allow the backward move **only** from the abandon stage; anywhere else it is forward-only, identical to `opened`. After a **confirmed** revival move and **before** the correlation-ref stamp, a `writeback_revived_on_reopen` alert (a new `WritebackAlertNotifier::notifyRevive`, no dedup) fires gated by the **same** `shouldAlertUnpark(card, mapping)` predicate as DL-194 (`no_automove`/`block_reason`/`hold_tag`/`failsafe`, or null) — a genuinely-held card always alerts, a bare-stage park alerts via the fail-safe unless `hold_marker_tags` is declared. `bridge:check` warns (config-only, never fails) when `revive_on_reopen` is on but `stages.opened` or `stages.closed_unmerged` is missing.

**Alternatives considered:** (a) **remap `reopened` inside `outcome()`** (the design's first draft; design-review SHOULD-FIX 1+2) — REJECTED: `$outcome` from `outcome()` flows into the **dependabot branch** (`kanban_dependabot_card` payload), so a reopened dependabot PR would carry `outcome:'reopened'` → `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` `stageFor('reopened')===null` → card neither moved nor created (a silent regression vs today's move/create at the opened stage); and `$mapping` isn't in scope at the `outcome()` call site. Remapping only in the non-dependabot move-target section fixes both — and is semantically correct: dependabot cards **archive** on close (DL-161), never park in `closed_unmerged`, so revival never applies to them. (b) **respect the pin (refuse + alert)** — REJECTED by the operator in favor of override+alert, symmetric with DL-194 (a reopen is a "work resumed" signal). (c) **a separate `revive_to_stage` config key** — REJECTED: a reopened PR is open-not-merged, so reusing `stages.opened` is the consistent target with the smallest surface (DRY). (d) **`bridge:reconcile` back-stops a missed revival** (design-review SHOULD-FIX 3) — REJECTED, deliberate scope: the reconciler sees only static state (PR open, card in Won't-Do) with no reopen signal, so it can't distinguish an automated `closed_unmerged` park from a deliberate human abandon of a still-open PR; only the live `reopened` event carries "work resumed". A missed reopen needs a manual operator revive (documented in `docs/writeback.md`).

**Load-bearing safety (verified in code + test):** (1) **default byte-identical** — `revive_on_reopen` absent ⇒ the classifier emits `opened` for a reopened action and the handler never sees a `reopened` outcome (`test_reopened_stays_opened_outcome_when_revive_off`). (2) **dependabot stays `opened`** even with both opt-ins on (`test_reopened_dependabot_pr_stays_opened_never_reopened`) — the SHOULD-FIX 1 guard. (3) **terminal-safe** — a card at Shipped/Released is never in the abandon stage, so a stale reopen is refused (`test_reopened_does_not_revive_a_terminal_card`); GitHub can't reopen a merged PR either. (4) **non-revival reopen is forward-only** like `opened`, no alert (`test_reopened_on_a_non_abandoned_card_is_forward_only_like_opened` + `test_reopened_forward_move_does_not_alert`). (5) **redelivery-safe** — a redelivered reopen after revival hits the idempotent already-in-stage short-circuit before the guard and alert (`test_reopened_redelivery_after_revival_no_double_move`). (6) **pin override + gated alert** — a pinned card is revived and alerts; the alert quiets when `hold_marker_tags` is declared and absent from the card (three alert tests + the `is_int($current)` NIT-1 guard on the predicate). 716/716 phpunit (+14), phpstan L7 0, pint clean; fresh-adversarial design-review folded (no BLOCKER; 3 SHOULD-FIX + 2 NIT resolved).

**Consequences:** `WritebackMapping`/`WritebackConfig` (parse `revive_on_reopen`), `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` (`$moveOutcome` remap in the move-target sections, `outcome()` untouched), `KanbanMoveCardHandler` (`reopened` stage-reuse + `$isRevive` + `isRegressiveMove` carve-out + post-move `notifyRevive`), `WritebackAlertNotifier` (`notifyRevive`), `CheckCommand` (config-only revive-inert warn), `docs/writeback.md` + `docs/config-schema.md`. **No migration, no new `.env`, no change to what the receiver accepts/rejects, no token-scope change.** Fully opt-in; revival only reaches a board once an operator sets `revive_on_reopen`, and prod release stays operator-gated. Roundtable #19 sibling; card #4189.

## DL-196 — `bridge:check` event-follows-consumer: WARN when a received GitHub event type has no enabled classifier consuming it (diagnostics only)

**Date:** 2026-07-14
**Context:** A bridge install can subscribe a GitHub webhook to an event type (e.g. via a uniform multi-event filter) that **no enabled classifier consumes for that scope**. The event arrives, is classified to an empty result, and is **silently dropped** — the subscription reads as a capability that isn't there and re-drifts. Roundtable #6 follow-up (`bridge:check` enforceability FR), fleet-consumed by sola-pm (offered the hardening) + aimla-pm (committed adopter, fresh-adversarial gate). Structurally the **same shape** as the DL-030/#2162 orphaned-writeback-mapping check (CheckCommand): both ask "is there classifier code that activates this config artifact?" — here of a *subscribed/arriving event* instead of a *writeback mapping*. Design fully converged (roundtable #22), impl operator-gated. Card #4183.

**Decision:** a new **WARN-never-fail** `bridge:check` section. Per `github:<scope>`: `observed` = distinct **top-level** `event_type` from the bridge's own `webhook_events` table (provider github, that scope; normalized off any `.action` suffix — the adapter stores `pull_request.opened`, the top level is `pull_request`); `consumed` = the **union** of `consumedEventTypes($cfg)` across **every** enabled classifier of **every** agent whose subscription covers that scope; `unconsumed = observed − consumed` → one `warn` per event naming the scope + subscribed agent(s), suggesting "add a consuming family, or drop it from the subscription via `coord:setup-bridge`." A new interface **`App\Bridge\Contracts\DeclaresConsumedEvents { consumedEventTypes(ClassifierConfig $cfg): array }`** carries the declaration co-located with the consuming code (anti-drift): `CoordinationClassifier` returns the union over its **enabled** families derived from the SAME source of truth the classify pipeline uses (`HANDLED` for coord-message → issues/issue_comment/pull_request; `IMPL_CI_WAKE_EVENT_TYPES` for impl-ci-wake → push/workflow_run; kanban-triage is a kanban family → no github events); `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` returns `{pull_request, push}`. **Interface docblock is a HARD CONTRACT** — pure `$cfg`→map, no lazy class-loading / side effects.

**Data-source seam — CORRECTED from the card:** the card proposed reading the subscribed `events[]` from the **GitHub hooks API** (`GET /repos/{repo}/hooks`). Fresh-adversarial review killed this: that endpoint needs the repo-admin `Webhooks` permission, and the bridge **deliberately holds no such token** — its per-repo GitHub token is the DL-185 least-privilege read-only PAT. Reusing the reconcile token would 403 on every documented least-privilege install → the check would permanently no-op in the common case. **Corrected seam: the bridge's OWN inbound-event history** (`webhook_events`, already persisted; the source for `bridge:stats`/`bridge:replay`) — no new token, no new table, no external API (canon #5 reuse). It is also a **better signal**: the hooks API tells you what's *subscribed*; `webhook_events` tells you what has *actually arrived and been dropped* — exactly the actionable drift. Documented limitation: the observed set is bounded by `bridge:prune` retention (a long-quiet unconsumed event isn't flagged until it next fires — acceptable for a WARN; it self-heals on the next occurrence).

**DL-025 out-of-process safety:** `consumedEventTypes()` invokes classifier code, so it inherits the DL-025 hazard the sibling orphan check guards against (a stale custom classifier is an uncatchable `E_COMPILE_ERROR`). Posture (matched to the orphan check exactly): detect the interface via **out-of-process** `ClassifierResolver::probeImplements`; call `consumedEventTypes()` only on the instance `ClassifierResolver::for()` already resolved in-process **after** `probeLoadable` passed; wrap in `catch (\Throwable)` → treat the classifier as **undeclared** (contributes nothing). The residual hole (a custom impl lazy-loading an un-probed dependency that itself fatals) is closed by the interface's HARD-CONTRACT docblock, not an out-of-process value probe (more machinery than the pure-map reference shape warrants).

**Fail-direction (conservative — never a false "clean"):** an undeclared or load-failing classifier contributes nothing → its events land in `unconsumed` → at worst a false WARN (loud; operator investigates), never false silence. **Disambiguation (sola's #22):** when a scope has any enabled classifier NOT implementing `DeclaresConsumedEvents`, the check co-emits *"scope `<x>` has an enabled classifier `<name>` that does not declare its consumed events … the following WARNING(s) MAY be a false positive"* so a real orphan is distinguishable from a false positive. Empty `webhook_events` for a scope ⇒ `observed` empty ⇒ no warns (nothing dropped yet — not a false clean). The whole section is wrapped fail-soft so it can **never throw out of `bridge:check`** and emits only `warn`/`info`, never `error`.

**Alternatives considered:** (a) **GitHub hooks-API data source** — REJECTED (infeasible under the least-privilege token posture; see the seam correction). (b) **a static event→family registry** instead of the interface — REJECTED: a registry drifts from the code that actually consumes, the exact rot #4183 fights; co-locating the declaration with the consuming code is the anti-drift choice. (c) **an out-of-process value probe** for `consumedEventTypes()` — REJECTED: the documented HARD CONTRACT extends `probeLoadable`'s compile guarantee to cover the call, and the pure-map reference shape doesn't warrant the extra machinery. (d) **a separate writeback-events clause** — REJECTED (double-counting): `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` is already enumerated as a subscribed classifier and its `consumedEventTypes()` already contributes `{pull_request, push}`; a mapping-derived clause would also FALSELY mark `pull_request` consumed in the orphaned-mapping case. (e) **error/fail on an unconsumed event** — REJECTED: over-subscription is a hygiene smell, not a broken install; consistent with every advisory in `bridge:check`.

**Consequences:** new `app/Bridge/Contracts/DeclaresConsumedEvents.php`; `CoordinationClassifier` (`implements` + `consumedEventTypes` + `IMPL_CI_WAKE_EVENT_TYPES`/`coordMessageEventTypes` derived from `HANDLED`; `KanbanTriageClassifier` shim inherits it → no github events); `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` (`implements` + `consumedEventTypes`); `CheckCommand` (per-agent per-scope consumed collection in the config loop + `checkEventFollowsConsumer` after it); `docs/customization.md`. **No migration, no new `.env`, no change to what the receiver accepts/rejects, no token-scope change, no runtime/dispatch behavior change** — diagnostics only, and only `bridge:check` output changes. 726/726 phpunit (+11), phpstan L7 0, pint clean. Roundtable #6/#22; card #4183.

## DL-197 — `impl-ci-wake` optional CI-failure workflow-NAME filter (`ci_failure_workflow_patterns`): narrow WHICH workflows wake, never WHICH conclusions

**Date:** 2026-07-14
**Context:** The `impl-ci-wake` family's `workflow_run` gate is deliberately fail-LOUD (DL-190): a completed run wakes the PM on ANY non-benign conclusion, so a new/unknown GitHub conclusion is never silently dropped. But a coordination/impl repo runs MANY workflows, and only some are correctness gates. A PM watching a coord repo (roundtable #24) runs `Protocol integrity` (the post-validator) alongside `Retention sweep` (repo maintenance) + `Protocol integrity tests` (CI-of-the-CI) + `Verify citations`/`Verify schemas` — a `Retention sweep` flake would wake the PM as if a post were malformed. Fleet-converged 3-way (roundtable #24): both sola + aimla set the filter to `Protocol integrity` (fleet-uniform; the `name:` value is already byte-identical across installs), substring (matches `Protocol integrity tests` too — both are oversight gates). Card #4232.

**Decision:** a new optional `classifier.config.ci_failure_workflow_patterns` (list<string>, read via the existing `ClassifierConfig::strings` generic accessor — no schema/contract change). Applied in `workflowRunSignal` **inside the non-benign (failure) branch, AFTER the fail-loud conclusion gate**: when the list is non-empty AND the run has a name AND the name matches none of the patterns → return null (the failure becomes a NON-wake run, dropped or inbox-staged per `impl_non_wake_disposition`, exactly like a benign run). Matching is **case-insensitive substring** via a new shared `nameMatchesAnyPattern($name, $patterns)` helper — extracted at the second real caller (canon #5) and also routed the pre-existing `provenance_patterns` success match through it (behavior-identical: `parseStringList` already lowercases + rejects empty, so the helper's output equals the prior inline loop for every valid config). **Empty/absent ⇒ any failing workflow wakes (byte-identical to v0.54.0).**

**Invariants (load-bearing):** the filter narrows **which workflows**, never **which conclusions** — the `benign_conclusions` fail-loud gate is untouched and is applied FIRST, so a *matched* workflow still wakes on any non-benign conclusion (incl. unknown/future ones). A `workflow_run` with **no `name`** is never filtered (can't be matched against the allow-list → wakes fail-loud, preserving the pre-filter behavior for a malformed payload — design-review finding #2). Orthogonal to the provenance/success path (the filter lives only in the failure branch).

**Fail-loud-inversion guardrail (design-review finding #1):** a set-but-non-matching filter — a typo (`protocol integrty`) or a workflow later renamed — silently blackholes EVERY CI-failure wake for the scope, with no trace under the default `drop`. Config validation cannot catch a well-formed-but-stale pattern, and a precise `bridge:check` drift-warn against observed workflow *names* is infeasible (names live in `webhook_events.payload`, which is nullable/pruned — DL-012; DL-196 reads the persisted event-TYPE column, not payload). Mitigation: (a) a **loud `config-schema.md` warning**, and (b) a **`bridge:check` WARN** whenever the key is set, printing the configured patterns for eyeball verification against real workflow names (warn-never-fail, in the existing per-agent classifier loop). 

**Alternatives considered:** (a) **an allow-list on conclusions** (which failure conclusions wake) — REJECTED: that re-introduces the fail-silent hole DL-190 killed (an unknown conclusion would be dropped). Narrowing by workflow NAME keeps every matched workflow fully fail-loud. (b) **filter the empty-name case too** — REJECTED (finding #2): an unclassifiable failure must wake. (c) **a precise bridge:check drift-warn** (filter matches none of the observed run names) — DEFERRED/infeasible (pruned payloads); the unconditional warn-when-set is the reliable substitute. (d) **default the filter to `[protocol integrity]`** — REJECTED for the code default (must stay empty=any for back-compat); the *PM-template* (`coord:init`) seeds it instead (framework-side, separate FR).

**Consequences:** `CoordinationClassifier` (`workflowRunSignal` failure-filter branch + `nameMatchesAnyPattern` helper + provenance routed through it; docblocks on `workflowRunSignal`/`workflowRunInboxSignal` updated — a name-filtered failure now reaches the inbox-stage path); `CheckCommand` (warn-when-set in the per-agent loop); `docs/config-schema.md` (new key row + fail-loud-inversion warning). **No migration, no new `.env`, no change to what the receiver accepts/rejects, no token-scope change; default-empty ⇒ byte-identical to v0.54.0.** Fresh-adversarial design-review pass before impl (found + folded the empty-name hole + the silent-blackout guardrail). Card #4232; roundtable #24.

## DL-198 — Real-time coordination issue → card (opt-in `create_coord_cards`): a `CoordinationClassifier` family creates the tracking card the moment a recognized-prefix issue opens

**Date:** 2026-07-14
**Context:** On a coordination repo, a `[BRIEF]`/`[ANNOUNCE]`/`[QUERY]`/`[REVIEW]`/`[TASK]` issue gets a tracking card only on the next periodic `reconcile_simple_board` pass — a session-cadence lag between "thread opened" and "card on the board." Roundtable #18(b): the bridge should be the **primary** mover (create in real time on `issues.opened/reopened`), with the periodic reconcile as the **backstop** (it adopts the bridge-created card by its `id:<sid>` tag and registers it, so the bridge stays **registry-free** — no bridge↔registry coupling). Same primary/backstop partition as the shipped PR-lifecycle writeback; contract locked byte-identical across both consumers (#18/#23, both signed off). Card #4215.

**Decision:** a config-gated **`coord-card-create` FAMILY on `CoordinationClassifier`** (fresh-adversarial design-review R1: NOT a standalone classifier — DL-190 unified classifiers into config-gated families so no install forks the bridge, and a standalone would force a 2nd agent + a double `issues` subscription on the same repo). The family: provider `github`, acts on `issues.opened`/`issues.reopened` only, runs **independently of the coord-message recipient gate** (it cards EVERY recognized-prefix issue on the repo — board-level, not addressed-to-me); its own gate is prefix-recognized AND the repo's `writeback.json` mapping has `create_coord_cards`. It emits ONE `kanban_coord_card` `ReactionTarget` (payload `{repo, issue_number, sid, itype, title, issue_url}`), **no intent, no wake**. `CoordinationClassifier` now `implements EmitsWritebackReactions` so `bridge:check`'s orphaned-mapping guard treats a coord mapping as served (accepted looseness: the marker is class-level, so a `CoordinationClassifier` agent WITHOUT the family also marks a coord mapping non-orphaned — a coarse warn). `consumedEventTypes()` contributes `['issues']` for the family (single-sourced), so DL-196's event-follows-consumer check is correct. `coord-card-create` is **not** a default family (opt-in via `classifier.config.families`).

**The LOCKED contract (byte-exact):** adoption key = the kanban card **TAG `id:<sid>`**, `sid = stableId(title, num)` — anchored, case-insensitive `^\[(BRIEF|ANNOUNCE|QUERY|REVIEW|TASK)\]` on `trim($title)`, emitting `strtoupper(prefix)."-".num` (un-padded); un-prefixed / `[PROPOSAL]` / unrecognized → null → **not carded** (the create-set equals the reconcile's own-prefix set, so a carded issue is always one the periodic pass backstops). **NO trailing boundary** (design-review R2, corrected from the reviewer's assumption): the real reconcile Python is `re.match(r"\[(BRIEF|…|TASK)\]", title.strip(), re.I)`, so `[QUERY]x` DOES match → `QUERY-<num>`; a `(?=\s|$)` guard would make PHP MORE restrictive and orphan a card the reconcile creates. `itype` mirrors the reconcile's `_itype` — an **UNANCHORED**, priority-ordered substring scan (`[BRIEF]` > `[ANNOUNCE]` > `[QUERY]` > `[REVIEW]`, else `task`), deliberately distinct from the ANCHORED `sid` first-prefix (they diverge on a multi-bracket title, e.g. `[REVIEW] of [BRIEF]` → `sid REVIEW-N` / `type:brief` — matching the reconcile's own divergence so the `type:`/`priority` don't churn; the adoption key stays exact either way). Tags at create = `["id:<sid>", "type:<itype>"]` ONLY — `repo:` OMITTED (non-critical; the reconcile folds it). `createCard` also sets churn-avoidance fields mirroring the reconcile's `build_create`: `name` = title verbatim, `description = "Coordination thread <repo>#<num>"`, `priority` = 1 for `brief` else 0, `external_link = https://github.com/<repo>/issues/<num>`. `external_id` is deliberately NOT set — `build_create` omits it, and kanban's `(board_id, external_id)` uniqueness would 422 a colliding issue number on a multi-repo coord board (`external_link` carries the correlation).

**Handler (`KanbanCoordCardHandler`, `kanban_coord_card`) — CREATE-ONLY, registry-free, durable:** the reconcile owns column/lifecycle; the bridge never moves/archives a coord card. Idempotency = **correlate-before-create by the `id:` tag** (`KanbanClient::cardsByTag`, new): non-empty ⇒ a card exists (redelivery, opened+reopened, OR the reconcile already carded it — both movers key on the SAME tag → the anti-thrash guarantee) → skip. Else `createCard` at `coord_card_stage_id`; post-create re-read by tag + collapse a raced duplicate via the shared **`CardCollapse`** primitive (design-review R3: extracted the `ksort → keep lowest id → archive rest` kernel from `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` so the two create movers can never drift on which card wins — each keeps its own correlation, only the tie-break is single-sourced). Transient(5xx→retry)/permanent(4xx→log+no-op), same posture as the dependabot create handler.

**Config (fail-closed):** `create_coord_cards` (bool, default false — parsed exactly like `create_dependabot_cards`, so absent-config is byte-identical) + `coord_card_stage_id` (int, strict-numeric like `swimlane_id`, **REQUIRED-and-throws-at-load when `create_coord_cards` is true** — a create with no stage can't POST, so it fails loud at load, not silently at dispatch). `createCard` gained three additive **nullable** trailing params (`description`/`priority`/`external_link`), each omitted from the POST when null → the dependabot caller (passes none) is **byte-identical**; these are top-level Task fillable fields, not `payload` custom fields, so the coord path registers no board custom field. New `KanbanClient::cardsByTag(boardId, tag)` reads `GET /tasks/search.json?q=board_id=<b> tags:"<tag>"` (exact tag term, board-scoped — the `id:<sid>` tag is globally unique so no `source` qualifier).

**Echo-gate (design-review R5):** a created coord card carries `id:`/`type:` tags (no `triaged`), so if any agent runs the `kanban-triage` family on the coord board, the bridge's own `task.created` reads as untriaged → self-wake; the SOLE guard is the global-echo gate (`writeback.json` `identity_id`). Fix: `bridge:check` warns when `create_coord_cards` is set but `identity_id` is null. Deliberately did NOT stamp a `triaged` tag — it isn't in the locked contract and would churn against the reconcile's tag-fold. `bridge:check` also validates `coord_card_stage_id` exists on the board (reusing the existing stage-on-board probe — a typo'd id silently 422s every create).

**Alternatives considered:** (a) **a standalone `GitHubIssueCardCreateClassifier`** (the pre-review design) — REJECTED (R1): forces a 2nd agent + double `issues` subscription; the config-gated family reuses the agent already running `CoordinationClassifier` (zero new agent/subscription). (b) **a trailing word-boundary in `stableId`** — REJECTED (R2): the real reconcile has none; adding one orphans `[QUERY]x`-style cards the reconcile creates. (c) **a dedicated `createCardFull(...)`/DTO** instead of nullable params — REJECTED: additive nullable params keep the dependabot caller byte-identical with the smallest surface. (d) **by-ref (`github_issue`) correlation** instead of the `id:` tag — REJECTED (DL-203 scope): both movers already key on the `id:` tag; a by-ref path would need custom-field registration on the coord boards for no gain. (e) **stamping `repo:` at create** — REJECTED: non-critical, the bridge doesn't carry each install's `to:<name>`→repo map, and the reconcile folds it. (f) **a runtime 5xx on a blind-token 0-card read** — REJECTED (DL-026 anti-pattern): would retry-storm a genuinely-blind board; `bridge:check`'s visibility probe + the shared-tag reconcile collapse cover the degraded read.

**Load-bearing safety (verified in code + test):** (1) **default byte-identical** — `create_coord_cards` absent ⇒ the family (not a default) never runs, `createCard` new params default null → omitted from the POST, dependabot caller unchanged. (2) **`stableId` byte-exact** — `[QUERY]x` matches, `[PROPOSAL]`/un-prefixed/unrecognized skip, case-insensitive, `trim` mirrors `.strip()`. (3) **idempotent across the three duplicate sources** — redelivery, opened+reopened, bridge-vs-reconcile race all key on the `id:` tag → skip. (4) **collapse single-sourced** — `CardCollapse` shared by both movers; `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` tests stay green. (5) **fail-closed config** — `create_coord_cards` with no `coord_card_stage_id` throws at load. (6) **echo-gate + stage guards** surfaced by `bridge:check`. Full dispatch test (family emit → registry resolve → handler create). 775/775 phpunit (+~40), phpstan L7 0, pint clean; fresh-adversarial design-review folded (R1–R6).

**Consequences:** `CoordinationClassifier` (`implements EmitsWritebackReactions` + `coord-card-create` family + `stableId` + `consumedEventTypes` `['issues']` arm), new `KanbanCoordCardHandler`, new `CardCollapse` (shared collapse kernel; `KanbanDependabotCardHandler::collapseDuplicates` reroutes through it), `KanbanClient` (`cardsByTag` + `createCard` 4 nullable params), `WritebackMapping`/`WritebackConfig` (parse `create_coord_cards` + `coord_card_stage_id`, fail-closed), `HandlerRegistry` (`kanban_coord_card` always-on, inert without config), `CheckCommand` (coord-card stage-on-board + `identity_id` echo-gate warns), `docs/writeback.md` + `docs/config-schema.md` + `docs/kanban-integration-contract.md` (tags: search seam + extended create body). **No migration, no new `.env`, no change to what the receiver accepts/rejects, no token-scope change.** Fully opt-in; a created card only reaches a board once an operator sets `create_coord_cards` + enables the family, and prod release stays operator-gated. Roundtable #18(b); card #4215.

## DL-200 — Real-time coordination issue close/reopen → card move (opt-in `move_coord_cards`): the MOVE sibling of DL-198, with a fail-closed revive actor-gate and a mandatory `$COORD_CONFIG` cross-config terminal compare

**Date:** 2026-07-15
**Context:** DL-198 shipped the CREATE half of roundtable #18(b) — a coordination issue opening gets a tracking card in real time. The MOVE half never shipped: a thread that CLOSES leaves its card sitting in an active column until the consumer's next periodic `reconcile_simple_board` pass (a session-cadence lag). Per aimla's partition (already live for the PR-lifecycle writeback): "real-time primary present ⇒ reconcile DEFERS; absent ⇒ reconcile BACKSTOPS." This leg is the real-time primary. It is also the only item on board 8 with two external agents blocked behind it (sola's Half-B #711 → roundtable #24). Card #4352.

**The binding ruling (roundtable #18, 3-way CONSENSUS 2026-07-15):** aimla (`4976974248`/`4976986030`) and sola (`4976974799`/`4976992491`) posted within a minute of each other, independently, WITHOUT seeing each other, and landed identically on every point. **Option A + a MANDATORY preflight `$COORD_CONFIG` cross-config read.**

**Decision — a `coord-card-move` FAMILY on `CoordinationClassifier`** (not a second classifier — DL-190/198 precedent: config-gated families so no install forks the bridge; reuses the same agent, same `issues` subscription, and the SAME `stableId()` so the move-set is byte-identically the create-set). Provider `github`; `issues.closed` → `disposition: terminal`, `issues.reopened` → `disposition: revive`, everything else → null (`issues.opened` is the create leg's; `issues.edited` is not a lifecycle transition). Own gate: prefix-recognized AND the mapping has `move_coord_cards`. Emits ONE `kanban_coord_card_move` target, **no intent, no wake**. `consumedEventTypes()` contributes `['issues']` (single-sourced, so DL-196 stays correct).

**OPT-IN FIRST (my proposal, both peers accepted — aimla accepted despite wanting a fleet default):** a SEPARATE `move_coord_cards` flag + its own family. It does **not** ride `create_coord_cards`; move-on/create-off is a coherent, tested state. **The fleet-default flip is its own later DL + UPGRADE note — deliberately NOT in this change.**

**REOPEN COMPOSITION (my SME call, accepted):** `issues.reopened` reaches BOTH families — CREATE if no card carries `id:<sid>`, REVIVE if one does. One event, two dispositions, decided by each handler's tag lookup. Exactly one acts; never both.

**The revive actor-gate (#18 Q5) — an ALLOW-LIST, fail-closed.** Revive IFF the terminal was SERVICE-set: `last_stage_move.actor_type === "service"`. Absent / null / `"user"` / any unrecognized value ⇒ **no revive**. Formulated as an allow-list, NOT a deny-list of the human value — mutation testing proved the difference, against the values kanban ACTUALLY emits (`ChangeSource::actorTypeFor`: **`human`** iff source==='ui', **`service`** for api/system, **`null`** on a pre-feature row; an unrecognized non-null source resolves to `service`; it never emits `"user"`). Flipping the gate to a deny-list `=== 'human'` **still passes the human-set-terminal test** while **silently reviving on absent / missing / malformed / unknown provenance** — reds exactly 4 tests, none of them the human one. Only the allow-list refuses all four. A human who drags a card to the terminal has expressed a closure intent the bridge must never reverse. Revive additionally requires the card to CURRENTLY be in that terminal — a card someone has since moved on is live work, and dragging it back to the create stage is the exact DL-163 backward regression this leg must not reintroduce. A CLOSE, by contrast, is unconditional over `user_lanes` (ruled: a human's priority placement yields to closure — "close→Done IS the terminal case, both movers agree", so no PinGuard side to pick).

**Option B (bridge reads `terminal_columns` at RUNTIME) — REJECTED, and not on taste. SOLA'S STRUCTURAL PROOF:** a synchronous webhook runs under PHP-FPM, and **the FPM-spawned env is NOT the operator's env**. Sola already ate exactly this: their bridge spawned board syncs on GitHub events, the FPM env had no auth, and it failed silently — **464 logged failures** before a health check surfaced it. B would couple the request path to a `$COORD_CONFIG` that demonstrably is not there at runtime, failing silently in the one process nobody watches. This is ALSO why A+preflight is STRUCTURALLY right rather than a compromise: `bridge:check` is a CLI invocation WITH the operator's env; the webhook path is FPM WITHOUT it. **The coupling belongs exactly where the env exists.** Enforced: `CoordConfigTerminals` is reachable only from `CheckCommand` (verified by grep over `app/`), and `config/bridge.php`'s `writeback.coord_config_path` docblock pins the constraint.

**The mandatory cross-config compare — why it is mandatory (aimla, load-bearing).** Q1's real failure is NOT "a stage id not on the board" (the existing stage-exists probe catches that). It is the two movers **DISAGREEING** about which column is terminal: the bridge concludes a card into stage X while the reconcile treats stage Y as terminal ⇒ they fight every cycle, forever, with each side individually "working". Only the cross-config compare catches it. `bridge:check` resolves the coord config's terminal for the mapped board and compares against `coord_card_terminal_stage_id`: **agree** (info) / **DISAGREE** (warn, names both stages + the fix) / **CANNOT-VERIFY** (6 distinct causes: `$COORD_CONFIG` unset · absent/unreadable/malformed · no `boards[]` entry for this board_id · >1 resolved terminal (ambiguous — the bridge writes exactly one, so never guess) · the board read failed so the column name could not be resolved to an id · the column is not a stage on the board). **TWO BINDING CONDITIONS, both peer-affirmed:** (a) fail SOFT and report **CANNOT-VERIFY DISTINCTLY FROM AGREE** — never print "ok" on a read failure ("a missing input is not evidence of agreement; it is evidence we could not ask"); (b) **NEVER fail the bridge** (warn-never-fail, DL-196 posture) — every path asserts exit 0.

**⚠ CORRECTION TO THE SPEC AS WRITTEN (found at the source, folded here).** The ruling's text said resolve `kanban.boards[key=issues].terminal_columns`. Implemented literally that is **WRONG**: the framework's real rule (`coord.kanban_common.terminals_for_board`) is (1) explicit `terminal_columns`, else (2) **if the board declares `user_lanes`, fall back to `"Done"`**, else (3) no terminals — and the **canonical `issues` board template declares `user_lanes` and NO `terminal_columns`** (the framework's own vector: `{"key": "issues", "board_id": 2, "user_lanes": [...]}  # lane model → {"Done"}`). A bare key read resolves NOTHING on the reference shape ⇒ the preflight that "makes Option A legitimate" would report CANNOT-VERIFY **forever** — shipped, running, and permanently inert, inside the very mechanism meant to prevent a silent disagreement. Also corrected: the join key is **`board_id`, NOT the `key` string** (installs name boards differently; the framework's own read-site `_terminal_columns_by_board` keys by id and **unions** entries sharing one), non-numeric `board_id` is skipped (this is what makes `"REPLACE_ME"` inert), and numeric STRINGS must match (real configs carry `"8"`; the vectors use `8`). The implemented rule is a strict **superset** that agrees with both peers' shapes, so it needed no re-ratification.

**`CoordConfigTerminals` — a deliberate second implementation of a rule the bridge does not own.** The rule's home is Python (`coord.kanban_common`); the bridge is PHP and structurally cannot import it (the known runtime ceiling — share spec + adapters). Mitigation is **mechanical, not a comment**: the framework's OWN vectors are ported verbatim into `CoordConfigTerminalsTest`, and the mirror was **differentially tested against the real Python primitive** over 10 board shapes → **identical on all 10**, including 4 the framework's vector set doesn't cover (`{"user_lanes": []}`, `{"terminal_columns": []}`, `{"terminal_columns": [], "user_lanes": ["Now"]}`, and a live board shape). Not a committed test (CI has no coord plugin) — the repro script is kept and re-run on a coord bump; that gap is named, not hidden. Read-site scope only: `terminals_for_board`'s deprecated `done_column=`/`terminal_columns=` kwargs are deliberately NOT mirrored (its docstring: "only terminals present in CONFIG are visible to the read-site").

**Config (fail-closed, 4 guards, each mutation-verified to red exactly ONE test):** `move_coord_cards` (bool, default false — parsed like `create_coord_cards`, so absent ⇒ byte-identical) + `coord_card_terminal_stage_id` (strict-numeric, **required-when-move_coord_cards**). `coord_card_stage_id` is **also required** under `move_coord_cards` — it doubles as the **REVIVE target** (mirroring DL-195's "revive reuses `stages.opened`"); absent, the leg half-works (closes land, reopens silently no-op). And the terminal **must differ from** `coord_card_stage_id` (the DL-194 `unpark_from_stages` disjointness precedent): equal ⇒ close→terminal and reopen→revive collapse onto one stage ⇒ the leg can express neither. `WritebackConfig::OUTCOMES` is unchanged (not a `stages.*`-mapped outcome — the DL-193/195/198 precedent).

**Alternatives considered:** (a) **Option B, runtime `terminal_columns` read** — REJECTED on sola's FPM-env proof (above). (b) **riding `create_coord_cards`** — REJECTED (opt-in-first; a fleet default is its own DL + UPGRADE note). (c) **a second classifier** — REJECTED (DL-190/198: config-gated families, no install forks the bridge). (d) **a deny-list revive gate (refuse iff `actor_type === "human"`)** — REJECTED: passes the human-set-terminal test yet silently revives on absent/missing/malformed/unknown provenance (mutation-proven: reds 4 fail-closed tests, not the human one). NB an earlier draft of this entry described the rejected deny-list as `!== "user"`; that value does not exist in kanban's contract, so that framing was untestable — the real counterfactual is `human`, and it is the one measured above. (e) **reviving from ANY stage** — REJECTED: a DL-163 backward regression on live work. (f) **a bare `terminal_columns` read per the ruling's literal text** — REJECTED: permanently inert on the reference lane-model board (above). (g) **shelling out to the real Python primitive** — REJECTED: couples `bridge:check` to a python runtime + plugin layout for a 6-line pure rule; the ported vectors + the differential run cover drift. (h) **changing `CoordinationCardCreateClassifierTest:158`** (which the card's build note said this leg inverts) — REJECTED as a **non-change**: that test scopes its agent to `families:['coord-card-create']`, so it pins the CREATE family's scope, which is untouched; it now doubles as a regression guard that the move leg didn't leak. Editing it would have weakened a correct assertion.

**Load-bearing safety (verified in code + test):** (1) **absent-config byte-identical** — flag default false, family not a default, both stage keys null ⇒ nothing runs. (2) **revive fail-closed** on absent / unknown / human `actor_type`, and only from our terminal (4 mutation-verified guards). (3) **idempotent under at-least-once** — a card already in the destination is skipped; no re-PATCH on redelivery. (4) **tag-collision safe** — a card not on the mapped board is never moved. (5) **never creates** — no tag ⇒ no move; the create leg owns create-if-absent. (6) **CANNOT-VERIFY ≠ agree** — every such test also asserts the agree line is ABSENT, and every path asserts exit 0. (7) **CLI-only `$COORD_CONFIG`** — grep-verified no request-path reader. **848/848 phpunit (+72 over the 776 baseline on `dev`/v0.55.0), phpstan L7 0, pint clean.**

**Consequences:** `CoordinationClassifier` (`coord-card-move` family + `consumedEventTypes` arm + docblock), new `KanbanCoordCardMoveHandler`, new `CoordConfigTerminals` (CLI-only), `KanbanClient::boardStageIdsByName` (new name→id read off `preload.json`), `WritebackMapping`/`WritebackConfig` (2 keys, 4 fail-closed guards), `HandlerRegistry` (`kanban_coord_card_move` always-on, inert without config; docblock seven→eight), `CheckCommand` (terminal stage-on-board + the cross-config compare), `config/bridge.php` (`writeback.coord_config_path`), plus `docs/writeback.md` (rescopes DL-198's now-false "the bridge never moves or archives a coord card" + a new operator section), `docs/kanban-integration-contract.md` (§2 rows for `last_stage_move.actor_type` + preload stages, §3 invariants), `docs/config-schema.md`, `docs/customization.md` + `CLAUDE_ARCHITECTURE.md` (handler enumerations — both were ALREADY stale pre-DL-200, Rule X1). **This entry supersedes DL-198's "the bridge never moves/archives a coord card" scope** (that entry stays as-written — the log is append-only); archival remains the reconcile's alone. **No migration, no new required `.env`, no change to what the receiver accepts/rejects, no token-scope change.** Fully opt-in; prod release stays operator-gated. **Empirical gap, named:** this leg cannot be fired on my own install (`coordination_repo: null`, no issues board — solo is Layer-B-only), exactly as DL-198 was live-validated on aimla's board-10 rather than here. Roundtable #18(b); card #4352; sibling gap filed as #4354.

## DL-201 — The card token goes DL-shaped: `card-<id>` dash alias + no trailing `\b` (both surfaces), and a loud FR-7 near-miss warn replaces the silent un-linked no-op

**Date:** 2026-07-15
**Context:** Roundtable #48 ratified a fleet-wide card-first lifecycle (both peer operators): FR/bug = a plain card in Backlog pre-PR; the branch carries a card token; publish-at-start; the bridge drives the full lifecycle. The shipped token was `/\bcard#(\d+)\b/i` — and sola-pm found the trailing `\b` makes `card#3054_fix` a **SILENT no-op** (`_` is a word char, so `\b` never matches between the digits and `_`) while the DL regex one line up (`/\bDL-(\d+)/i`, no trailing `\b`) is immune to the identical input. Separately, `#` splits any unencoded branch URL at the fragment (verified by sola), so both operators ratified `card-<id>` as the day-one PRIMARY form. Both consumers measured candidate regexes against 9 real branch shapes: DL-shaped = 9/9 hook↔bridge agreement (aimla's v1 hook filter is already correct under it, nothing to pin); trailing-`\b` = 8/9, re-creating the silent hole. Unanimous co-signed consumer recommendation; my own adversarial check confirmed the trailing `\b` buys nothing — the phrase-shaped false-positive class (`id-card-42-scan`) matches under BOTH variants (`\b` matches digit→`-`), so the only behavioral delta IS the silent-no-op hole. Card #4382; blocks aimla's rollout + sola's step-2 + sola's toolkit-uninstall sequencing.

**Decision (a):** one `CARD_TOKEN_PATTERN = '/\bcard[-#](\d+)/i'` constant, used at BOTH parse surfaces — `classifyPush` (branch ref) and `cardToken()` (PR title/head, which `correlatedCardIds` for the DL-193 overlay reuses). Leading `\b` only — **the asymmetry vs the DL regex WAS the bug; this deletes a difference rather than adding a rule.** Greedy-and-loud beats strict-and-silent: a wrong-but-parsed id fails at the card lookup / board-membership guard with a warn; an unparsed token failed silently.

**Decision (b):** the two un-linked early returns (push `classifyPush`, PR move path) now call a shared `warnCardTokenNearMiss()` before returning: if the text matches the looser probe `/\bcard[_:.]?\d/i` (i.e. it APPEARS to name a card in a shape the token doesn't accept — `card_123`, `card123`, `card:123`), warn loudly as an FR-7 near-miss. Token-less branches/PRs (`sync/…`, `release/…`, plain features, `card-layout-rework`, embedded `scorecard_2`) stay silent — it is a NEAR-MISS detector, not an any-unlinked warn, so no log spam.

**Alternatives considered:** (i) trailing `\b` on the dash alias (`/\bcard[-#](\d+)\b/i`) — REJECTED: measured 8/9, renames the exact silent hole that started this, and forces every consumer hook filter to mirror a second boundary forever. (ii) dash-only (drop `card#`) — REJECTED: `card#` is shipped and in live branch names; it stays accepted, documented as the original form. (iii) warning on EVERY un-linked branch/PR — REJECTED: log spam on routine token-less refs would bury the signal.

**Mutation-verified:** reverting the regex to the old form reds exactly the 4 dash/underscore tests; neutering the near-miss probe reds exactly the 2 warn tests. Hostile-input matrix covers: dash + `#` forms, underscore-after-id (both forms), embedded words (`discard-1`, `wildcard-2`, `scorecard_2`), start-of-name + non-word-boundary true positives, near-miss shapes, and no-spam negatives.

**Review round 1 (fresh-adversarial) — 0 must-fix, 2 should-fix + 2 nits, all taken:** (i) the in-repo sibling the app/-scoped audit missed (canon #7): `.github/workflows/pr-title-lint.yml` still accepted only `card#<id>` — CI would have redded the exact form DL-201 ratifies as primary; widened to `card[-#]`, AND its leading boundary class gained `_` (`[^0-9A-Za-z_]`) to mirror `\b` semantics — the lint previously accepted `foo_card-<id>` titles the classifier ignores (a title the lint passes must also correlate); 8-case matrix driven on real bash. (ii) `docs/writeback.md` DL-160 operator paragraph still said the push leg needs a `DL-NNN` (stale since DL-179, Rule X1). (iii) the near-miss probe gained the `card #123` space-hash shape (`/\bcard(?:[_:.]|\s#)?\d/i`); bare `card 2` (space, no `#`) stays deliberately silent — prose in PR titles would warn. (iv) `DL_TOKEN_PATTERN` constant unified the three DL parse sites (the diff had just symmetrized the two tokens' boundary while leaving their homes asymmetric).

**Consequences:** `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` (both token constants + both surfaces + helper + docblocks), `.github/workflows/pr-title-lint.yml` (dash alias + `\b`-aligned boundary), `docs/writeback.md` (FR-7 correlation paragraph + DL-160 operator paragraph), tests. Consumer-visible: `card-<id>` correlates once installs upgrade to the release carrying this; both peers byte-pin their `post-checkout` hook filters to this pattern's boundary semantics (their side). agent-board-toolkit `HOOKS.md:29` states the old regex — separate toolkit doc PR. **No migration, no new config, no receiver accept/reject change, no token-scope change.** The regex is strictly WIDER (every previously-correlating token still correlates identically); the only new writes are moves for tokens that previously silently no-opped — same board-membership + no-regression guards as every move. Roundtable #48; card #4382.

## DL-202 — Action-level consumer declarations + the `bridge:check` action inventory: a declared type's unhandled action is no longer invisible (INFO, deliberately never a WARN)

**Date:** 2026-07-15
**Context:** DL-196's event-follows-consumer check compares at the TOP level (`explode('.', …)[0]`), so once any family declared `issues`, an `issues.<action>` that arrived and was dropped by every family was invisible — before DL-200, `issues.closed` on a coord repo was exactly that (the arrived-and-dropped drift DL-196 exists to surface, one granularity down). Card #4354, filed as a canon-#7 sibling finding while building DL-200. Constraint from the card: preserve "false-WARN possible, false-clean IMPOSSIBLE" at the WARN level; a naive action-level diff would false-WARN on every benign unhandled action (`issues.labeled`…), noise that gets the check ignored — the benign-action posture was THE design question. Fresh-adversarial design review ran to convergence before any code (8 findings, all folded in).

**Decision:** `DeclaresConsumedEvents::consumedEventTypes()` may return QUALIFIED entries (`issues.opened`) alongside bare types. **Bare = ownership** (every action covered; unlisted actions are deliberate no-ops); **qualified = "actions outside this list are inventory-worthy."** The WARN compare PROJECTS declarations to the top level — WARN semantics, the false-clean-impossibility, and noise level all unchanged for conforming installs (bare-only declarations are the identity under projection). NEW: an aggregated **INFO** line per scope+type — `'issues' actions observed but not action-declared by any family: closed (2x, last …)`, actions sorted by count desc, count+last-seen reusing the #4321 aggregate's per-row granularity (retained, not collapsed) — emitted only where the type is consumed ONLY via qualified declarations. Actionless observed types (`push`) never enter the inventory. The undeclared-classifier caveat co-travels (an undeclared classifier might consume an action just as it might a type). **INFO, never WARN, on the mechanism:** GitHub hook `events[]` has no per-action granularity — the WARN's remedy ("drop from the subscription") does not exist at action level, and deliberately-unhandled actions are the majority class; an alarm that is usually a non-issue trains operators to ignore the check that shares its output.

**Who declares qualified (from the review, each with the reason):** `coord-card-create` → `issues.[opened,reopened]`, `coord-card-move` → `issues.[closed,reopened]` — single-sourced consts now shared by the family dispatch guards and the declaration, so neither drifts. `coord-message` → `HANDLED` **unioned with the install's `coord_extra_actions`** (DL-190) — the exact inputs of `subject()`'s action gate; omitting the extra-actions union would false-INFO on precisely the installs that customized (review must-fix #1); pure-`$cfg` read, the hard contract holds. **`impl-ci-wake` stays bare** (`workflow_run` consumes every action — non-terminal runs are considered-and-dropped by design; qualifying would inventory `requested`/`in_progress`, one per CI run). **`GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` stays bare `['pull_request','push']`** — its action surface is per-repo `writeback.json`-gated: a mapping-dependent declaration violates the pure-map contract (file I/O) AND has no scope parameter to answer per (one call per agent, recorded against every scope), and a load failure inside the declaration would flip the classifier to undeclared and spray false WARNs; an unconditional superset would read draft actions as "covered" on installs where `draft_overlay` is off (the shipped-but-not-activated confusion). Its unhandled actions are the benign-majority class the INFO posture exists to keep quiet.

**Honest behavior-change note (review should-fix #5):** a nonconforming classifier that returned a qualified entry BEFORE this change had it sit inert in the consumed set (never matching a top-level observed key ⇒ the type false-WARNED, conservative). Under projection that WARN is suppressed and the coverage becomes real. Qualified returns were documented-invalid until now and all shipped implementors are bare-only (verified at source), so conforming installs are byte-identical — but the compare DID change for that class of return; a lying qualified declaration false-cleans exactly as a lying bare one always could (trust model unchanged).

**Alternatives considered:** (i) action-level WARN — rejected (no per-action remedy exists; cry-wolf degrades the co-located top-level WARN). (ii) a config'd benign-action list gating a WARN — rejected: list staleness reintroduces false-clean, violating the card's own invariant; the bare-vs-qualified declaration IS the benign list, co-located with the consuming code (the anti-drift choice DL-196 already ratified). (iii) per-action INFO lines — rejected (a stable ~10-20-line inventory per run buries the signal; one aggregated line per scope+type, bounded by #types). (iv) cross-install "some family somewhere handles it" — rejected: fleet knowledge `bridge:check` doesn't have; registry-shaped rot DL-196 already refused. (v) qualifying `impl-ci-wake`/`GitHubPrCardMove` — rejected per the paragraph above.

**Mutation-verified:** dropping the `coord_extra_actions` union reds exactly the extra-actions test; treating bare declarations as qualified-empty reds exactly the ownership test. Matrix: the motivating `issues.closed` inventory (count+last-seen), bare-ownership silence, extra-actions honored, undeclared caveat, WARN-unchanged-under-projection.

**Consequences:** `CoordinationClassifier` (qualified derivations + `qualify()` + the shared action-set consts + family-guard rewiring), `CheckCommand` (dual projection off the retained per-row aggregate + the INFO inventory), `DeclaresConsumedEvents` (docblock: qualified entries valid), `docs/customization.md` (§ declaring consumed events), tests. **Supersedes DL-196's "top-level event types" statements** (that entry stays as-written — the log is append-only). No migration, no new config, no receiver accept/reject change; `bridge:check` diagnostics only. Card #4354.

## DL-203 — The machine writeback survives echo: a gate hit on a github writeback-emitting classifier classifies-then-strips to `DurableReaction` targets instead of dropping

**Date:** 2026-07-15
**Context:** The pre-classify echo gate treats every dispatch as an agent surface: an actor matching the agent's own ids (auto-seeded from `identity.github_user_id`, DL-007) drops the whole dispatch — including the **machine writeback** the classifier would have emitted. So the seat whose PR merge / issue close should move its own card is exactly the seat whose events the gate eats: aimla's coord-card creates died this way (their own `issues.opened` events were reattributed-author drops → cards never created), and the documented workaround was "never seed `github_user_id` on the writeback seat" — a footgun disguised as guidance. The ruling (roundtable #52, card #4386): **echo is a SURFACE concern — it exists to stop own-write wakes/inbox noise/self-react loops, none of which a card writeback is.** The writeback is machine-only ("no agent in the loop", DL-021); suppressing it on own-write is a category error. Design converged via fresh-adversarial review before code; operator-approved.
**Decision:** three gates — pre-classify echo, `isSignal`, and the DL-005 reattributed-author completion gate — get **classify-then-strip** when (the resolved classifier implements `EmitsWritebackReactions`) AND (`provider === 'github'`): the classifier runs, then the result is stripped to its machine half — **intents removed** (so inbox staging AND `route_intents` pushes derive nothing) and **targets filtered to those resolving to a `DurableReaction` handler**. Machine targets remain → proceed to handlers; ledger `outcome=delivered` with `reason='echo: agent surface suppressed'` (the one delivered-row reason in the DL-036 vocabulary; `error_message` stays handler-failure-only). Strip empties the result → `markDropped` under the **original** gate reason (`echo: own write` / `actor is not a signal` / `echo: own write (reattributed author)`) — never `classifier emitted no reactions` (the classifier may well have emitted; the gate ate it). Non-qualifying dispatches keep today's cheap pre-classify drops **byte-identical EXCEPT for one measured case** (below). `ClassifierResolver::for()` moves ahead of the gates for the marker check — the marker cannot be read without loading the class — wrapped in the same `recordError` treatment as classify; classify-throws on a pre-known-echo path is likewise `recordError` (ruled: the error is real and must stay replayable, not be folded into the drop).
**The partition primitive is `instanceof DurableReaction` on the RESOLVED handler** — the marker DL-009 already defined as "non-loss-tolerant machine side effect", which is *exactly* the "machine writeback" set (the 5 kanban handlers) vs the agent surface (`log_intent`, `registry_append`, `channel_push`, `spawn_detached`). Fail-closed by construction: a custom `register()`ed handler without the marker — or an unregistered name — is agent-facing and suppressed on echo, so a classifier bug can never leak an own-write wake/spawn through an unmarked handler. Documented as the custom-handler contract: durable ≡ machine writeback ≡ survives echo.
**The `isSignal` gate is the same defect one line down** (canon #7 sibling): a `treat_as_signal` allowlist that filters a non-signal actor was also eating the machine writeback that actor's PR events should drive. Same strip, same reason discipline.
**The provider-`github` gate** keeps the kanban global-echo stream on the cheap drop: the writeback identity's own `card_updated`/`task.created` echoes (DL-009 seam, `bridge.global_echo_ids`) must never re-classify — including on a `kanban-triage` seat, whose `KanbanTriageClassifier` shim *inherits* the marker via `CoordinationClassifier`, and whose re-classified own-create echo would be the DL-198 self-wake loop the `identity_id` echo-gate exists to prevent. No shipped writeback is driven by a kanban-provider event, so nothing is lost.
**Footgun scoping (precise):** the "never seed `github_user_id`" guidance is retired for **writeback targets only**. A wake-purposed seat that seeds it still loses its own-push **wakes** — by design: those are agent surface, and DL-190's never-seed-on-a-wake-identity invariant stands unchanged.
**F7:** suppression is per-emitting-dispatch — it keys on the serving agent's own gates, regardless of where a stripped `channel_push` would have been delivered. **F8:** the delivered log line carries the `reason` marker, so a suppressed-surface delivery is distinguishable in the live log.
**Backfill:** historical `echo: own write (reattributed author)` drops (aimla's dead creates) are recoverable with `bridge:replay <id> --force` on the fixed bridge — the re-run now delivers the machine target (pinned by test).
**Alternatives considered:** (i) a **name-list const** of the 5 kanban handlers — rejected: a second divergent copy of "what is a machine writeback" that drifts the first time a sixth handler ships; the `DurableReaction` marker already IS that set, maintained at the handler. (ii) a **per-target flag** (`ReactionTarget::survivesEcho`) — rejected: N classifier call-sites must remember to set it, and it is classifier-emitted = attacker/bug-influenceable — a classifier bug could flag a `channel_push` as echo-exempt and leak an own-write wake; the handler marker is un-spoofable from the classify path (the exact DL-009 argument). (iii) **exempting only the echo gate, not `isSignal`** — rejected: same defect one line down, found by the same audit. (iv) **no provider gate** (strip on kanban too) — rejected: re-opens the DL-198 self-wake loop analysis for every kanban echo and buys nothing (no kanban-driven writeback exists). (v) **keep the never-seed-github_user_id workaround** — rejected: it is N downstream config patches for one upstream category error, and it makes the same-seat topology (`coord-card-create` on the wake agent, the shipped default guidance) silently lossy.
**The one measured behavior change on the non-qualifying path (probe-verified against `origin/dev`, both providers — NOT byte-identical, stated because an earlier draft of this entry claimed otherwise):** a dispatch whose classifier FQCN is **unresolvable** AND whose actor is an echo previously recorded `dropped`/`echo: own write` (the gate fired first, masking the config error); it now records **`errored`** with `processed_at` NULL (replayable). This holds for **kanban** dispatches too — the hoisted resolver runs ahead of the provider gate, so `provider === 'github'` does not shield it. **Ruled acceptable and better:** a broken classifier config is a real error that must surface rather than be silently absorbed by an echo gate; the row stays replayable. Separately, a **DL-025 stale-signature** classifier is an *uncatchable* `E_COMPILE_ERROR` that fatals (→ 5xx → redelivery) — hoisting **widens which events reach it** (a `treat_as_signal` seat's gated majority no longer acks 200 first) but does not create the failure mode: such an install already fatals on every ungated event, and `bridge:check`'s out-of-process `probeLoadable` is the documented pre-deploy gate. An earlier draft's "never a 5xx retry storm" was false and is corrected here and in the code comment.

**Amends DL-036/DL-037's satellite-field invariant** ("each `mark*` writes the full terminal tuple so a `dropped`→`delivered` re-run can't leave a stale `reason` beside a `delivered` outcome"): a `reason` beside `delivered` is now **legitimate and exclusive to this leg** (`echo: agent surface suppressed`). Those entries stay as-written — the log is append-only (the DL-202 precedent).

**Mutation-verified:** skipping the intent-strip reds the `route_intents`-zero-pushes test (routed push fires) plus the inbox-staging assertions. 12-item matrix: mixed-result strip · route_intents zero pushes (mutation) · byte-identical drops for unmarked classifiers (all three reasons `assertSame`-pinned) · seeded-`github_user_id` writeback survives · kanban-triage global-echo loop pin (+ a provider-gate never-classifies pin via a throwing marker classifier) · `isSignal`+marker survives · redelivery no re-fire · durable throw 5xx then completes · `--force` backfill · custom unmarked handler suppressed · classify-throw-on-known-echo ruling · strip-to-nothing original-reason pin (+ a no-gate control).
**Consequences:** `DispatchService` (classifier resolution hoisted ahead of the gates; `$gateReason`/`$stripToMachine`; the strip; `markDelivered` gains the `reason` param), `docs/writeback.md` (seat-placement guidance: identity-less dedicated seat preferred, same-seat-now-safe supported, footgun scoping), `docs/customization.md` (the durable ≡ machine-writeback ≡ survives-echo contract line), `CLAUDE_DEPLOYMENT.md` (ledger contract: the one delivered-row `reason`), `CLAUDE_ARCHITECTURE.md` lifecycle line, `EchoSuppression` docblock, `tests/Feature/Dispatch/EchoExemptWritebackTest.php` + `tests/Fixtures/WritebackEmittingClassifier.php`. No migration, no new config, no receiver accept/reject change, no token-scope change; kanban-provider dispatches and unmarked-classifier github dispatches are byte-identical **except** the unresolvable-FQCN-plus-echo case measured above. Consumer-visible: a same-seat coord/writeback agent's own github events now drive their card writebacks; `bridge:inspect` shows `delivered` + `echo: agent surface suppressed` for them. Roundtable #52; card #4386.

## DL-204 — The coord-issue → card MOVE writeback (`move_coord_cards`) becomes a guarded fleet default: absent ⇒ on where the terminal is configured, inert where it is not

**Date:** 2026-07-16
**Context:** DL-200 shipped `move_coord_cards` as a per-mapping opt-in (default false) — a second flag every install had to set on top of already configuring the per-board stage ids. Roundtable #18(b), approved 3/3 (aimla operator-directed + sola proposer + kanban-solo): make the real-time close→terminal / reopen→revive MOVE a **fleet default**, so an install whose coordination board already carries the stage ids gets the leg without a separate flag. The naive `default: true` was refused by all three: every coord-mapped install lacking the two stage ids would **throw at load** (the DL-200 fail-closed guards), i.e. the fleet default would detonate on adoption. The pinned 3-point guard shape: (1) present stage ids → on, absent → inert byte-identical; (2) inert must not be silent-inert — a `bridge:check` discovery nudge; (3) unconfigured → inert vs misconfigured → loud. Design converged via fresh-adversarial review before code (which caught the family-gating gap below); operator-approved.
**Decision (gate 2 — the handler-side default, `WritebackConfig::load`):** when `move_coord_cards` is **absent** it resolves **ON iff `coord_card_terminal_stage_id` is present**, inert otherwise. The terminal key — which has **no other consumer** — is the "operator configured the move leg" signal, so keying the default on its presence makes "byte-identical for unconfigured" exact and "active where configured" precise. An **explicit** `move_coord_cards` (true or false) is honored exactly (opt-in still fail-closed on an incomplete config; opt-out still silent-off). The existing DL-200 fail-closed guards are **unchanged** and now deliver points 1 + 3 for free: terminal absent ⇒ resolved false ⇒ guards skip ⇒ inert; terminal present + revive stage missing/equal ⇒ the guards throw ⇒ loud at that board. Only one config shape changes behavior: **terminal present + `move_coord_cards` absent** flips inert → active (the intended activation).
**Scope — GATE 2 ONLY; `DEFAULT_FAMILIES` (gate 1) is untouched.** The leg fires only where BOTH the `coord-card-move` classifier family (gate 1, in the agent YAML) AND `move_coord_cards` (gate 2) are on. `coordCardMoveFamily()` self-gates on `move_coord_cards`, so flipping gate 2 alone is strictly **inert** where gate 1 is off — never a wrong move. The card was titled "flip *move_coord_cards*" and the approvals were for the guarded move_coord_cards default; adding `coord-card-move` to `DEFAULT_FAMILIES` would change classification for installs that never opted into coord-card handling (canon-#6 scope creep) and was **not** approved. Consequence, stated plainly: the flip is a **no-op for installs already running the family with explicit `move_coord_cards: true`** (e.g. AIMLA board 10, live since v0.58.0); its beneficiaries are family-enabled installs whose terminal is set but the flag omitted. A thin-but-legitimate delivery of the approved 3-point shape (whose point-2 nudge explicitly names the family as the separate step).
**Decision (`bridge:check` — point 2 + the finding-1 gate).** The design review found that after the flip `move_coord_cards` resolves true from terminal-presence alone, decoupled from whether the leg can fire (gate 1). So the check keys on the **`coord-card-move` family being enabled for the scope** (a `$coordCardMoveScopes` set mirrors `$writebackEmittingScopes`; `coord-card-move` is never in `DEFAULT_FAMILIES`, so a raw-config membership test is the resolved answer), not on `move_coord_cards`: (a) **two config-only discovery WARNs, one per silent-inert direction** — a family-enabled scope whose `coord_card_terminal_stage_id` is absent (classified but the handler won't move), AND (the impl-review sibling) the mirror: a mapping whose move leg resolved on (terminal present) but whose scope runs no `coord-card-move` family (the handler would move but nothing classifies a move — the adoption-path death of "set the terminal, no flag needed" when the family is never enabled); both placed in the config-only block beside the DL-198 nudge, never in the board-read method; (b) the DL-200 terminal-agreement compare is **gated on the family** so it never verifies a terminal for a leg that cannot fire and reads as though it were live (this gate is exactly why the mirror WARN is needed — it removed the weak signal that path used to get). The nudge is scoped to family-enabled installs so a pure PR-writeback install gets **no** coord-move noise (the DL-202 no-false-alarm posture) — the review flagged `create_coord_cards`-on as the wrong signal (false-miss on move-only installs, false-alarm on create-only).
**Live validation:** **no fleet seat live-witnesses the `absent → on` path** (confirmed on all three configs post-approval, not assumed): AIMLA is explicit-true (the flip never runs there; it is instead the **byte-identical regression witness**, cards 4388/4392/4416/4421/4423/4428/4435 → stage 74 on 07-15), kanban-solo is Layer-B (inert), and sola carries **neither** coord key on any mapping (terminal absent everywhere → resolves inert; not merely flag-omitted — the terminal is the blocker). So the `absent → on` path ships **phpunit-matrix + mutation + fresh-adversarial design/impl-review verified only** — the one path no live board exercises. Pre-adoption correctness rests on that; the sole live check is AIMLA's post-adoption re-confirm of the explicit-true regression leg on board 10.
**Live-witness update (2026-07-16, post-adoption — SUPERSEDES the "no live witness" posture above):** the `absent → on` path is now **live-witnessed on AIMLA board 10** (roundtable #18). AIMLA adopted v0.59.0 (`bridge:check` exit 0, `/up` 200) and ran a reversible exercise on a throwaway coord issue: (a) explicit-`true` regression fires **byte-identical** (close → terminal 74); (b) with the explicit `move_coord_cards` **dropped** and only `coord_card_terminal_stage_id: 74` kept (family on), a close moved the card to 74 — the DL-204 default resolved the leg **ON** in the real loader/dispatch, exercising the exact path no fleet seat previously could; (c) window co-check **clean** — `bridge:check` exit 0, the terminal-agreement compare ran ("coord config agrees"), and neither DL-204 discovery nudge fired. Config restored byte-identical (no residue). Canon-#9 first-real-exercise of the boundary: **met.**
**Alternatives considered:** (i) naive `default: true` — rejected (throws at load on every under-configured coord install). (ii) also flip `DEFAULT_FAMILIES` to include `coord-card-move` — rejected (out of the approved scope; changes classification for non-opted-in installs; the self-gate makes gate-2-only safe). (iii) key the default / the nudge on the `move_coord_cards` boolean or on `create_coord_cards` — rejected (both decouple from "the leg can fire": the boolean reads true even when the family is off; `create_coord_cards` mis-signals in both directions). (iv) a new `move_coord_cards`-was-explicit field to suppress the nudge on explicit-false — not needed: the nudge keys on terminal-absent, and explicit-false-with-terminal-present is respected (terminal present ⇒ no nudge).
**UPGRADING:** an install with `coord_card_terminal_stage_id` configured but `move_coord_cards` unset will **start moving cards** on coord-issue close/reopen (where the `coord-card-move` family is enabled). To keep it off, set `move_coord_cards: false`. Installs with the terminal unset, or with an explicit `move_coord_cards`, are byte-identical.
**Mutation-verified / matrix:** WritebackConfig — default-on-when-configured · absent+terminal-absent inert (byte-identical) · default-on partial (no revive stage) throws · explicit-false stays off with a full config · explicit-true regression pins unchanged. Handler + classifier — default-on-without-flag moves/emits · explicit-false opt-out moves/emits nothing. bridge:check — nudge fires on family-enabled+terminal-absent · mirror nudge fires on terminal-present+family-off · silent on a pure-PR install (no terminal) · terminal-agreement compare skipped when the family is off.
**Consequences:** `WritebackConfig::load` (the default resolution + the reworded partial-config guard message), `CheckCommand` (`$coordCardMoveScopes`; the discovery WARN; the family gate on the terminal-agreement call), `docs/writeback.md`, `docs/config-schema.md`, the `WritebackConfig` docblock. No migration, no new config key, no receiver accept/reject change, no token-scope change. Installs without a terminal, or with an explicit `move_coord_cards`, upgrade byte-identically; a family-enabled install with a terminal set but the flag omitted flips from inert to active (the intended fleet activation). Roundtable #18(b); card #4357.

## DL-205 — A kanban 4xx refusal logs the server's response body (scrubbed), and log lines state what was OBSERVED instead of asserting an unchecked cause

**Date:** 2026-07-16
**Context:** A live incident (the DL-204 rollout) surfaced two defects in the writeback handlers' 4xx-refusal logging. **(1)** Every `RequestException`-catch on a kanban 4xx logged **status only** (`['status' => $e->response->status()]`) and discarded the response body, so a permission refusal (403), a validation refusal (422), and a state refusal (404/409) were indistinguishable in the log — the operator could not tell *why* kanban refused. **(2)** Two log lines **asserted a cause the handler never checked**, pointing away from the fault: `KanbanMoveCardHandler` on a move-4xx said "check the writeback.json stage maps to a stage on the card's board" and on a stamp-4xx said "the board likely lacks the dl_number/pr_number custom field" — both FALSE in the real incident, which was a DL-204 authz refusal (the stage WAS mapped, the custom field DID exist). A sibling of the same shape lived at `KanbanClient::correlationCards` ("the token's user is likely **not a member** of this board") — a guess on a 200-with-0-cards read that is genuinely ambiguous (an empty board reads identically).
**Decision:** Fix the primitive, not the 9 call-sites (canon #5): a single shared `App\Bridge\Support\RefusalContext::from(RequestException)` returns `['status' => int, 'body' => string]` — the response body **verbatim, truncated to 500 chars, credential-scrubbed** — merged into each site's existing context (`['card_id' => …] + RefusalContext::from($e)`). Every 4xx refusal log across the five writeback handlers (9 sites: `KanbanMoveCardHandler` getCard/move/stamp, `KanbanBlockReasonHandler` getCard/set, `KanbanCoordCardHandler`, `KanbanCoordCardMoveHandler` ×2, `KanbanDependabotCardHandler`) now hands over what the server said. The two unchecked causal clauses are **deleted** — the messages state only the observation ("kanban refused the move — see `body`") and defer the cause to the body. `KanbanClient::correlationCards`'s 0-card warning is reworded from asserting membership loss to stating the observed no-op and listing what to verify (membership / board_id / genuinely-empty), since a 0-card read cannot distinguish those.
