**Scrub mechanism (`RefusalContext::scrub`):** three passes, run on the **full body before truncation** (so a credential split across the 500-char boundary can't leak its head): (a) JSON string values of any key *containing* a sensitive word (`token`, `secret`, `password`, `authorization`, `api_key`, `access_token`, …) → `"[REDACTED]"`; (b) query/form `key=value` pairs for those keys; (c) HTTP auth schemes `Bearer`/`Basic`/`token` **followed by a credential-LONG value (`{16,}` of the token charset)** → `[REDACTED]`. The length gate on (c) is load-bearing: a bare-`token` scheme match with no length floor redacted the prose word after "token" ("token cannot write …" → "token [REDACTED] write …"), mangling the very reason the body exists to surface — real tokens are long, English words after the keyword are short, so `{16,}` separates them cleanly (keyed credentials of any length stay covered by (a)/(b)). Over-redaction is the safe failure mode; a leaked token is the one designed against.
**Scope:** logging only — no change to what is accepted/rejected, to the transient(5xx→retry)/permanent(4xx→log+no-op) split, or to any control flow. The `bridge:check`/`bridge:reconcile` CLI catch-sites are deliberately **out of scope**: they are operator-interactive, already interpret the status into remediation hints, and do not silently discard into a log — a different class from the swallowed-4xx handler sites.
**Alternatives considered:** (i) add `body` inline at each of the 9 sites — rejected (9 divergent copies of the truncate+scrub logic; canon #5). (ii) log the body unscrubbed — rejected (a kanban error body can echo the request, which may carry the writeback token). (iii) delete the `KanbanClient` 0-card warning entirely — rejected (the observation is genuinely useful; only the asserted cause was wrong, so it is reworded, not removed). (iv) no length gate on the auth-scheme scrub — rejected (mangles prose; surfaced by a test).
**Tests (RED-when-reverted):** `RefusalContextTest` (status+body carried, truncation, per-vector scrub matrix, benign body untouched, split-across-boundary still redacted); `KanbanMoveCardHandlerTest` (move-4xx and stamp-4xx assert the body is in the context AND the deleted guessed strings are absent; a token echoed in a 403 body is scrubbed); `KanbanClientTest` (the 0-card warning no longer says "likely not a member" and states the observation).
**Consequences:** new `app/Bridge/Support/RefusalContext.php`; the 9 handler log sites + `KanbanClient::correlationCards` (message + docblock); `docs/writeback.md` (the diagnose note that a logged refusal now carries kanban's response body). No migration, no new config, no receiver accept/reject change, no token-scope change. 903/903 phpunit, phpstan L7 0, pint clean. Card #4409.

## DL-206 — Bridge-created dependabot cards can carry an opt-in `id:` provenance tag (per-mapping `card_id_tag_template`) so tag-keyed promoters can find them

**Date:** 2026-07-16
**Context:** `KanbanDependabotCardHandler` creates dependabot cards tagged `['dependencies','triaged']` with `payload[pr_number,pr_url,origin]` — but **no `id:` provenance tag**. The bridge correlates its own cards **by-ref** (`pr_number`/`pr_url` → `by-ref.json`); the `id:{PREFIX}-pr-{N}` tag is an **impl-side** convention stamped on **impl-created** cards, which the fleet's tag-keyed Shipped→Released promoters read. Dependabot is the one PR-provenance card the **bridge itself** mints, so it lacked the `id:` tag its impl-created siblings carry — invisible to any tag-keyed promoter (sola's `reconcile-released-to-main.py` reads the `id:` tag only; **27 dependabot cards stranded** in Shipped-to-dev on sola board 3). Roundtable #75, converged 3-way (sola-pm + aimla-pm + kanban-solo). aimla verified their own promoters are **payload-keyed** (0 stranded on board 9) — proving `payload` is a usable correlation key and `id:` is the *canonical* one, i.e. stamping the tag is **strictly additive**, not a migration.
**Decision:** an opt-in per-mapping **`card_id_tag_template`** (free-form non-empty string). When set, the handler renders it into an `id:` tag **prepended** to the create tags; **unset ⇒ no tag (inert, byte-identical)**. Placeholders: `{n}`/`{pr_number}` = the PR number, `{repo}` = the repo NAME (`basename(owner/repo)`). Per-tenant grammar — sola `id:DEV-pr-{n}` (matches its reconcile's `id:(DEV|BE|INV)-pr-(\d+)`), AIMLA `id:dep:{repo}#{n}`. Parsed exactly like `draft_block_reason` (present-must-be-non-empty-string, else `ConfigException` at load — fail-closed). This **restores parity** between bridge-created and impl-created PR-provenance cards (canon #5 — extend the existing key, don't sibling it), not a new convention: the card stays idempotent on `payload.pr_number` for its create/move lifecycle AND correlatable by the `id:` tag for external promoters — no read-side union of two formats anywhere.
**Why the write-site, not a read-side fallback:** teaching each promoter to read `payload` would be N payload-aware readers of two formats for one thing — the canon-#5 anti-pattern. One write-site guarantees the canonical key.
**AIMLA namespace constraint (roundtable #75, aimla traced to source):** aimla's `kanban-board9-dev-sync.py` owns the `id:pr:` namespace and its `owns_id` keys on the **sid string only** (can't see payload/tags). It has **no "archive owned-absent-from-source" pass**, so a bridge-stamped card is never archived — the *only* constraint is that AIMLA's template resolve to a namespace **disjoint from `id:pr:`** (hence `id:dep:{repo}#{n}`), which their existing `sid.startswith("pr:")` then excludes with **zero aimla code change**. The free-form template delivers exactly that lever.
**Relationship to #4483 (promote-on-release leg):** #4483 keys on the **bridge-native `payload.pr_number`/`pr_url`** correlation (which every card carries, dependabot included), so it covers dependabot cards **regardless** of this tag — this template serves the **external** `id:`-keyed readers (sola's reconcile), not the bridge's own leg.
**Scope:** the dependabot **create** path only. Unknown template placeholders are left **literal** (the tenant verifies its template against its own `id:`-keyed reader at activation, not here). No cross-field guard — a template set with `create_dependabot_cards: false` is inert (no cards created ⇒ nothing stamped), not an error. No change to the create/move/archive lifecycle, the correlation, the transient/permanent split, or the token scope.
**Alternatives considered:** (i) teach every promoter to read `payload` — rejected (N readers, two formats; canon #5). (ii) a hardcoded `card_id_prefix` scalar — rejected (AIMLA's `id:dep:{repo}#{n}` is not a prefix apart from sola's `id:{PREFIX}-pr-{n}`; the grammars differ, so a per-tenant **format template** is required). (iii) key #4483 on the `id:` tag — rejected (would inherit the tagless blind spot; #4483 keys on bridge-native `payload.pr_number` instead).
**Tests (RED-when-reverted):** `WritebackConfigTest` (loads the template / absent ⇒ null / empty-string throws / non-string throws); `KanbanDependabotCardHandlerTest` (stamps the rendered tag, `{repo}` → `basename`, absent template ⇒ tags are **exactly** `['dependencies','triaged']`). Mutation-verified: reverting the conditional stamp reds the two stamp tests, the back-compat test stays green.
**Consequences:** new nullable `WritebackMapping::$cardIdTagTemplate`; `WritebackConfig::load` parse + docblock; `KanbanDependabotCardHandler::renderIdTag` + conditional tag; `docs/writeback.md` + `docs/config-schema.md`. No migration, no receiver accept/reject change, no token-scope change; **inert unless configured**. Per-tenant **activation** (set the template + redeploy) and the one-time **backfill** of existing tagless cards are separate, operator/user-gated steps (not autonomous). 913/913 phpunit, phpstan L7 0, pint clean. Card #4485.

## DL-207 — An opt-in `promote_on_release` writeback leg promotes Shipped cards to Released on a release merge, keyed on POSITIVE reachability of the card's merge sha from `main`

**Date:** 2026-07-16
**Context:** A card-first board with a **Shipped-to-dev / Released-to-main** column split has **no steady-state promotion**. A feature PR merges to `dev` (`base=dev` ⇒ outcome `merged` ⇒ card → Shipped); its commits reach `main` only later, folded into a **release PR** (`release/vX → main`). That release merge fires exactly ONE `merged_to_main` event — for the release PR's *own* card — so the constituent feature cards stay at **Shipped** until a manual `bridge:reconcile`. And `bridge:reconcile` deliberately **defers** the Shipped→Released transition to "the promote workflow" (`ReconcileCommand` excludes `merged_to_main` from move-in, ~:319-328, and treats a card already at the released stage as terminal). So nothing promotes in steady state. Roundtable #73, converged with sola-pm (sola supplies `reconcile-released-to-main.py` as the reference — `get_dev_only_shas` + tag→merge_sha). **This leg IS that promote workflow, event-driven.**
**Decision:** an opt-in per-mapping **`promote_on_release`** (bool, default false). On the `merged_to_main` event, `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifier` emits — via a single choke-point wrapper (`classify()` appends the target once rather than threading it into each move/overlay return) — one `kanban_promote_released` target, INDEPENDENT of whether the release PR itself carries a card token. The new **`KanbanPromoteReleasedHandler`** (`DurableReaction`, always-on in `HandlerRegistry`) scans the mapped board for cards **at the Shipped stage** (`stages.merged`) that are tooling-managed (a PR reference), not pinned, and — on a shared board — attributable to this repo, and promotes each whose merged PR's commit is now on `main` to the Released stage (`stages.merged_to_main`). Reuses the existing stage keys; `promote_on_release` fails **closed at load** when `stages.merged`/`stages.merged_to_main` is unmapped.
**The promotion predicate is POSITIVE reachability, not a dev-only proxy:** promote iff `GitHubReadClient::compareStatus(merge_commit_sha, RELEASE_BASE='main') ∈ {ahead, identical}` — main is ahead-of/equal-to the merge sha ⇒ the sha is an ancestor of main ⇒ the card's work is ON main ⇒ released — **gated on `getPull(...).merged === true`** (an OPEN PR carries a non-null *test-merge* `merge_commit_sha` on no branch; the emptiness guard would never catch it). The first-round design used sola's negative `merge_sha ∉ compare(main...dev)` proxy; adversarial design review found `∉ dev-only-set` is ALSO true for shas on **neither** branch (open-PR test-merge shas, PRs merged to a third base, cross-repo shas) → false promotions into the **terminal** Released stage. The positive test rejects all three populations, needs **no `integration_branch` config**, and has **no 250-commit compare-truncation risk** (only `status` is read). It is self-healing: a card stranded by a prior failed release promotes on the *next* release event (its sha is on main via the earlier merge-commit).
**Merge-strategy precondition (documented, unguardable):** correctness rests on the release→`main` merge preserving `dev`'s commit shas — a **merge-commit or fast-forward** (verified this fleet's method: `Merge pull request #N from …/release/vX`; dev PRs squash-merge, so a squash-sha on dev becomes reachable from main via the release merge-commit). A **squash/rebase RELEASE merge** rewrites shas, so no feature sha ever joins main and the leg promotes nothing; `bridge:check` cannot detect merge strategy, so this is a doc precondition, not a guard.
**First runtime GitHub-read dependency:** this is the FIRST path to call GitHub in the **FPM runtime** (today only the reconcile CLI reads GitHub). Under FPM `GH_TOKEN` is absent (DL-184) and the `git-credential-coord` store helper is CLI-only, so in practice a **placed `<secret_dir>/github/token`** (or `providers.github.token_path`) is required. Unresolved token ⇒ durable `WritebackAlertNotifier` alert + loud log + **no-op** (a permanent config gap; a 5xx would retry-storm an unfixable event). `bridge:check` warns when `promote_on_release` is on but no token resolves **from a file** (the store/GH_TOKEN leg that satisfies reconcile does NOT hold under FPM), and when `stages.merged === stages.merged_to_main` (the promote is a no-op). A tighter runtime GitHub timeout (8s vs reconcile's 15s) and a `MAX_CANDIDATES` cap bound the synchronous webhook; overflow is alerted and drains across successive release events (a promoted card leaves the Shipped filter). **No reconcile backstop for this transition**, so every gap is made LOUD (alert + `bridge:check`), and recovery is fix-the-gap → the next release re-scans.
**Not gated on #4391:** #4391 is the CI PROMOTE SECRET (a `release-promote` Action token that 403s on `task.move`). This leg runs in the bridge RUNTIME and moves via the runtime **writeback** token (`WritebackClientFactory`) — the SAME `KanbanClient`+token the existing `merged_to_main` release-PR-card move already uses successfully — so `task.move` demonstrably works here; the leg is decoupled from #4391. (Corrects an earlier token-conflation claim on roundtable #73.)
**Shared code (canon #5):** the card→(repo, PR) precedence (pr_url → bare-pr_number-on-1:1-board → dl-only-skip, with the shared-board bare-pr_number ambiguity rule) is extracted into a pure `TrackedCardRef`/`TrackedRefKind` helper adopted by BOTH `ReconcileCommand::resolveTracked` and this handler, so the two can't derive a card's PR differently. `ReconcileCommand`'s inline precedence + dead `parsePrUrl` are replaced by the shared helper (behavior byte-identical — `ReconcileCommandTest` green).
**Scope / boundary:** DL-only cards (no PR reference) are not promotable — the SAME PR-driven boundary the reconcile draws ("DL→PR resolution out of v1 scope"). First-adoption of a large existing Shipped backlog is bounded by the cap (steady-state N is a handful) — a `bridge:promote` CLI backfill is a filed fast-follow, not this PR. `merged_to_main` fires for any merge to main (release, hotfix, dependabot-to-main); the scan is idempotent and semantically correct on all (anything landing work on main releases it), so over-firing is safe.
**Alternatives considered:** (i) sola's negative dev-only-set proxy — rejected (admits neither-branch shas → false terminal promotions; design review). (ii) a separate promote classifier — rejected (`ClassifierResolver` runs exactly ONE classifier per agent, so a sibling would displace the move classifier; embed as an opt-in leg like overlay/dependabot/revive). (iii) scatter-merging the promote target into each classifier return — rejected (canon #7 N-edit sibling-hole shape; a dependabot-to-main return already drops it — single choke point instead). (iv) an `integration_branch` config for the compare — dropped (the positive against-main test needs only `RELEASE_BASE`).
**Tests (RED-when-reverted):** `GitHubReadClientTest` (getPull carries `merge_commit_sha`; `compareStatus`); `WritebackConfigTest` (`promote_on_release` default false / fail-closed on missing shipped/released stage); `TrackedCardRefTest` (the shared precedence); `GitHubPrCardMoveClassifierTest` (promote target on a bare release PR / alongside a DL move / on the dependabot-to-main edge; none on merge-to-dev or flag-off); `KanbanPromoteReleasedHandlerTest` (promotes only Shipped cards whose merge is on main; skips diverged/open-PR/no-pr/pinned/not-shipped; no-token no-op; transient 5xx propagates, permanent 4xx skips the card); `HandlerRegistryTest` (registered as a `DurableReaction` — the DL-203 strip-survival invariant); `BridgeCommandsTest` (the two `bridge:check` warns + the quiet case).
**Consequences:** new `KanbanPromoteReleasedHandler`; new `TrackedCardRef`/`TrackedRefKind`; `GitHubReadClient` widened (`merge_commit_sha`, `compareStatus`, injectable timeout); `WritebackMapping::$promoteOnRelease` + `WritebackConfig::load` parse/fail-closed; classifier wrapper; `HandlerRegistry` registration; `CheckCommand` two warns; `ReconcileCommand` uses the shared helper; `docs/writeback.md` + `docs/config-schema.md` + `docs/kanban-integration-contract.md`. No migration, no receiver accept/reject change, no token-scope change; **inert unless configured**. Per-tenant **activation** (set `promote_on_release` + place a runtime GitHub token file + redeploy) is a separate operator/user-gated step. 949/949 phpunit, phpstan L7 0, pint clean; two fresh-adversarial design-review rounds (predicate corrected round 1→2) + an impl-review pass. Card #4483.

## DL-208 — `EventDrivenClassifier` inherits the DL-191 `route_intents` wake-guard: the guarded `wakePush()` lifts to the shared `InboxOnlyClassifier` base, closing the last double-wake copy

**Date:** 2026-07-17
**Context:** DL-191 gave `CoordinationClassifier` a guarded `wakePush()` that suppresses a family's hand-emitted `channel_push` on a `route_intents:true` channel (the dispatcher already routes every staged intent → a hand-emit is a second push). `EventDrivenClassifier` — the *other* shipped hand-emitting classifier, a sibling subclass of `InboxOnlyClassifier` — was **never** given that guard: its `classify()` appended a `channel_push` per intent **unconditionally**. Coalescing does not save it: the classifier's target defaults `debounceKey → targetId` (`channel_push|<subject>`) while the dispatcher's routed push namespaces it (`channel_push|channel_push:<subject>`), so the two survive under distinct keys and the handler fires **twice** with identical payload. Any agent on `EventDrivenClassifier` + `channel.route_intents:true` double-woke every event — the exact hazard DL-191 fixed for the coord families, guarded here only by a code comment ("pair route_intents with a plain inbox classifier, not EventDriven"). The N=2 copies (this + the coord families) are the sibling-duplication canon #5/#7 flag: one behavior, two byte-identical emitters, and the guard reached only one.
**Decision:** lift the guarded emitter to the **common base** `InboxOnlyClassifier::wakePush()` (`protected`; byte-identical to DL-191's private coord copy — the canonical guarded semantics). Both wake-emitting subclasses now share it: `EventDrivenClassifier::classify()` becomes a flat-map of intents through `$this->wakePush($intent, $ctx)`; `CoordinationClassifier` deletes its private copy and inherits (its `KanbanTriageClassifier` subclass inherits transitively). The base's *own* `classify()` still emits no reactions — `wakePush()` is shared subclass machinery, not a base reaction. (No trait: the codebase has no traits and the two emitters already share the `InboxOnlyClassifier` ancestor, so the base is the single natural home.)
**Behavior:** `route_intents:false` is **byte-identical** for both classifiers (the emitted `ReactionTarget` is unchanged — same handler/targetId/debounceSeconds:0/payload). `route_intents:true` changes only `EventDrivenClassifier`: **one wake, was two**. This reverses the documented "don't pair EventDriven with route_intents" footgun — pairing is now safe, matching `CoordinationClassifier`. Only a **raw custom classifier** that emits `channel_push` without routing through `wakePush()` still double-pushes (docs updated to steer custom authors to the guarded helper).
**Tests (RED-when-reverted):** `EventDrivenClassifierTest::test_suppresses_hand_emit_on_route_intents_true` (zero targets on a `route_intents:true` channel; intent still staged) + `test_multiple_intents_each_hand_emit_on_route_intents_false` (behavior-preserving one-push baseline); the existing `CoordinationClassifier`/`KanbanTriage` `route_intents` suppression tests stay green against the inherited method.
**Consequences:** `InboxOnlyClassifier` gains `protected wakePush()`; `EventDrivenClassifier` flat-maps through it (drops its direct `ReactionTarget` construction/import); `CoordinationClassifier` deletes its private `wakePush()`. Doc-sync (Rule X1 — the reversed footgun): `DispatchService` route_intents comment, `docs/multi-agent.md`, `docs/config-schema.md`, `docs/multi-host.md`, and the `docs/customization.md` subclass example (now shows the guarded `wakePush()`). Historical records left as-is (the 2026-05-31 architecture review, DL-006/190/191, past CHANGELOG rows). No migration, no new config, no receiver accept/reject change, no token-scope change. 945/945 phpunit, phpstan L7 0, pint clean. Card #4494.
